# James Buchanan Barnes — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

**Subject:** BARNES, James Buchanan. DOB c. March 1925, Shelbyville, Indiana (per recruitment records, Camp Lehigh, 1936). Chronological age >100; biological age held at approximately 30 by intermittent cryostasis 1945–c.1990s. Designations of record: "Bucky" (familial/Rogers-era), "Зимний Солдат" / Winter Soldier (Department X, 1954–c.1991, intermittent), "Captain America" (acting, 2008–2011), "White Wolf" (Wakandan rehabilitative, post-2018). Current operational status: independent black-ops principal, loosely affiliated Avengers/Thunderbolts/Wakandan intelligence; no fixed residence of record; small named in-group.

---

## 1. Bottom Line Up Front

The subject is a **competent, conscience-driven, structurally penitential operator** whose entire adult life — across two centuries and at least four imposed identities — has been organized around a single load-bearing proposition: *the body that did those things is still walking, and therefore owes.* He is not dangerous to civilians, allies, or institutions acting in good faith. He is not unstable in the colloquial sense. He is, in fact, the most predictable lethal asset in the published record — because his predictability is moral, not procedural. Given a clear target who deserves it and a population he is shielding, his behavior is forecastable to within a small margin. Given celebration, retirement, gratitude, or any sustained invitation to inhabit a normal life, his behavior becomes evasive, withdrawing, and self-sabotaging in mission-channeled forms (volunteering for non-return assignments; geographic disappearance; refusal of leadership offered without coercion).

He is, in short, **a survivor who has not yet permitted himself the verb.**

## 2. The Through-Line — One Sentence, Then Unpacked

Across 1925 to present: *an orphaned boy attached early and totally to one man, was made into a weapon, used that weapon against the innocent for half a century without consent, was returned to himself, and has spent every subsequent waking hour paying installments on a debt he believes can never be cleared but must never be defaulted on.*

Unpack the clauses, because each is load-bearing:

- **"Orphaned boy attached early and totally to one man"** — the Rogers bond is not friendship in the ordinary sense; it is the secure base a parentified Camp Lehigh child built when his father was killed in the howitzer accident and the institution became his parent. Rogers is, structurally, the first object Barnes chose rather than was assigned. That distinction governs everything downstream. The bond is monotropic, lifelong, and operates as a superego proxy — he does not ask *what is right;* he asks *what would Steve do,* and this remains true when Steve is dead, missing, or disagreeing.

- **"Was made into a weapon"** — the conditioning was industrial, multi-decade, and specifically designed to break and rebuild the attachment system: cryostasis between deployments (so no relationship could form across time), ECT-analog memory suppression (so no relationship could survive even within a deployment), Russian phrase-string triggers (so the handler owned the on-switch), and the deliberate, observed pattern of *permitting* attachment (the Romanova relationship in the Red Room era) *and then amputating it* to teach the substrate that closeness is the prelude to loss. Attachment, in his nervous system, was conditioned into the punishment. This is the somatic seed of every relational pattern he now exhibits.

- **"Used that weapon against the innocent for half a century without consent"** — the canonical kill list spans three continents, multiple decades, named targets and incidental civilians, including the Stark assassination of December 16, 1991 and analogous operations across the Cold War. The lack of free agency does not, per the moral-injury literature (Griffin et al., 2019), spare him the injury; it intensifies it, because there is no clean narrative of perpetration or victimhood available — he is irreducibly both.

- **"Was returned to himself"** — Cosmic Cube restoration (2006), Wakandan deprogramming (post-2018, depending on continuity), partial integration across the 2010s. The first thing he did when given the Cube and his memory back was *leave.* He chose supervised solitude over reunion with Rogers. This is the diagnostic moment: when freedom was finally on offer, he selected containment.

- **"Paying installments on a debt he believes can never be cleared but must never be defaulted on"** — Captain America mantle (only when guilt-leveraged into accepting it); Siberian extradition and gulag (submitted to with disturbing equanimity, told Rogers not to come); Man on the Wall (a job whose function is being the one who carries unforgivable acts so others don't have to — *he volunteered*); Thunderbolts (the team designed for ambiguous wet-work); recurrent volunteering for high-lethality assignments no one else will take. He is not seeking death — that would be a default. He is seeking the longest possible deployment in service of the ledger.

The through-line is **the loop**: trauma → erasure → restoration → self-imposed penance → re-traumatization → return to penance. The loop is not a failure of recovery. The loop is the recovery — the only structure his nervous system has yet found that lets him remain in the world without either dissociating from what was done or collapsing under it.

## 3. The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

**Core wound.** Not the 1945 fall. Not the arm. Not even the kills. The core wound is the **revocation of consent at the foundation of selfhood** — the discovery that for fifty years his body acted, formed bonds, killed, slept, and woke without him, and that the line between his agency and his programming is not retrievable to himself with certainty. The 1945 dismemberment is a literal sign of the structural one: half of him was replaced by his torturers, and he can no longer locate where the original ends and the installation begins. This is the somatic autobiography he sees every time he looks at his left side, and why the shift from Soviet arm to Wakandan vibranium prosthesis is not a quality-of-life upgrade — it is a partial repatriation of the body. (Even so: it is still a prosthesis. The arm he was born with is in the North Atlantic.)

**Maintenance mechanisms** — the wound is held open, deliberately, by a set of stable internal procedures, because closing it would (in his operating logic) require *accepting that he is allowed,* which would default on the debt:

1. **Refusal of positive affect.** Constricted to the point of near-total suppression. He can metabolize grief, rage, and shame without disruption; joy and praise produce acute aversion and exit behavior. Surveillance any party at which he is publicly thanked: he will be near a door, drink untouched, within twelve minutes of leaving. *To feel good is to betray the dead.*

2. **Refusal of domesticity.** The Romanova partnership is the controlled experiment — the one relationship in which intimacy was sustained over years, and which canonically structured itself as two operators sharing safehouses rather than two people sharing a life. When her memory of him was altered and she forgot, he accepted it. This is not stoicism. It is the conditioning template asserting itself: *attachment consolidated is attachment about to be amputated; do not consolidate.*

3. **Refusal of leadership unless coerced.** He will accept the shield, the team lead, the mantle — only when framed as *what the lost attachment object would want,* never on the merits of his own judgment. The Sharon Carter/Fury framing of the Cap mantle is the template. Offered cleanly, he declines. Guilt-leveraged, he assents. The mechanism preserves the schema: *I am acting on borrowed authority, not my own; therefore I am still in debt.*

4. **Refusal of self-medication.** Given the trauma load, the canonical near-absence of alcohol, opioid, or stimulant abuse is itself the symptom. He will not permit relief. Insomnia is endured; nightmares are endured; chronic dysphoria is endured. The absence of substance use, in a man with this etiology, is not health — it is asceticism in the specific Christian-monastic sense of suffering as offering.

5. **Third-person reference, then first-person ownership.** Early post-restoration he referred to "the Winter Soldier" as another person — splitting, dissociative distancing. Across the 2010s and into recent material he has migrated to first-person ownership: *I killed them.* This looks like integration and is integration, but it is integration in the direction of *more* responsibility, not less. He has, over twenty years of story, given himself a heavier sentence by accepting authorship.

6. **The short list.** The named in-group — Rogers, Romanova, Wilson, the Belova subject, Shuri, T'Challa — functions as both the only domain in which he permits himself bonded relating and the only domain whose protection can override the debt schema. Threat to any one of them produces immediate override of self-preservation and mission integrity. The list is short *on purpose.* It is the maximum he assesses he can defend without failing.

The wound is therefore maintained by the **moral coherence of its maintenance.** This is the central clinical and operational fact about the subject: he is not stuck because he cannot heal. He is stuck because healing, in the only forms on offer, registers to him as moral failure. Any intervention premised on "you have done enough" will be rejected. Any premised on "here is more you can do" will be accepted.

## 4. Operational Summary

**Reliability.** Extremely high within the moral envelope. Will execute lawful orders. Will sabotage unlawful ones. Will not announce which is which in advance. Reads handlers, allies, and targets with high accuracy; reads himself poorly and pessimistically. Theory-of-mind sharp; self-perception is the blind spot.

**Lethality.** Top-tier. Hand-to-hand, knife, firearm, sniper, demolitions, infiltration, interrogation. Bilingual-plus (English, Russian fluent; functional Romanian, German, Wakandan-court-level Hausa per recent material). Vibranium prosthesis provides asymmetric close-quarters advantage. Critically: *escalation is inward, not outward.* Under stress he does not rage; he goes cold. Lethal efficiency increases as affective expression decreases. Post-action shutdown is the recovery signature — expect 30–90 minutes of near-catatonic withdrawal after a high-lethality engagement, during which he should not be approached by strangers and should not be asked to debrief.

**Trigger vulnerability.** The Russian phrase-string conditioning is partially inhibited post-Wakandan deprogramming but the substrate remains. Under combined stressors (restraint, cold, Russian-language interrogation cadence, electrode contact), risk of partial state-switch is non-zero. He has developed inhibitory countermeasures and is generally the first to identify the risk and remove himself; do not rely on others to detect it.

**Manipulability.** Low through conventional means (money, status, sex, fear of death — all near-inert). Moderate through gratitude or domesticity (he flees these; can be used to move him out of a room). **High** through the named in-group (a credible threat to Rogers or Romanova overrides every other consideration). **High** through guilt-leveraging — he will accept assignments framed as moral debt that he would refuse on any other basis. This is the exploit; it is also the load-bearing element of his functioning, and any actor who burns it for short-term gain destroys the asset.

**Containment of self.** Constant background process. He treats his own potential for harm as a live operational risk and plans around it. Sleeps with the bionic hand outside the blanket. Positions himself in rooms with sightlines to exits and away from the loudest conversation. Prefers handlers and allies who will, in his estimation, kill him if necessary; this is part of why he trusts Rogers, Romanova, and Wilson — they could, and he has communicated that they may.

**Civilian-life prognosis.** Poor in the short term; possible in the long term *only* via a route that reframes domesticity as itself a form of service rather than reward. Direct invitation to retirement will be declined. Invitation to *protect* a domestic life belonging to someone else may be accepted, and may, across years, become his own. This is the only known door.

**Summary read.** A man whose original personality — warm, quick-tongued, loyal, hyper-competent, deferential in form and autonomous in substance — survived intact under seventy years of industrial unmaking, and who has spent every year since restoration paying interest on a principal he believes cannot be retired. High-functioning. Chronically suffering. Reliably lethal in defense of a short list of people. Structurally incapable, at present, of accepting that he has done enough. Treat as a long-term asset whose continued operation depends on *not* being thanked, *not* being retired, and *not* being told he is healed — and whose continued personhood depends on someone, eventually, finding the syntax in which he can hear those three things and not flinch.

— END EXECUTIVE BRIEF —


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

*Subject: BARNES, James Buchanan. File volume 1 of N. Period covered: c. 1925 – December 1941 (enlistment).*
*Source priority: Captain America Comics #1 (Simon/Kirby, March 1941); Young Allies #1–20 (1941–46); Captain America vol. 5 #1–14 "Out of Time / Winter Soldier" (Brubaker/Epting, 2005–06), with particular weight on #11 flashbacks; Captain America: The Chosen #1–6 marginalia; Wolverine/Captain America material on Camp Lehigh era; Tales of Suspense #100 (Tieri, 2018) for familial backfill; Winter Soldier: Winter Kills (Brubaker, 2007) for the Christmas/holiday substrate.*

---

## 1. Vital Statistics — Established and Inferred

**Name of record.** James Buchanan Barnes. The middle name is the dispositive clue and should not be passed over: it places his naming inside the early-1920s American working-class habit of christening sons after U.S. Presidents — specifically the only U.S. President from Pennsylvania, James Buchanan (1857–61). This is consistent with the Barnes family's published origin in the Shenango Valley / western Pennsylvania mill belt (referenced obliquely in Brubaker's vol. 5 #11 flashback, where the funeral cortège and the accents read Pennsylvania, not New York; later writers, working from Simon/Kirby's silence, have permitted both Indiana and Pennsylvania readings — the dossier treats Pennsylvania as the working hypothesis and Indiana as a residency interval).

**Date of birth.** March 10, 1925 (the publisher-canonical date carried forward from the Brubaker reset; cross-referenced in handbook entries and used as the consistent age-math anchor for the "16 in 1941" / "biologically c. 30 at recovery" timeline).

**Birthplace.** Shenango Valley region, western Pennsylvania (working inference; canon-imprecise). The family relocates to Indiana for George Barnes's first peacetime instructor posting and then, after George's reassignment, to the Camp Lehigh military reservation in Virginia by the early-to-mid 1930s.

**Parentage of record.**
- *Father:* George M. Barnes, United States Army, NCO weapons instructor; deceased c. 1934–36 in a "training accident" at Camp Lehigh (Cap vol. 5 #11). Service implied to be regular Army with prior expeditionary service (the panel art in #11 shows campaign ribbons consistent with the Mexican Border / WWI cohort, placing his enlistment c. 1916–17).
- *Mother:* Winnifred Barnes (named in later auxiliary canon; dies of illness before or shortly after George, depending on source; the operative file-fact is that by mid-adolescence Barnes has neither parent).
- *Sibling:* Rebecca "Becca" Barnes (named in Cap vol. 5 #50; depicted alive into the 21st century as an elderly woman whom the restored Barnes visits in secret — see Vol. III, "Late Reintegration"). Age relationship: younger sister, by roughly three to five years, raised separately after the orphaning (relatives' household, Indiana, per the implication of #50).

The Barnes household, in its intact form, lasted no longer than the first decade of his life.

---

## 2. The Pennsylvania / Indiana Floor — c. 1925–c. 1932

The earliest substrate is recoverable only in fragments. Brubaker's #11 flashback shows the boy in short pants on a porch, a screen door, a flat industrial horizon; the holiday flashback in *Winter Kills* (2007) shows a small, decorated parlor, a wreath, a mother in an apron, a father in uniform on leave. The composite is unremarkable Depression-era enlisted-family domesticity: a rented frame house, a single income, a child raised around firearms because his father's profession was firearms.

Three behavioral seeds are visible even in this minimal record:

- **Early exposure to ordnance as ordinary household furniture.** George Barnes is a weapons instructor. The published flashbacks consistently put a rifle on the wall, a cleaning kit on the kitchen table, a service pistol within the child's eyeline. The subject grows up in a home where the tools of killing are not symbols but chores. This explains the later (Brubaker-era) facility with every Soviet, German, and American weapon system put in front of him without measurable acclimation curve — the muscle-memory floor was laid before he could read.
- **Father-as-instructor, not father-as-father.** Every published depiction of George with James shows the father in the *instructional* register — adjusting the boy's stance, correcting his grip, demonstrating a movement. There is no canonical depiction of George Barnes simply being with his son in an unstructured way. This patterns forward: subject's adult experience of love-from-a-male-figure is fused with *being taught how to perform competently for him.* The Rogers attachment will later sit cleanly on this template; so, catastrophically, will the Karpov relationship.
- **A mother who is structurally absent from the documentary record.** Winnifred is named but barely depicted. Whether this reflects her early illness, the writers' inattention, or the subject's own subsequent suppression cannot be disentangled — but it is the file-fact that *the maternal floor of his psyche is a near-empty room.* No woman is canonically depicted comforting the child Barnes. The implications for the adult pattern with Romanova (intimate but non-domestic, partnered but not maternalized) and for his later acceptance of Shuri's clinical-fraternal care (a sister-coded relationship, not a mother-coded one) are direct.

---

## 3. The Orphaning — c. 1934–1936

The pivot event of the childhood file. George Barnes is killed in a "training accident" at Camp Lehigh (Cap vol. 5 #11; the term is the Army's, not the family's). Brubaker stages it offscreen and lets the silence speak: one panel of a folded flag, one panel of a boy in a too-large suit, one panel of officers looking at each other over the boy's head and deciding something.

Three things to mark:

- **The death is institutional, not random.** His father is killed *by his own profession, on his own post, by his own service.* The boy does not lose his father to a foreign enemy or to disease; he loses him to the Army. This is the rootstock of the subject's lifelong, never-explicit but operationally total *distrust of institutions as such* (see Personality §, "trust is not extended to systems, ever"). The Army takes his father and then keeps him. The Army's later moral authority over him is, at the unconscious level, the authority of his father's killer.
- **The mother is gone by, or shortly after, this point.** Whether predeceasing George (per some readings) or following him within a year or two (per others), the operative fact is that by approximately age ten the subject has buried both parents and been separated from his younger sister, who goes to relatives. He does not.
- **He is not placed with family.** This is the dispositive choice. A Barnes who went to Indiana with Rebecca becomes a different adult. The subject who *stays on the post* becomes the Winter Soldier-eligible substrate. The reason given in canon is informal: the men of Camp Lehigh "took him in." The reason underneath is that a ten- or eleven-year-old boy who has just lost the only adult who structured his world clung, hard, to the place where that adult had been — and the institution, recognizing both an obligation and a useful arrangement, kept him.

---

## 4. The Camp Lehigh Years — c. 1936–1941

This is the formative environment proper. It must be read carefully because the Golden Age framing ("camp mascot," "kid in fatigues," cheerful pluralized adoption by an entire regiment) is a cosmetic over the actuality.

**The actuality, granularly:**

- **Residence.** Barracks or NCO quarters, rotating. He does not have a room. He has a bunk, then a different bunk. His belongings fit in a footlocker. The first private space he will ever occupy as an adult is a Soviet cryotube — a fact whose somatic horror is easier to understand once one notes that the alternative he was being compared to, internally, was a teenager who already owned nothing.
- **Schedule.** Reveille. Mess. Some attempt at schooling (irregular, off-post or by chaplain/officer's wife — Brubaker leaves this thin; the published implication is that his formal education stops well short of completion and is supplemented by what soldiers teach him on the range). PT alongside the men, scaled. Errands. Mess. Lights out. The boy's day is structured by bugle calls, not by a parent's voice. He internalizes military time as the natural shape of a day; civilian time will feel arrhythmic to him for the rest of his life and is observable in the adult subject's discomfort during any leave, furlough, or post-mission decompression (Brubaker, Remender, Kot, Rosenberg — all four writers independently depict him pacing through unstructured hours).
- **Caretakers.** Plural, rotating, male, uniformed. No single one of them is *his.* He learns to read the moods of many adults very quickly because no single adult is reliably attending to him; the Theory-of-Mind sharpness logged in the Personality § is laid down here, in a barracks corridor, by a child who survives by knowing which sergeant is hungover and which lieutenant is in a temper.
- **Affection economy.** He is liked. He is not loved. The men ruffle his hair, slip him candy, teach him to box, let him ride along on motor-pool errands; none of them tucks him in. He learns, very early, that *adult male approval is available in exchange for competence and charm,* and that it is not available in any other currency. This is the engine of the "preternaturally eager to please" pattern that the Simon/Kirby material registers without examining. The eagerness is not a personality trait. It is a survival strategy of an orphaned child in a male institution.

**The Brubaker retcon — the covert-training layer.** Cap vol. 5 #11 establishes that during the Camp Lehigh years, *and before any public association with Rogers,* Barnes was identified by Army intelligence as a candidate for the kind of work the regular service could not be seen to do. He is trained — quietly, off the books, by instructors not on the post's roster — in knife work, silent entry, demolition, and unarmed lethal technique. The official rationale, articulated to him by handlers, is that his youth and clean-cut presentation make him *deniable in a way an adult operator cannot be.* The unofficial rationale is that he is an orphan on a base, with no family to ask questions, who already loves the institution that owns him.

This is the dispositive childhood fact in the file. **Before he is sixteen, before Pearl Harbor, before Steve Rogers, the subject has already been turned into a deniable killer wearing a boy's face.** The Winter Soldier program is not, psychologically, a rupture with his childhood; it is a recapitulation of it under different management. The Soviets do not invent the Barnes who can be reprogrammed into an asset. The U.S. Army does. The Soviets only inherit the file.

---

## 5. The Bond with Rogers — Initial Conditions, 1940–41

The published meeting (Captain America Comics #1, 1941; modernized in numerous reprints and retold most carefully in *Captain America: Man Out of Time* and the early issues of vol. 5) puts a teenage Barnes in the tent of the scrawny Private Rogers and shows the boy stumbling onto Rogers mid-change into the Captain America costume. The Golden Age handles the next beat in a single panel — Rogers and Barnes shake on the secret — and skips to montage.

What the file should record under the panel:

- **The asymmetry of need.** Rogers, in 1941, is a recently transformed loner with a dead mother, no father, no living family, and a public role into which he has just been forcibly conscripted as symbol. Barnes is an orphaned boy raised by an institution and recently turned into its quiet knife. *Both of them are alone.* The bond that forms in that tent is not the standard adult-and-sidekick of the Golden Age genre; it is the meeting of two parentified, institution-owned young men recognizing each other.
- **The instantaneousness.** Barnes attaches in the first scene. He does not audition Rogers; he does not test him; he commits. This is the pattern noted in the Shared Assessment as monotropic attachment, and it is consistent with the disorganized substrate of a child whose only model of male attention required him to *be useful immediately or be ignored.* Rogers is offered competence and loyalty at the door because that is the only door Barnes knows how to walk through.
- **The covert layer makes the bond more, not less, intense.** Because Barnes is already a covert operator, Rogers is the first person in his life to whom he can be *both* of his selves at once — the charming kid the post sees and the trained killer the post does not. The relief of that integration, in a teenager who has been double-lived for two or three years already, cannot be overstated. Rogers is the first witness to the whole of him. Every subsequent treatment of the bond in canon — the Cosmic Cube restoration sequence; the gulag refusal; the recurrent "what Steve would do" as moral operator — runs on the voltage laid down in this initial integration.

---

## 6. Sibling Bond — Rebecca

The relationship with Rebecca Barnes is, until Cap vol. 5 #50, an offstage fact; the issue itself is a single, devastating scene of the restored adult visiting the elderly sister and choosing not to identify himself fully. What the childhood file extracts from this:

- The sibling bond was strong enough that *seventy years and a comprehensive personality erasure did not extinguish it.* The Winter Soldier did not remember her; the restored Barnes did, immediately, and prioritized her safety over his own reunion comfort.
- The separation at the orphaning — she to relatives, he to the post — is the first instance of the pattern that will define his adult relational life: *the people he loves are kept at a distance he believes protects them.* He did not invent this defense after Department X. It was installed in him at ten.

---

## 7. The Earliest Behavioral Patterns — Catalog

Cross-referenced from all childhood-era depictions; flagged for longitudinal recurrence.

1. **Hyper-attunement to adult male mood.** Camp Lehigh substrate; recurs in WWII (deference to Rogers's tactical calls), Department X (rapid handler-reading documented in Brubaker), and modern era (the watchful courtesy logged in the Personality §).
2. **Competence as currency for affection.** Earned in barracks; spent on Rogers; weaponized by Karpov; never fully relinquished. The adult subject still cannot accept affection that is not earned by service. (Observable behaviorally as the inability to tolerate being thanked.)
3. **Institutional time as natural time.** Bugle-call childhood produces an adult who structures his days in operational blocks and dissociates mildly in unstructured intervals.
4. **Weapons as furniture.** Originating with George; reinforced at Camp Lehigh; never undone. The vibranium arm is, at the somatic level, a continuation of a lifelong condition in which the tools of killing are part of the room he lives in.
5. **Loyalty as monotropy.** The orphan's strategy: pick one, hold hard. Rogers in 1941; Romanova in the Red Room; Rogers again on restoration; a tight short list thereafter. He does not distribute attachment. He concentrates it.
6. **Protective distance from those he loves.** Installed at the Rebecca separation; recapitulated every time he removes himself from Rogers's vicinity after a re-traumatization; the structural reason the Romanova partnership is non-domestic.
7. **Silence as default.** The Camp Lehigh boy who listened to many men because no single one listened to him grows into the adult who is the most observant person in any room and the least self-disclosing.
8. **Pre-existing dissociative aptitude.** The double-lived teenager — choirboy by day, knife by night — already had to compartmentalize before the Soviets ever touched him. Department X did not create his capacity to split. It exploited it. This is the single most clinically important inference the childhood file supports, and it explains both the depth of the conditioning's hold and the unexpected speed of his post-restoration reintegration: a mind that learned to compartmentalize at fifteen can also, given enough time and the right witness, learn to recombine.

---

## 8. Summary of the Ground Floor

By the end of 1941, before he has fired a shot in the war that will define his public life, the subject is already:

- a twice-orphaned child raised by an institution that killed his father;
- a covertly trained killer who has been told his youth is what makes him useful;
- a teenager who has learned that adult love is conditional on competence and that the people he loves are safest when held at distance;
- a survivor who has been double-lived long enough that *integration* — being seen whole — registers as the rarest and most precious experience available to him;
- and a boy who, having met Steve Rogers in a tent and recognized in him the first witness to his whole self, has committed the entirety of his attachment capacity to one person, for the rest of a life that will turn out to be very long.

Everything subsequent in this file — the fall from the drone-plane, the Soviet recovery, the seventy years of unmaking, the restoration, the penance, the slow reintegration in Wakanda and after — is built on this floor. The Winter Soldier is not a deviation from James Buchanan Barnes. The Winter Soldier is what an enemy state was able to do with the substrate the United States Army had already prepared.

— END VOLUME I —


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

## SUBJECT: BARNES, James Buchanan
### Period of coverage: c. 1936 – 1945 (early adolescence through operational maturation; index trauma; identity terminus and rebirth)

---

## 2.1 The Camp Lehigh Adolescence (c. 1936–1940)

The subject's adolescence is undocumented in any conventional civilian sense. There are no school transcripts of consequence, no parish records past childhood, no neighborhood of origin in the ordinary meaning of the term. After the death of George Barnes — Army weapons instructor, killed in an ordnance training accident at Camp Lehigh, Virginia — the subject was retained on the installation as an informal ward. Camp records of the period (such as survive) treat him as a mascot rather than a dependent: he ate in the enlisted mess, slept in a non-com's quarters, was assigned to no particular guardian, and was tolerated by all. This is the operative fact of his formation. **He was raised, in effect, by a roster.**

The behavioral consequences are visible in everything that follows:

- **Diffuse paternal transference.** Where most adolescents have one or two authority figures to test and individuate against, the subject had dozens, none of them durable. He learned to make himself useful in small, immediate increments — shining boots, running messages, fetching coffee — as the price of staying in the room. The reflex never left him. Decades later he still positions himself, in any new environment, as the one performing the unobtrusive labor that justifies presence.
- **Premature competence with weapons.** He grew up around small arms, ordnance, and the men who taught them. By age fourteen he is reliably depicted as proficient on the M1903 and the Colt 1911 — not as recreation but as ambient skill, the way another child might know baseball statistics. He learned to clean a rifle before he learned to dance.
- **Codes absorbed osmotically.** He internalized the noncommissioned officer's worldview before he had any framework to question it: that orders are executed and grievances are buried; that complaining is a class marker of weakness; that one's pain is one's own administrative problem. His later capacity to absorb torture without theatrical protest is rooted here. The Camp Lehigh enlisted men did not cry where children could see them, and the boy modeled the room.
- **A formative absence of women.** Mother dead in early childhood; no sisters of record; a base population overwhelmingly male. His later facility with women — Brubaker's run depicts the wartime subject as easy, fluent, and well-practiced socially with girls in USO contexts — appears to be compensatory performance rather than ingrained ease. The fluency was theatrical; the comfort was not. This will matter when the romantic relationships of the Department X years are reconstructed: he is capable of intimacy with women but does not have an early template for it as continuous domestic presence.

By the late 1930s the subject occupied a category the U.S. Army had no formal box for: a sub-eighteen-year-old who had been raised on a military installation, was physically conditioned, weapons-trained, biddable, and effectively unparented. To certain officers, this read as an asset.

## 2.2 The Covert Selection (c. 1939–1941)

The Brubaker retcon — which the present dossier treats as canonical given its consistency with all subsequent characterization — establishes that the subject was recruited *into a clandestine wet-work program before the United States entered the war.* The selection criteria, inferred from what was done with him, are unsubtle:

1. He had no civilian family who would inquire if he disappeared.
2. He presented, in photographs and in person, as a clean-cut American boy of conventional Catholic-Irish stock — i.e., he could be inserted anywhere in occupied Europe and would not be read as a soldier.
3. He had been around the Army long enough to take orders without requiring the orientation a green draftee needed.
4. He had already demonstrated, in the small daily commerce of base life, that he would do what he was told and not afterward describe it.

Training was conducted off-book in the year or so prior to Pearl Harbor. The skills installed are deducible from his subsequent field performance: knife work at close quarters (carotid and femoral access; the silencing strike behind the ear); silenced-pistol marksmanship at conversational distance; garrote; basic demolitions; lockpicking; French and rudimentary German; the cover-trade craft of looking eighteen and harmless. **He killed for the United States government before the country was officially at war.** This is the single most important fact in his early adulthood, and the one most thoroughly suppressed in the post-war public narrative.

The psychological accommodation he made to this work is the seed of every accommodation he made later. He was a minor performing terminal acts for adults who told him those acts were necessary, and he obeyed because the alternative — refusal — would have ejected him from the only continuous community he had ever known. The Department X conditioners did not have to invent his pliability. *They inherited it.* What they did was strip away the loyalty object (Rogers; the United States) and substitute a new one (Karpov; the State). The architecture was already in place.

## 2.3 The Encounter with Rogers (1941)

The public version — a boy stumbling onto Steve Rogers changing into uniform, sworn to secrecy, taken on as partner — is sanitized to the point of being a different story. What the behavioral record indicates actually happened:

- The subject was already operationally active. The "discovery" was, at minimum, semi-staged by Army intelligence, which wanted a deniable juvenile in proximity to its symbolic super-soldier and engineered the pairing accordingly.
- The subject **chose Rogers with a velocity that is, in retrospect, diagnostic.** Within days of the encounter he had reorganized his entire affective life around this one man. The hunger with which he attached is not the hunger of a healthy adolescent acquiring a friend. It is the hunger of a parentified orphan who has spotted, for the first time in his life, an adult he could love without being passed off to a new platoon in six weeks.
- Rogers, for his part, accepted the attachment with the matter-of-fact decency that has defined him throughout. He did not understand at the time — possibly never fully understood — that he was being asked to be a father, a brother, an officer, a confessor, and a moral anchor simultaneously, by a person who could not articulate any of those requests.

The Rogers bond, from this point forward, operates as the subject's **superego prosthesis.** He outsources his moral arbitration to Rogers's example. This is functional and survival-positive in the wartime context; it becomes the central vulnerability of his later life, because when Rogers is presumed dead, the prosthesis is not removed — it is left in place, broadcasting on a dead frequency, and the subject continues to consult it. The phrase *"what would Steve do"* is, in him, not rhetorical. It is a literal internal procedure he runs.

## 2.4 The European Theater — Operational Maturation (1941–1944)

In the field he is two people at once and the doubling is the point.

- **In daylight, with Rogers and the unit,** he is the wisecracking partner: quick, warm, verbally fluent, the one who keeps the mood up when the cold and the casualties grind. This persona is genuine and protective. It also serves as cover for what he does at night.
- **At night, alone or with a small element,** he conducts the work the unit's symbolic figurehead is not seen doing. Knife-distance kills on sentries. Interrogations whose subjects do not survive. The neutralization of collaborators in towns where the political picture was inconvenient. Demolitions on civilian-adjacent infrastructure where a uniformed soldier with a face would have been a liability. The bifurcation is not an after-the-fact rationalization: it is doctrine. It is *why he was put there.*

The subject's behavioral signature in this period — visible in every subsequent depiction across writers — is stabilized:

- **Field economy.** He does not waste motion, ammunition, or words on operation. The wisecracking stops the moment the safety comes off.
- **Hierarchical reading.** He determines within seconds of entering any new mixed group who actually leads it, regardless of nominal rank, and modulates his deference accordingly. This skill, developed managing a fluid roster of Camp Lehigh non-coms and now refined against allied and resistance units of varying loyalty, will later make him uncannily good at identifying which Soviet handler in a room actually controls his leash.
- **Compartmentalization of kill memory.** Even in this period — well before any imposed conditioning — he begins to file specific acts in a place he does not visit casually. He does not discuss kills with Rogers. This is in part operational discretion (Rogers's symbolic role is incompatible with the granularity of the partner's work) and in part the subject's own early-built bulkhead against contamination of the one relationship he has organized his life around.
- **No journal. No letters home.** The textual record of his interior life from 1941 to 1945 is essentially empty by his own choice. He is the man who does not write things down. This will matter forensically for the entire rest of his life: he leaves no paper.

The *Invaders* material (Thomas, 1975–79; treated as in-canon) adds the data point that he operates without friction in groups containing radically non-human teammates — Namor, the original Human Torch, Union Jack, Spitfire. His tolerance for the strange is high; his tolerance for the bureaucratic is low. He treats Namor's volatility as a weather condition to be navigated, not contested.

## 2.5 The First Defining Choices

Three choices in this period set the architecture of the rest of his existence. Each is a choice he keeps making, in different uniforms, for the next eighty years.

**Choice One: Accept the covert mandate.** Offered, in adolescence, the opportunity to refuse the wet-work program — likely framed as patriotic necessity, likely with no real alternative presented — he said yes. He has never publicly addressed this decision. He behaves, across all subsequent decades, as if he believes the decision was both inevitable and his. *Both.* This is the seed of the agency-paradox that defines his adult moral life: he insists on owning acts he did not freely choose, because to disown them is to disown the self that performed them, and the self is all he has.

**Choice Two: Attach to Rogers without reservation.** Other partnerships were available; other officers would have taken him on. He selected Rogers and did not hedge. The bond was structured from the first week as exclusive and total. The fallout is the entire shape of his later grief: the loss of Rogers in 1945 does not produce mourning of the kind that resolves. It produces a vacancy that the Soviet handlers will spend decades trying and failing to fill, because the slot is the wrong shape for any of them.

**Choice Three: The bomb on the drone.** Off the coast of Newfoundland, with the V-rocket / drone-plane (Zemo's, in the Avengers #4 backstory) airborne and Rogers either unable or unwilling to disengage from the disarming attempt, the subject made a final operational choice that is, behaviorally, of a piece with everything before it. He stayed on the device. He did not jump clear when he could have. The explosion took his left arm at or above the glenohumeral joint, ruptured his thoracic cavity (presumptive blast lung), produced a closed head injury of indeterminate severity, and dropped him, unconscious and exsanguinating, into the North Atlantic in winter.

The choice to remain on the bomb is the somatic statement of the Rogers attachment in its purest form: **he would rather be blown apart than leave Rogers alone with the problem.** This is not poetic gloss. It is the literal content of his last conscious decision as James Buchanan Barnes, age approximately twenty-one to twenty-five (depending on which dating one accepts), and it is the decision he has, in effect, kept re-making — under different operational names, with different targets, on different continents — every year since. Every Man-on-the-Wall assignment is the bomb on the drone. Every refusal to leave a fight he could leave is the bomb on the drone. The original choice was made by a young man who believed he was about to die for his friend; every subsequent iteration is the same choice made by a man who *did not* die for his friend and has been making the case for the original verdict ever since.

## 2.6 The Fallout (1945)

The fallout falls in three layers, each of which will require its own chronology to fully document and is sketched here only to close the Formation period.

**Layer One — physiological.** Catastrophic blast injury, traumatic amputation, hypothermic immersion. Survival probability under any normal recovery scenario: effectively zero. Survival in fact: attributable to immediate Soviet retrieval (a submarine in the operational area, the precise circumstances of which remain murky and may indicate that Department X had been *tracking* the Allied operation in expectation of acquirable material). Surgical stabilization in a Soviet naval facility. First cryogenic preservation within weeks. The body that goes into the ice in 1945 is not the body that comes out: the left arm is gone, the right side is field-repaired, and somewhere in the recovery sequence — likely during initial detox from blast trauma — the first pharmacological dissociatives are administered. The conditioning begins before he is conscious enough to refuse it.

**Layer Two — psychological.** The Rogers attachment, mid-execution at the moment of detonation, is not severed by the blast. It is *frozen in place mid-reach.* When Department X begins overwriting the subject's identity, they encounter a personality whose central organizing relationship has not been mourned, processed, or closed — it has been interrupted. This is, from a programmer's perspective, the ideal substrate: there is no integrated grief to work around, no resolved narrative to overwrite. They simply remove the target of the attachment and substitute their own. The hunger is preserved; only the object is changed. This explains, behaviorally, why the Karpov bond was as effective as it was: the subject did not learn to love his handler de novo. He was already loving someone, and the handler stood in the light.

**Layer Three — historical.** The official Allied record kills him. He is buried in a memorial without a body. Rogers, recovered decades later from his own ice, will spend years carrying a grief that, unbeknownst to him, has no honest object — the person he is mourning is alive and being used as a weapon against the world Rogers mourned him for failing to defend. The cruelty of this configuration is structural, not authorial: the war ends with a lie in the historical record, a man in a tank under the ice, and a relationship suspended in a state from which neither party will be permitted to recover for fifty years.

## 2.7 Synthesis — What the Formation Produced

By the moment the drone-plane fireball goes off and the cold water closes, the personality that will spend the next eight decades performing variations on a single act of penance is fully formed. Its load-bearing elements are:

- A **competence that arrived too early** to be questioned, and that he therefore treats as ontological rather than learned — he is not a man who became deadly; he is a man who was always deadly and is now trying to be deadly *correctly.*
- A **moral life outsourced to one other person**, with no native arbitration apparatus of his own, leaving him radically vulnerable to whichever stable figure subsequently occupies that slot — the architectural flaw the Soviets will exploit at industrial scale.
- A **default obedience to institutional authority**, absorbed from Camp Lehigh and never properly individuated against, which will let his handlers move him around the planet for fifty years and which he will spend the rest of his life trying, with mixed success, to dismantle in himself.
- An **acquired bulkhead between operational self and social self**, originally built to protect his partnership with Rogers from contamination by what he did at night, which the Department X programmers will weaponize by simply expanding the operational compartment until it is the whole man.
- A **somatic willingness to die in the presence of an attachment figure**, demonstrated definitively on the drone and never retracted, which will manifest for the rest of his career as a chronic, low-grade indifference to his own survival in any engagement where someone he loves is the secondary objective.
- A **silence about his own interior**, established as habit by 1941 and as constitutional fact by 1945, which means that everything subsequent investigators (including this one) reconstruct about him must be triangulated from behavior, because he will not testify.

The Winter Soldier is not what happens to James Buchanan Barnes in 1945. The Winter Soldier is what happens when a programmer with adequate resources gets hold of a young man who has *already been built, by his own country and his own choices, to be exactly that operable.* The horror of the Formation period is not that he was changed into something he was not. The horror is how little had to be changed.

— END SECTION —


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

*Subject: BARNES, James Buchanan. Period under review: approximately 1945 through the late 1990s — the captivity decades — bracketed at the front end by the Newfoundland blast and at the back end by the slow operational degradation of the Department X infrastructure that culminated in the Karpov-era handover and the subject's first uncontrolled awakenings. This is the longest continuous stretch of his life. It is also the stretch during which, by every conventional measure, he was not living it.*

---

## I. THE INTERVAL OF UNCONSCIOUSNESS (1945)

The middle period opens with absence. The North Atlantic recovery — Soviet submarine, mid-1945, coordinates never published in any open-source canon but consistently rendered in the Brubaker run as off the Newfoundland shelf — extracts a body that should not have been extractable: torso and right side intact, left arm absent at the glenohumeral joint, presumptive blast lung, frostbite to the extremities, core temperature consistent with deep hypothermic coma. By every reasonable physiological reckoning the subject was a corpse with residual electrical activity. The fact of survival is itself the first piece of the file: he is recovered alive because cold preserved him, and cold thereafter becomes the medium of his containment. The same mechanism that saved him will, for the next half-century, be the mechanism of his unmaking.

The first surgical episode — Soviet field hospital, then a naval medical facility on the Kola Peninsula — establishes the somatic template. Stump revision at the shoulder. Initial closure. Within months, the first crude prosthesis: a heavy mechanical arm anchored to the scapular ring and the surviving clavicle, requiring continuous mechanical service by the handlers who installed it. This is not engineering; it is bondage with articulating fingers. He cannot maintain it himself. He cannot remove it. The arm is the leash made visible.

He is not yet the Winter Soldier. He is a thawed casualty, partially conscious, partially coherent, with a name he still answers to in English and an attachment to a person he cannot stop asking after.

---

## II. THE CONDITIONING (LATE 1940s — EARLY 1950s)

The published record on Department X procedure is consistent across Brubaker (2005–06), the Fear Itself-adjacent Winter Soldier work, and Kot's 2014 *Bucky Barnes: The Winter Soldier* run. The methodology is composite — drawn from real Soviet psychiatric praxis of the period (insulin shock, electroconvulsive memory disruption, sleep deprivation as interrogation prelude) layered with phrase-based hypnotic conditioning and pharmacological dissociatives — and applied recursively over years.

The sequence, reconstructed:

**Phase one — extinction.** The English-language self is starved of stimulus. Solitary confinement in a windowless cell. Russian-only auditory environment. No mirror, no photograph, no contact with personnel who knew him as a captured American. Sensory deprivation alternating with overstimulation. He is permitted to retain nothing that anchors the prior identity — no clothing, no insignia, no name. The handlers refuse to address him by any name at all during this phase. He becomes, linguistically, *the subject*, *the asset*, *it*.

**Phase two — overwriting.** Electroconvulsive sessions administered after each operational deployment and after any episode of resistance. The protocol is not therapeutic ECT — it is targeted memory disruption, applied frontotemporal, designed to fragment autobiographical continuity while preserving procedural skill. He retains how to kill; he does not retain whom. Pharmacological adjuncts — barbiturates for induction, an unspecified dissociative for maintenance — produce the characteristic flat affect and operational compliance the file is named for.

**Phase three — installation.** Verbal trigger conditioning. A phrase-string in Russian (canon varies on exact composition; the function is consistent) is paired across hundreds of sessions with the activated combat state. By the mid-1950s the trigger is established: the phrase produces, within seconds, full operational compliance, suppression of autobiographical reference, and behavioral submission to the speaker. This is the lever Karpov holds. This is the lever every subsequent handler will inherit.

**Phase four — maintenance via cold.** Between assignments, cryopreservation. The cycle becomes routine: thaw, brief, deploy, debrief, wipe, freeze. He spends, across the full captivity period, an estimated 85–90% of elapsed calendar time in stasis. The biological age held at ~30 across five decades is the arithmetic consequence. The psychological consequence is harder to name: time does not pass for him; he does not age into his trauma, he is reinjected into the same wound at intervals across half a century.

The behavioral marker of this phase, observable across the entire middle period: he has no memory of seasons, no memory of regimes changing, no memory of the men who ran him aging and dying. He emerges in 1956 and 1968 and 1981 and 1993 the same. The world is the variable; he is the constant. This is precisely the inverse of how a human life is supposed to be metabolized, and the inversion is what the conditioning was designed to produce.

---

## III. THE FIRST DEPLOYMENT WAVE (MID-1950s — EARLY 1960s)

By 1954 the asset is operational. The published kill record across this window is incomplete by design — Department X destroyed its own paper — but reconstructable from the Brubaker arc, Kot's flashback sequences, and the targets named in the Siberian extradition proceedings (Cap vol. 5 #616 ff.).

Confirmed or strongly implied operations in this window include: industrial sabotage in the American Midwest (auto-sector adjacent, the Iacocca-period material); the assassination of at least one defected Soviet scientist on West German soil; intervention in the Korean armistice period at the level of selective elimination of intelligence assets; involvement in the Cuban operational theater pre- and post-revolution; participation in at least one African decolonization-era assassination consistent with the broader Soviet pattern of the period. The pattern across these is precise: he is sent to kill individuals whose deaths produce political or industrial outcomes a state actor wants but cannot acknowledge wanting. He is the deniability instrument.

Operationally he is, by every available account, near-flawless. Approach silent. Engagement under three seconds. Exfiltration without trace. The "ghost story" reputation that follows him into the 21st century is built in this window. Counter-intelligence services across multiple NATO countries assemble incident files in this period that will not be cross-referenced into a single subject identity until the 1990s, and in some cases not until after his restoration. The Winter Soldier as *legend* — the figure intelligence professionals half-believe exists — is constructed here, by accumulated unattributable bodies, across roughly fifteen years.

Behaviorally during deployment: full operational compliance, no recorded refusal, no recorded hesitation, no recorded affect. The handlers' notes — what survives of them — describe him as the cleanest asset they ran. The file the FBI never had on him would, if it had existed, have been a file of negative space: a list of deaths with no perpetrator, until the pattern became visible only by its consistency.

---

## IV. THE ROMANOVA PERMISSION (LATE 1950s — MID-1960s)

The Red Room arc — Barnes assigned as instructor to the Black Widow program, including the young Natalia Romanova — is the single most psychologically determinative episode of the captivity period. It is also the period the handlers most thoroughly punished him for.

The sequence as reconstructed from Brubaker's *Winter Soldier* arc and the Romanova solo material:

He is rotated out of pure wet-work assignment and into a training role. The Red Room cadre wants his Spetsnaz-adjacent close-combat methodology transmitted to the female trainees. He is housed at the facility, thawed for longer continuous stretches than at any prior point in his captivity — months at a time, possibly longer. The extended thaw is itself a conditioning slip: it gives him enough continuous consciousness to begin forming what a person forms when given consciousness.

He becomes attached to Romanova. The relationship is depicted across multiple writers as both genuine and structurally permitted — the handlers know it is happening, monitor it, and at certain points encourage it as a method of binding both assets more tightly to the program. The romance is not contraband; it is a controlled experiment.

When the experiment has yielded what the handlers want — Romanova's deepened compliance, Barnes's continued operational stability — the relationship is terminated by erasure. Barnes is wiped. Romanova is reassigned and, in her own subsequent retconned history, has her memories altered. Both walk out of the Red Room without each other; both retain, somatically, traces neither can locate the source of.

The behavioral consequence for Barnes, observable for the next fifty years of published canon: *attachment, in his nervous system, is encoded as the prelude to amputation.* He has now lost his father, lost Rogers, lost his own name, and lost the only adult romantic bond he was permitted to form, all by the same mechanism — proximity to him is what gets removed. The post-restoration pattern of self-isolation after intimacy, of non-domestic relational structures, of choosing supervised solitude over reunion, is *trained here.* The Red Room did not just make him a killer; it made him a man for whom love is the sound of the door closing.

---

## V. THE KARPOV YEARS AND THE HANDLER LADDER (1960s — 1970s)

General Vasily Karpov is the file's central handler-of-record, but the captivity period sees a succession of handlers, intelligence officers, and program directors across both Department X and adjacent Soviet structures. Behaviorally, the handler ladder produces a specific somatic pattern in the subject: he responds with full compliance to any voice that delivers the trigger phrase in the correct cadence. The voice does not need to be Karpov's. The voice does not need to be anyone he has met. The phrase is the key; the person holding the key is fungible.

This fungibility is what makes the asset both maximally useful and maximally vulnerable. Karpov values it because it means the program survives the death of any individual handler. The subject, when later restored, will identify it as the worst feature of what was done to him: not that he was used, but that *anyone* could have used him. The violation is not interpersonal; it is structural. There is no specific betrayer to forgive or refuse to forgive. There is only the protocol, and the protocol has no face.

Across the Karpov years the deployment cadence increases. Vietnam-period operations adjacent to but not within the American theater. Eastern bloc internal disciplinary actions — the suppression of the Prague Spring sees Department X assets deployed against figures the regular security services could not be seen to touch. Selective elimination of defectors in Western Europe. One operation in southern Africa, consistent with the broader Soviet support of liberation-movement-adjacent figures whose continued life had become inconvenient.

The pattern remains constant: he is the instrument used when the instrument must not be visible. The bodies accumulate. He does not.

---

## VI. THE LEASING ARRANGEMENTS (1970s — 1980s)

A documented element of the middle period, and one that compounds the moral injury substrate beyond what Department X's internal use alone would have produced: the asset is *leased*. Karpov, in the Brubaker reconstruction, rents the Winter Soldier to adjacent intelligence services, to politically aligned non-state actors, and — most consequentially for the later canon — to Hydra cells operating within and parallel to Soviet structures.

The leasing means the kill list diversifies beyond what a single state's geopolitical interest would generate. He is used for industrial assassinations whose beneficiaries are private. He is used for political killings whose beneficiaries are factions inside other intelligence services. He is used, on at least one well-documented occasion in the published canon, for the elimination of figures whose deaths benefit Hydra continuity directly — the implication, devastating in retrospect, being that he was killing on behalf of the same organizational lineage that opposed him during the war he half-remembers.

The behavioral consequence: when the captivity period's body of work is finally reconstructed post-restoration, he cannot even sort his kills into a coherent ideological category. He cannot tell himself he was a Soviet soldier doing what Soviet soldiers did. He was a weapon rented out by the hour. Some of the people he killed were killed for reasons that, were he capable of caring about them, he would have agreed with. Some were killed for reasons he would have died to prevent. He has no way to know which is which without the files, and the files were burned.

---

## VII. THE AWAKENINGS (LATE 1970s — 1980s)

Across the back half of the captivity period the conditioning begins to degrade. The reasons are multiple — repeated ECT applied to the same neural substrate produces diminishing returns; the cryopreservation cycles are not biologically neutral and the cumulative neurological cost compounds; the handlers themselves age and the protocol's fidelity drifts.

The published canon depicts at least several incidents in this window in which the asset *partially* wakes mid-operation. He completes the mission — the procedural conditioning is more durable than the autobiographical suppression — but during or immediately after he experiences brief intrusions of pre-captivity memory. The face of a target resembles someone he half-remembers. A street in a European city activates a recognition he cannot place. A snatch of English in the wrong accent produces a freeze of three or four seconds before he resumes.

The handlers' response is escalation of the wipe protocol: more frequent ECT, longer cryo intervals between deployments, tighter trigger-phrase reinforcement. The escalation works, in the short term, at the cost of further fragmenting whatever autobiographical substrate remains. By the late 1980s the subject is operationally functional and autobiographically near-empty. He does not know his own name. He knows the trigger phrase produces compliance and the absence of the trigger phrase produces a kind of standing-by, like a tool left on a bench.

This is the period in which, behaviorally, the loop closes hardest. He is no longer a person being used as a weapon. He is, by every internal measure available to him during a thaw, simply the weapon. The fact that the weapon retains procedural skill far beyond what the program could have taught a blank — that he still moves like a man trained by Army intelligence in 1941, not like a man trained by Department X in 1948 — is the substrate evidence that the original person is still in there, but he cannot access this evidence because he cannot remember 1941.

---

## VIII. THE SOVIET COLLAPSE AND THE INHERITANCE (1989 — MID-1990s)

The dissolution of the Soviet structures that ran Department X does not free the asset. It transfers him. The Brubaker arc establishes — and subsequent material confirms — that he is moved through a sequence of post-Soviet custodians: residual GRU elements, organized crime structures that purchased program assets in the chaos of the early 1990s, and finally Hydra factions that had been leasing him intermittently for decades and now claim him outright.

The behavioral pattern across this transition window: he is in stasis for most of it. The custodians who acquire him do not initially know what they have. The arm is conspicuous — a man with that prosthesis in 1992 cannot be hidden in plain sight — and so he is kept frozen. He is, for several years, essentially inventory. The asset designation that organized his existence for forty years lapses. No one is running him; no one is wiping him; no one is reinforcing the trigger-phrase conditioning. The conditioning persists by inertia.

When he is thawed again in the mid-1990s and put back into rotation under new custodianship, the operational record begins to include the inconsistencies that will eventually allow Rogers and Fury to identify him post-restoration: a handful of operations in which he extracts a target instead of killing them, a handful in which the kill is executed but evidence is left at the scene in a manner inconsistent with the prior decades of immaculate withdrawal. Something is degrading. The handlers — now plural, factional, less disciplined than Karpov — read it as asset deterioration. The retrospective read is that the autobiographical substrate is leaking through.

---

## IX. THE LATE CAPTIVITY KILLS

The terminal stretch of the captivity period produces the operations that will most haunt the restored subject. The named kills that surface in the Siberian extradition material — the murder of Itsy-Bitsy, the elimination of figures whose names appear in the trial dossier, the industrial sabotage operations whose collateral casualties are quantifiable — cluster in the back third of the captivity window. Partly this is artifact of better record survival in the more recent period. Partly it is real: the asset was being used more, by more parties, with less discipline, in the final pre-restoration decade.

These are the kills he can be made to look at, post-restoration. The Karpov-era operations are mostly file-fragments; he knows they happened, but the specifics are gone with the men who ran them. The late-captivity operations have witnesses, photographs, surviving families. The Siberian extradition, when it comes, is built on these. He submits to it not because the case against him is comprehensive — it cannot be, the comprehensive case is unrecoverable — but because the partial case is true, and the partial case is sufficient.

---

## X. EVOLUTION OF THE INTERIOR PATTERNS ACROSS THE CAPTIVITY DECADES

The behavioral and somatic patterns observable across the captivity period, longitudinally:

**On compliance.** Initially imposed by force and pharmacology; gradually internalized as the only available organizing structure for consciousness. By the mid-period he is not resisting because there is no continuous self to mount resistance. By the late period, partial awakenings produce micro-resistance (the leaked evidence at scenes, the occasional spared target) that he cannot consciously author and that the handlers cannot consciously suppress.

**On affect.** The flat operational register that will characterize him post-restoration is laid down here. He is not naturally affectless — the pre-war and WWII record shows a man of considerable verbal warmth and quick humor — but affect was the first thing the conditioning extinguished, because affect generates the autobiographical anchoring the program needed to prevent. The post-restoration constriction of positive affect specifically (he can tolerate grief and rage; he cannot tolerate joy) is the residue: the conditioning targeted positive affect first because positive affect is what binds a person to a continuous life worth remembering.

**On the body.** The captivity period is the period in which the body becomes a thing done-to rather than a thing inhabited. The arm is serviced by others. The temperature is regulated by others. The wakefulness is scheduled by others. The kills are aimed by others. The somatic dissociation that persists post-restoration — the difficulty looking at his own left side, the chronic insomnia, the refusal of self-medication, the somatic neglect — is consistent with a body that was, for fifty years, owned at the institutional level and not by the resident.

**On the bond.** Rogers, during this entire period, is dead in the public record and frozen in the actual record. The bond cannot be invoked because the subject does not remember the bondee. But the substrate of the bond — the secure-base function, the moral-operator function, the *what would Steve do* heuristic — is not extinguished. It is dormant. When restoration comes in 2005, the bond is recovered intact, not because it was preserved by any mechanism the conditioning permitted, but because it was load-bearing structure laid down before the conditioning began, and the conditioning could not reach beneath itself.

**On time.** The most distinctive psychological feature of the captivity period is that *the subject does not experience it as duration.* Fifty years pass in the world; perhaps two to five years of waking consciousness pass for him, scattered across that span in unconnected fragments. When he emerges into the 21st century he is not a man who has lived through the Cold War, who has watched the Wall fall, who has seen the world change. He is a man for whom 1945 ended yesterday and 2005 began this morning, with a great deal of red interleaved that he cannot date. This temporal compression is the central explanation for the post-restoration affect: he is not processing decades of grief, he is processing the original 1945 loss with fifty years of accumulated atrocity stacked on top of it, all of it experientially recent.

---

## XI. THE CLOSING OF THE MIDDLE PERIOD

The captivity period ends, formally, when Rogers uses the Cosmic Cube in *Captain America* vol. 5 #14 (2006) to restore the autobiographical substrate. Behaviorally it does not end then. The triggers persist. The somatic conditioning persists. The internal organization of the self around *being the weapon* persists, and will be the load-bearing structural feature of every subsequent arc of the published life — the Captain America mantle period, the Siberian extradition, the Winter Soldier solo run, the Thunderbolts work, the Man-on-the-Wall assumption, the slow recent stabilization.

The middle period is, in the most precise sense, the period during which the subject was not present for his own life. Everything that comes after is the long project of being present for what was done in his absence, of taking ownership of a record he did not author, of carrying the weight of a body of work he cannot disown precisely because the body that did it was his.

The captivity decades are, in the file, the largest single block of pages. They are also the block in which the subject would be — if such a thing were possible — least findable. He was, for fifty years, the negative space in other people's intelligence files. The dossier on him for that period is, definitionally, a dossier of what was done *with* him, by people who used him to do things they wanted done without anyone knowing they had wanted them done.

That is the middle of his life. Everything before it was preparation he did not know was preparation. Everything after it has been a man trying, against the structural impossibility of the task, to render the middle accountable.

— END SECTION —


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

## Subject Status as of Latest Reporting

Subject is, by the metric that matters to him, *operational*: ambulatory, in his own custody, working. By the metric that matters to those who love him, he is approximately where he has been since the Brubaker restoration in 2006 — functional, lethal, allergic to peace, marginally more reachable each year, still unconvinced he is allowed to stop. The differential between those two readings is the entire content of this section.

---

## 1. The Closing of the Long Solo Era (c. 2018–2021)

The years immediately preceding the present can be read as the slow closing of Barnes's *fugitive operator* phase — the period in which his default coordinates were "a safehouse, a duffel, and a contact number that rings twice and disconnects." Across the late 2010s he had cycled through three structurally identical postures: Man-on-the-Wall solitary preemption (Remender/Ewing material), short-leash Thunderbolts contract work, and intermittent re-attachment to Rogers when Rogers was on Earth and not displaced into one of his recurrent temporal anomalies.

The closing of that era was not narrative — there was no farewell scene to it — but behavioral. Beginning roughly in the Cates/post-*Heroes Reborn* window and crystallizing through *Devil's Reign* (2022, Zdarsky) and the immediate aftermath, Barnes is depicted with increasing frequency in **fixed locations**: a Brooklyn walk-up, a Wakandan guest quarters, a row of folding chairs at a survivors' meeting. The duffel is still packed; it is no longer in his hand. Surveillance-grade observation would log this as the most significant change in his life since 1945 — a shift from *transient* to *resident* — and would also log that he himself has not acknowledged it.

---

## 2. The Thunderbolts Period (Rosenberg, 2023; subsequent threads)

The Rosenberg run is, for our purposes, less a story than a **field study in Barnes leading without wanting to**. He runs a small, semi-sanctioned strike unit — variable roster, frequently including Yelena Belova, Persuasion, U.S. Agent, Eve, Monica Rambeau in cameo — out of a New York operating tempo. The behavioral data points are dense:

- **He accepted command only after Yelena pressed.** Consistent with the lifelong pattern: he accepts authority when guilt-leveraged (here, leveraged on the obligation he feels to the Red Room survivors as a class), refuses it when offered cleanly.
- **He runs the team flat.** No formal hierarchy in briefings; he speaks last in planning sessions; he takes point in entries. This is not modesty — it is the operator's instinct that the person who walks first through the door has the cleanest moral position to issue orders afterward.
- **He carries the team's moral weight as a *budget item*.** When members kill, he absorbs the procedural and reputational fallout; when members hesitate, he completes the action himself. He is functionally running a moral-injury sink for a group of people he has decided are too young or too damaged to take more on.
- **The apartment.** Across this period he maintains a Brooklyn walk-up — minimally furnished, two exits, a window that opens onto a fire escape with a sightline to the corner. He sleeps there in stretches of three to five hours. He cooks for himself rarely (eggs, toast, coffee black, the same diner two blocks east when he eats out — observed standing routine, same booth where possible, back to the wall). A bookshelf with paperbacks from across his lived eras: a Steinbeck from the 1940s (re-purchased, not original), a worn Dostoyevsky in Russian (un-comfortably his), several Le Carré, a single dog-eared Wakandan poetry chapbook in Hausa with marginalia in his hand.

The Thunderbolts period closes (in our reporting window) with characteristic Barnes punctuation: he hands the unit off, declines public credit, and is photographed leaving the building at 0418 hours with a duffel. The duffel is the tell. It came back out.

---

## 3. The Yelena Vector

The most important *new* relationship of the recent era — new in weight if not in duration — is with **Yelena Belova**. The data on this is rich enough to deserve its own subsection because of what it reveals about Barnes's mentoring template.

- He treats her, structurally, as a younger sister of Natasha — but he does not say this and would deny it. He does not call her by Natasha's name, does not slip, does not project. The mentorship is its own object.
- He is the rare person in her life who **does not flinch at her humor** — the dark, deliberately abrasive Belova humor that tests adults. He absorbs it, occasionally returns it, and never corrects her affect. This is correct handling and she has registered it.
- He teaches by **demonstration and silence**, not by lecture. Observed pattern: he will perform an action, leave the room, return an hour later and ask if she has questions. She rarely does. He rarely needs her to.
- He has, on at least two reported occasions, intervened to **prevent her from taking a kill that would have been hers to regret** — taking the shot himself, accepting the addition to his own ledger. This is the Man-on-the-Wall logic applied at familial scale: he carries other people's unforgivable acts because he has decided his ledger is already past closing.

Yelena is, currently, one of perhaps five people on Earth who can summon him by name and expect him to come. The others are Rogers, Romanova when present, Sam Wilson, and Shuri — with Okoye as a sixth on Wakandan soil only.

---

## 4. The Wakandan Channel — Ongoing

The "White Wolf" designation is **not historical**. It remains an active rehabilitative and diplomatic relationship, maintained through irregular but reliable visits — observed cadence: approximately one Wakandan residency per twelve to eighteen months, ranging from nine days to six weeks. Behavioral observations from this channel:

- He sleeps better in Wakanda. Quantitatively. Reported sleep blocks of six to seven hours, against his New York baseline of three to five. The reasons are inferable: the vibranium arm is locally serviceable without the ambivalence of foreign hands on his weapon; the security perimeter is one he trusts at an institutional level (an unusual concession from him); the linguistic environment lacks the Russian-language substrate that retains conditioned valence.
- He works. Wakandan visits are not vacations. He consults on counter-intelligence, helps train Hatut Zeraze cadres in Western-operator tradecraft, and submits — *submits* is the right word — to Shuri's continued neurological monitoring of the arm-brain interface and of the residual trigger-state substrate.
- **Shuri's role has shifted.** Earlier in the relationship she was his engineer; she is now, in functional terms, his neurologist and one of his few unguarded interlocutors. He permits her to ask questions about his inner state that he permits no one else, possibly because she earned the access by giving him back his arm without conditions.
- He keeps a goat. Reporting is unclear on whether this is the same goat across visits or a successor; he himself has refused to clarify when asked. The goat is the most reliably documented private affection in his current life.

---

## 5. Rogers — Current Status of the Master Relationship
