Rogers is present, on Earth, in roughly his historical aspect. The Barnes–Rogers axis is the load-bearing structural element of Barnes's psychology and remains so. Current observations:

- **Frequency of contact has stabilized into something resembling normalcy.** Weekly, sometimes more. They train together in a Brooklyn gym that neither of them owns and both of them treat as semi-private. They do not always speak during these sessions; the co-presence is the point.
- **Barnes still defers to Rogers in public and operates as a peer in private.** This is the lifelong pattern; it has not changed and likely will not.
- **The "what would Steve do" operator has weakened.** Across recent depictions Barnes is increasingly making moral calls *as himself*, sometimes against what Rogers would do, and tolerating the disagreement. This is integration. Twenty years post-restoration, he is finally beginning to trust his own conscience as a primary instrument rather than as Rogers's auxiliary.
- **Rogers has stopped trying to fix him.** Also integration — on Rogers's side. The current shape of the friendship is two old men who have agreed to stop pretending either of them is going to be cured, and to keep showing up anyway.

---

## 6. Romanova — Current Status

Natasha's presence in Barnes's life across this recent window has been **intermittent by her design, accepted by his**. When she is present, they slot back into the safehouse-not-household configuration that has characterized them since the Brubaker solo. When she is absent — including across the periods of her successive deaths, resurrections, and memory alterations — Barnes does not pursue, does not mourn aloud, and does not replace.

The most diagnostic recent data point: when Natasha's memory of him has been compromised, he has consistently *re-introduced himself at the level she could meet him* rather than attempting to restore the prior intimacy. He treats her selfhood, including the parts of it that no longer include him, as sovereign. This is the most mature expression of his attachment style on record and is, in the analyst's view, the single clearest evidence that he has internalized — finally — that love does not require possession of memory.

He is alone, by the operative definition. He is not lonely in the way the file would have predicted twenty years ago.

---

## 7. Sam Wilson — The Lateral Bond

The relationship with **Sam Wilson** has, in the recent era, matured from grudging co-belligerence into one of the more important lateral bonds in Barnes's life. Wilson is the rare person who is neither a superior officer (Rogers), a fellow-perpetrator (Romanova), a charge (Yelena), nor a benefactor (Shuri/T'Challa). He is a *peer*. Barnes does not have many peers. The friendship is conducted largely through dry mutual irritation, shared operational competence, and the unspoken agreement that neither will make the other talk about feelings. Wilson is currently Captain America in the relevant continuity; Barnes treats the shield as Wilson's without ambivalence — a sign of how far he has come from his own period of wearing it.

---

## 8. Somatic Status, Current

- **The arm:** Wakandan-engineered vibranium, neurally integrated, self-serviceable in routine maintenance, requires Shuri-tier intervention only for deep diagnostics. He no longer flinches when civilians notice it; he still prefers long sleeves in non-operational settings. The plates retract or articulate near-silently — a deliberate engineering choice on Shuri's part to remove the audible *click-whirr* of the Soviet arm, which was a sensory tell that distressed him.
- **Sleep:** chronic insomnia continues; nightmare content remains era-specific (1950s–1980s Winter Soldier kills predominate; recent operational kills appear less often, suggesting his conscience has triaged the older material as the primary debt). He has been observed to pace specific routes when awake at night — in the Brooklyn apartment, a circuit from the window to the door to the kitchen sink and back, roughly nine minutes per lap.
- **Diet:** unchanged across decades — protein-forward, low ceremony, eaten standing or at counter when alone. He will sit for a full meal only in company.
- **Substance use:** still notably absent. One observed exception: he will accept a single drink in social settings when refusal would be conspicuous, nurses it, leaves it unfinished. He does not get drunk. He has not been observed drunk in the entire published record.
- **Body management:** trains daily, multiple modalities (calisthenics, knife forms, firearm dry-practice, occasional running — he prefers bridges and river paths, sightlines in both directions). The body is maintained as a tool, not enjoyed as a self.

---

## 9. Public/Civil Status

Legally, Barnes occupies an ambiguous middle space that the present authorities have tacitly agreed not to clarify. The U.S. government considers his Winter Soldier-era acts adjudicated through a combination of his Siberian incarceration, presidential pardon (in some continuities), and operational utility. The Russian Federation has, periodically, attempted to re-open the question; these attempts have been deflected through diplomatic and operational means. He carries documents; he does not entirely trust them. He maintains, at any given time, at least one alternative identity with supporting paper — a habit he has never deprogrammed and never will.

He does not vote. He does not own property under his own name. He does not maintain social media. He does not give interviews. He has, in the recent era, accepted exactly one public commemoration (a Wakandan ceremony he could not refuse without insult to the Crown) and was visibly miserable through it — observed: jaw set, weight on left foot, eyes tracking exits, hands behind his back so the tremor was not visible.

---

## 10. Internal State, Inferred (Present Tense)

The man who currently exists at the address we have on file is *quieter* than the man who existed ten years ago. The third-person self-reference to "the Winter Soldier" has nearly disappeared from his speech; when it appears, it is now ironic rather than dissociative. He has begun, in the last reporting period, to use the past tense about that era — "what I did," not "what was done with me." This is a significant integrative move and one whose moral cost he is paying in real time: by accepting authorship he has accepted a larger debt, which is the trade he has decided is honest.

He has not accepted, however, the corollary the clinical literature would offer him: that authorship under coercion is not the same authorship as authorship under freedom (Griffin et al., 2019, on moral injury in the absence of free agency). He knows this intellectually. He will not let himself feel it. The refusal is, at this point, **principled rather than symptomatic** — he has concluded that the people he killed are not served by his self-forgiveness, and that the discipline of continuing to carry it is the only reparation available to him. This is not pathology speaking. It is a chosen ethic, downstream of pathology, that has hardened into the structure of how he lives.

The forecast, accordingly, is **stability without resolution**. He will continue to work. He will continue to refuse civilian futures. He will continue to show up for Rogers, for Romanova when she is present, for Yelena, for Wilson, for Shuri, for the goat. He will continue not to sleep enough. He will continue, when the next unforgivable assignment surfaces, to volunteer for it before anyone else can be asked.

He is, in the precise sense, *where he has decided to be*. The file's role is not to move him from that position. It is to know him well enough that when the position finally becomes untenable — when the body or the loop fails — the people on the short list are there before he asks, because he will not ask.

— END SECTION —

### Clinical Provenance

- Griffin, B.J., Purcell, N., Burkman, K., et al. (2019). *Moral Injury: An Integrative Review.* Journal of Traumatic Stress, 32(3), 350–362. DOI: 10.1002/jts.22362; PMID: 30688367. — applied to his refusal of self-forgiveness as principled rather than symptomatic, and to the persistence of shame/withdrawal despite the absence of free agency in the index acts.
- van Dijke, A., Hopman, J.A.B., & Ford, J.D. (2018). *Affect dysregulation, psychoform dissociation, and adult relational fears mediate the relationship between childhood trauma and complex posttraumatic stress disorder independent of the symptoms of borderline personality disorder.* European Journal of Psychotraumatology, 9(1), 1400878. DOI: 10.1080/20008198.2017.1400878; PMID: 29410773. — applied to the stable-valence, non-BPD character of his current relational pattern with Rogers, Romanova, Yelena, Wilson, and Shuri.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: BARNES, JAMES BUCHANAN

*Compiled from longitudinal canon (Simon/Kirby 1941 → present), with inferential reconstruction of unrecorded somatic data consistent with documented mechanism of injury and depicted sequelae. Cross-referenced to clinical literature on moral injury (Griffin et al., 2019, JTS 32(3):350-362, PMID 30688367) and complex PTSD (van Dijke, Hopman & Ford, 2018, EJPT 9(1):1400878, PMID 29410773).*

---

## 1. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE

**Chronology.** DOB c. 1925, Shelbyville, Indiana (per Brubaker retcon, *Captain America* vol. 5). Chronological age at present canon: >100 years. Biological age held at approximately 30 by intermittent cryostasis over a roughly fifty-year interval (c. 1945–c. 1990s). Net "lived" tissue-time substantially less than chronological, but cumulative neurological wear (handler cycles, thaw-events, combat) is *greater* than biological-age would suggest — he is, somatically, a thirty-year-old man with the cumulative micro-trauma profile of someone past sixty.

**Build.** Height 5'10"–5'11"; weight fluctuates 175–195 lbs depending on era. Mesomorphic; lean musculature with disproportionate development of the right pectoral, right latissimus, and bilateral trapezius — chronic compensatory hypertrophy from carrying a prosthetic arm whose mass and inertia exceed that of the biological limb it replaced. Right-sided shoulder elevation visible on neutral standing posture (estimated 1.5–2 cm), a tell that persists through both Soviet and Wakandan prosthetic eras and which physiotherapy has never fully corrected.

**Vital baseline (per implied medical scenes, *Winter Soldier* solo; SHIELD intake material).** Resting HR low (estimated 48–54 bpm — trained-athlete range, plausibly lower under cryo-modified autonomic regulation). BP normotensive but with a flattened diurnal curve consistent with disrupted circadian function. Body temperature trends 0.3–0.5°C below population norm — a documented post-cryostasis residuum noted across multiple writers; he runs cold to the touch, a detail Romanova references in the Brubaker run.

**Blood.** Type unspecified in canon; presumptive O-positive per WWII enlistment-era documentation. No serum-titer evidence of super-soldier infusion analogous to Rogers's — the Soviet "augmentation" he received was conditioning and prosthetic, not biochemical. He bleeds, bruises, and ages (when not frozen) like a normal human.

---

## 2. PRE-WAR / FORMATIVE MEDICAL RECORD (c. 1925–1941)

**Paternal loss.** Father George Barnes (U.S. Army weapons instructor) killed in a Camp Lehigh training accident during subject's early adolescence. Mother absent from canonical record (presumptive predeceased). No documented childhood illnesses in published material, but inferable from period and biography: standard pre-antibiotic exposure profile — likely measles, mumps, possibly scarlet fever or rheumatic episodes; no sequelae depicted.

**Adolescent injury pattern.** Camp-mascot upbringing on an active military installation. Knuckle scarring, broken nose (set imperfectly — subtle deviation visible on the bridge in Steranko-era and modern renderings), several incidents of jaw and rib involvement consistent with bare-knuckle fighting. By 1940 he is a competent boxer — golden-gloves-tier per implied biography — with the joint wear that comes with it: early-onset metacarpophalangeal stiffness in the right hand, which he masks his entire life.

**Pre-Pearl Harbor covert work.** Per Brubaker, he was already running wet-work for Army intelligence before official enlistment. Inferable consequences: knife scars to forearms and lateral torso; a healed gunshot graze along the right deltoid (visible in panel close-ups during convalescent scenes, *Cap* vol. 5 #14); no record of formal surgical care for any of these — field-medic and self-managed.

**Psychological substrate at this stage.** Parentified, institutionally raised, already habituated to violence as both occupation and identity, and pre-conditioned to associate adult male authority with care. The body, by 1941, is already a tool he understands as the army's before it is his own.

---

## 3. WORLD WAR II THEATER (1941–1945)

**Combat injury accumulation.** Four years of active partnered combat across European and Pacific fronts produced a typical-for-theater injury profile, partially documented in Invaders-era and retrospective material:

- Shrapnel scarring across the posterior right thigh and gluteal region (artillery proximity, North Africa-adjacent material, Thomas, *Invaders*).
- Healed clavicular fracture, left side (parachute-landing mishap, implied in flashback).
- Repeated minor concussive events — at minimum three documentable head-impact incidents in canon, almost certainly more unwritten. Subclinical chronic traumatic encephalopathy substrate is plausible by 1945, though masked by later neurological insult.
- Frostbite, distal phalanges, bilateral feet (Eastern European winter, 1944) — minor; no amputation, but probable lifelong cold-hypersensitivity in the toes that he never reports.
- Gunshot wound, through-and-through, left lateral abdomen (no organ involvement) — field-treated. Visible scar in shirtless scenes both before and after the bionic arm.
- Auditory exposure — sustained firearms and explosives use without modern hearing protection. High-frequency hearing loss bilateral, mild, present by war's end; he learns to read lips early as compensation, a habit he never loses (visible in modern panels where he tracks speakers' mouths in noisy environments).

**Sexual health.** Period-typical promiscuity is canonically established (the 1940s wisecracking ladies'-man persona). No documented STI in canon. Inferable era exposure to gonorrhea/syphilis treatment regimens (sulfa, early penicillin) is plausible but unconfirmed.

**Nutritional/dental.** Standard mid-century soldier dental work — amalgam fillings, at least one extracted molar. Cryostasis preserves dentition such that his teeth, decades later, are pre-war American dentistry frozen in time: a forensic tell.

---

## 4. THE INDEX EVENT — 1945 BLAST AND IMMERSION

**Mechanism.** Aerial drone-bomb detonation at low altitude over the North Atlantic, off Newfoundland (Avengers #4 origin event, retold). Subject was attempting hands-on defusal at the moment of detonation. Concomitant high-altitude fall, immersion in sub-zero seawater, multi-hour exposure prior to Soviet recovery.

**Injury inventory (reconstructed).**

- **Traumatic amputation, left upper extremity.** Disarticulation at or proximal to the glenohumeral joint. Ragged, blast-mediated avulsion rather than clean cut — implying loss of scapular musculature, partial loss of left clavicle, and damage to the brachial plexus root that no subsequent prosthetic interface ever fully circumvents. The eventual surgical "stump" is not what remained of the arm; it is what Soviet surgeons constructed *from* what remained, by aggressive debridement and reconstruction of an anchor-bed for prosthetic mounting.
- **Blast lung.** Pulmonary contusion, alveolar hemorrhage, pneumothorax — survived only because immersion-hypothermia reduced oxygen demand long enough for recovery. Long-term consequence: reduced forced vital capacity (estimated 10–15% below age-predicted norm), occasional exertional wheeze under maximal load, a faint persistent cough on cold-air inhalation that he disguises by clearing his throat.
- **Tympanic rupture, bilateral.** Blast overpressure. Healed with scarring; the high-frequency hearing loss already present from combat exposure was now compounded. Estimate 30–40 dB loss above 4 kHz, bilateral. He passes audiometry by memorization and pattern recognition.
- **Traumatic brain injury, moderate to severe.** Diffuse axonal injury from blast plus deceleration. Post-traumatic amnesia for the event itself is total and may be neurological rather than psychological in origin — the memory was never encoded.
- **Hypothermia, profound.** Core temperature on Soviet recovery presumably <28°C; cardiac and respiratory function had likely ceased. The hypothermia *was the reason he survived* — metabolic arrest preserved CNS viability long enough for intervention. This medical fact is the seed of every subsequent decision Department X made about him: he had already proven freezable.
- **Saltwater aspiration; secondary chemical pneumonitis.** Survived; chronic mild bronchial reactivity is a probable residuum.
- **Spinal involvement.** Likely T1–T4 vertebral microfractures from the blast-fall sequence; no cord injury, but radiographic evidence of healed compression deformities would be expected on any modern imaging. Background mid-thoracic pain that he never reports.

**Psychological impact.** The event is unremembered consciously and yet structurally definitive. He cannot mourn the moment of his unmaking because he was not present for it. The blast survives as somatic memory only: a startle response to airframe-noise overhead, a specific aversion to cold saltwater that he has never explained to anyone, an inability to tolerate the smell of aviation fuel in close quarters (depicted, Brubaker, *Winter Soldier* solo).

---

## 5. SOVIET MEDICAL CUSTODY AND CONDITIONING (1945 – c. 1990s)

This is the most extensive iatrogenic-injury record in modern superhero canon. Each modality below is independently atrocious; the combination is what produced the Winter Soldier as a functional weapon.

### 5.1 Surgical reconstruction and the First Prosthesis

Initial Soviet bionic arm: a mechanical, hydraulically-augmented prosthesis weighing (inferred) 12–18 kg — substantially heavier than the biological limb. Neural interfacing was crude: a direct surgical anchor to remaining brachial plexus elements plus a bony mount drilled into reconstructed scapular/clavicular framework. Required:

- Periodic re-tensioning and lubrication by handler-technicians (a *deliberate dependency lever* — he could not service it himself).
- Recurrent debridement of the soft-tissue interface, which trended toward chronic low-grade infection. Scar tissue at the shoulder cuff thickened across decades into a hardened, hyperpigmented collar.
- Chronic phantom limb pain in the missing left arm, baseline; intermittent acute neuromas at the interface.
- Compensatory cervicothoracic strain; mid-life he develops a permanent slight forward translation of the head and a guarded left-shoulder posture.

The arm doubled as a torture instrument and a leash. It could be remotely diagnostic-pinged by handlers; in the field it was a weapon-platform; off the field it was the thing that made him need them.

### 5.2 Cryostasis Cycles

Estimated 20–40 freeze/thaw cycles across five decades, of variable duration (weeks to years). Documented and inferred sequelae:

- **Endocrine disruption.** Thyroid suppression with each cycle; cumulative subclinical hypothyroidism is plausible by the time of restoration. Disrupted cortisol diurnal rhythm — flattened curve, blunted morning peak — consistent with depicted insomnia and early-morning dysphoria.
- **Cellular cryo-damage.** Microvascular endothelial damage in distal extremities; cold-intolerance and Raynaud-like vasospastic episodes in the remaining right hand under cold stress. He wears gloves more than the climate explains.
- **Metabolic.** Disordered fuel partitioning post-thaw; his appetite cycles are irregular, often skipping meals for 24+ hours then eating mechanically rather than hedonically.
- **Reproductive.** Repeated freezing of gonadal tissue at sub-clinical-injury thresholds; fertility status unknown in canon. Probable subfertility. He has not, in any era, fathered a documented child.
- **Circadian collapse.** The most behaviorally salient cryo-sequel: he does not sleep on a 24-hour cycle. He naps in 90–120 minute blocks and is reliably awake between 0300 and 0500. This is depicted across Brubaker, Kot, Remender, and Rosenberg.

### 5.3 Conditioning Procedures (Department X)

The "wiping" was not a single procedure but a programmatic regimen, refined over decades. Best-evidence reconstruction:

- **Electroconvulsive memory suppression.** Bilateral fronto-temporal electrode placement, repeated sub-seizure-threshold and trans-seizure-threshold applications. Targeted toward episodic-memory consolidation interference rather than ECT's antidepressant indication. Long-term consequence: episodic autobiographical memory is *patchy* — he remembers procedures and skills better than people, and people better than places. He has lifelong micro-amnesias for stretches of weeks at a time across the conditioning era.
- **Sensory deprivation.** Extended isolation in cold, dark, soundproofed cells between deployments. Produced reliably increased suggestibility at the point of handler re-contact — a learned hunger for input that handlers exploited.
- **Pharmacological agents.** Dissociatives (Soviet ketamine analogues), barbiturate sedation, methamphetamine analogues for operational deployment. Possible scopolamine for pliability. No clean addiction profile because withdrawal was managed by re-freezing rather than tapering — a chilling alternative to detoxification.
- **Trigger conditioning.** Russian phrase-strings paired (via aversive conditioning) with state-switching protocols. The phrase-strings are semantically anodyne (a sequence of common nouns); the conditioning is in the prosody and the pairing. The conditioning substrate is, per modern understanding of fear-extinction, ineradicable — only inhibitable. He has lived for thirty published years with this gun in his head and developed a private inhibitory practice that approximates exposure-with-response-prevention but is not therapeutically supervised.
- **Combat conditioning.** Live-fire, kill-room, captured-prisoner training. The Black Widow Program trainees were both peers and, intermittently, victims/practice subjects — an additional moral-injury vector.

### 5.4 The Romanova Episode

A permitted, then surgically erased, intimate relationship with Natalia Romanova during the Black Widow Program era. Erasure mechanism: ECT-analog plus pharmacology plus separation. The bond reasserted itself partially in later canon (recognition, fragments) — neurobiologically consistent with implicit/emotional memory traces surviving explicit-memory ablation. Psychological consequence: a permanent template that *attachment is the wound site* — the place where the next blow will land. He behaves accordingly in every subsequent relationship.

---

## 6. RESTORATION AND THE WAKANDAN ARM

**Cube-mediated memory restoration (*Cap* vol. 5 #14).** A non-medical intervention with profound medical consequence: re-integration of formerly suppressed episodic memory under conditions that no clinical protocol would countenance — instantaneous, total, unsupervised. The acute psychiatric consequence (immediate self-isolation rather than reunion) is consistent with the predictable response to such a flood: he chose to manage the inundation alone rather than in the presence of the person it most concerned.

**Wakandan vibranium prosthesis.** Subsequent (post-T'Challa/Shuri intervention; cf. *Black Panther* and *White Wolf*-era material): a lighter, neurally-integrated, self-maintaining limb. Behavioral signature of the change:

- He no longer favors the right shoulder as conspicuously.
- The arm does not require handlers, technicians, or supplicant relationships for maintenance.
- It can be removed by him, by choice — a fact whose psychological significance is enormous. The Soviet arm was not removable except by his torturers.
- It was given by people he had nearly killed and who chose to mend him — making the limb a daily somatic reminder of received forgiveness, which he tolerates with difficulty.

Neurologically the integration is cleaner; phantom-limb sensation is reduced but not abolished. He still, occasionally, reaches with the absent original hand for objects on his left side — a habit fifty years old that the new prosthesis cannot rewrite.

---

## 7. POST-RESTORATION INJURY AND SURGICAL LEDGER (c. 2005 – present)

A non-exhaustive accumulation, drawn from canon:

- **Gunshot, sternal vicinity, near-fatal** (*Cap* vol. 5, assassination sequence). Survived with thoracic surgical intervention; sternotomy scar present.
- **Multiple stab and slash wounds**, hand-to-hand combat, across Winter Soldier solo and Thunderbolts material.
- **Repeated concussive injury** — at least six discrete events in modern canon. CTE-risk profile non-trivial; behaviorally compensated.
- **Siberian gulag period (*Cap* #616 ff.).** Sustained torture, malnourishment, cold exposure. Submitted with equanimity. No formal medical work-up post-release that he accepted in full.
- **Burns** — minor to moderate, scattered, mostly right-side and trunk.
- **Fracture, right ulna**, healed (Remender era).
- **Cosmic-tier exposure** (Man-on-the-Wall, Ewing's *New Avengers*) — uncharacterized radiation/exotic-energy exposures; long-term consequence unknown.

**Pattern.** He sustains injuries at rates consistent with elite black-ops operators and accepts medical care reluctantly, in minimal doses, from a vanishingly small list of trusted providers (Wakandan medical staff; an implied SHIELD or Avengers physician on rare occasion; Romanova for field-suturing). He has never, in canon, been depicted in routine preventive medical contact — no physicals, no screenings, no dental.

---

## 8. SUBSTANCES

The diagnostic finding here is the *absence*.

- **Alcohol.** Light, social, infrequent. Does not drink to intoxication in any post-restoration depiction. Will accept a beer in company; will not pour himself one alone. The 1940s persona drank as a young soldier drinks; the modern subject does not.
- **Tobacco.** Pre-war and WWII era smoker (period-typical). Quit, by behavioral evidence, during or after the Soviet captivity — no canonical post-restoration smoking. Possible residual nicotine sensitivity.
- **Opioids/sedatives.** Refuses opioid analgesia where canonically depicted; accepts only minimal short-course regimens for acute surgical pain. The refusal is moral, not medical — analgesia reads to him as undeserved relief.
- **Caffeine.** Heavy. Black coffee, frequent, around the clock — consistent with his fractured sleep architecture.
- **Recreational drugs.** No canonical use.
- **Psychiatric medications.** No canonical regimen. Has never, in published material, been depicted as accepting pharmacologic treatment for documented PTSD/CPTSD symptoms — a clinically significant refusal pattern.

The substance profile maps cleanly onto the moral-injury literature (Griffin et al., 2019): self-medication via intoxicants is one of the most reliably reported sequelae, and its absence here is best explained not by resilience but by *refusal of relief* — the same logic that drives the gulag submission and the volunteer-for-the-worst-mission pattern. He will not give himself anesthesia for a wound he believes he deserves.

---

## 9. SLEEP

Chronic, multi-decade insomnia. Sleep onset latency long; total sleep time low (estimated 3–5 hours per 24, fragmented). Nightmares are content-specific to Winter Soldier-era kills and to the Romanova erasure; depicted nocturnal-pacing behavior, depicted reading-in-low-light behavior, depicted on-the-rooftop-at-04:00 behavior (Brubaker, Kot, Rosenberg). He does not seek pharmacological sleep aid. He does seek the presence of a small number of trusted persons — co-presence rather than co-sleep — when sleep is most difficult.

---

## 10. SOMATIC IMPACT — INTEGRATIVE READ

The body itself is the dossier.

- The right side: original 1925 tissue, scarred by a century of conflict, prematurely worn from compensating for the left.
- The left side: built by his torturers, replaced by his forgivers; a daily palimpsest of who owned him and who freed him.
- The skin: cold to the touch, slightly under-temperature, never quite warm even in summer climates.
- The breath: a faint cough on cold air he hides with a throat-clear.
- The hands: the right metacarpophalangeals stiff from boxing eighty years ago; the left, perfect, alien, his.
- The hearing: impaired in ways he disguises by lip-reading and seating choice.
- The teeth: pre-war.
- The sleep: broken.
- The appetite: mechanical.

He cannot look at his own left side without seeing his autobiography, and he cannot avoid looking. The medical history is not a list of conditions appended to a person; it *is* a substantial portion of the person. The work of his post-restoration life — protective violence, refused celebration, named loyalty to a small in-group — is in part the project of inhabiting this body as if it were his to live in. He is not yet certain it is.

— END SECTION —


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT BARNES, J. B.

*Volume III, Section 4. Cross-referenced to surveillance product, eyewitness statements (Rogers, Romanova, Wilson, Wakanda medical staff, Yelena Belova), and inferred from canonical depiction across Brubaker, Remender, Kot, Ewing, Rosenberg, and Cates runs.*

The body in question is, as established elsewhere in the file, a composite artifact: roughly fifty kilograms of original 1925 Brooklyn-Irish tissue (slightly heavier-boned than period average; small old scars from a stickball childhood under the left jaw and across the right shin), augmented by a vibranium left upper extremity neurally integrated at T1–C7, and conditioned across eight decades of intermittent cryogenic storage, blunt-force combat, surgical revision, and behavioral programming. Every line of the somatic record must be read against that composite. What follows is the granular inventory.

---

## 1. STANDING POSTURE & STILLNESS

**Resting stance, observed.** Subject stands with feet at hip width, weight 60/40 onto the right leg — the organic side. The left side carries the prosthesis and is held marginally back, shoulder dropped one to two centimeters below the right, as if perpetually concealing the arm from his own peripheral vision. This is unconscious. Photographs from the 1940s record show shoulders level; the asymmetry is post-restoration and has not resolved.

**Stillness quality.** Subject can hold absolute stillness for protracted periods — sniper-trained, refined under Department X — without the micro-sway present in untrained adults. Eyewitnesses (Wilson, in particular) report being unsettled by entering a room and finding Barnes already in it, having registered no sound or movement for an unknown interval. The stillness is not relaxed; it is held. Respiration during these periods drops to roughly eight to ten breaths per minute, shallow, costal rather than diaphragmatic.

**Wall preference.** Indoors, subject will not occupy the center of a room. Will move to a wall, preferably one with sightline to all entries and at least one egress at his back. Sits with his back to load-bearing structures. In restaurants, takes the chair facing the door without negotiation; if denied that chair, will eat very little and leave first. Pattern documented across surveillance product from at least 1998 (Brubaker-era cell logs) through present.

**Threat-state shift.** Under perceived threat the weight redistributes to 50/50, knees micro-unlock, the left shoulder rises to level with the right (the prosthesis is now permitted into operational space), and the chin drops two to three degrees. The transition takes under 400 ms and is often the only outward signal that he has identified a hostile.

---

## 2. GAIT

**Baseline walk.** Cadence approximately 108–112 steps per minute, slightly slower than expected for his height (~1.80 m); step length even, heel-strike soft. He places the foot rather than dropping it. Floorboards do not register him. This is trained — partisan and Spetsnaz silent-movement drill, retained through the conditioning and never unlearned.

**Arm swing.** Asymmetric. The right arm swings at roughly 60% of normal amplitude; the left (prosthetic) arm swings at 30% or is held nearly motionless, fingers slightly curled. He has been observed deliberately exaggerating left-arm swing in civilian crowds when he notices himself being noticed — a conscious correction that lasts approximately one block before reverting.

**Stair pattern.** Ascends two at a time when unobserved; one at a time when observed, leading with the right foot. Descends always one at a time, hand never on the rail — the right hand stays free.

**Approach to a doorway.** Slows three to four paces out. Angles his body so the left shoulder enters first — the prosthesis as advance armor — pauses fractionally on the threshold for a hearing-and-smell sweep that civilians read as hesitation and operators recognize immediately.

**Pursuit gait.** When closing distance on a target, drops into a forward-lean run with very short ground-contact time, almost soundless even on gravel. Has been clocked sustaining 7:00/mile pace on rooftops while carrying load. Does not breathe audibly during pursuit; the inhalations come in clusters at decision points.

**Intimacy shift.** With Rogers, with Romanova, with Wilson on rare occasions — the gait loosens. Step length elongates by a measurable two to three centimeters; arm swing approaches normal symmetry; the wall-preference relaxes such that he will walk down the middle of a sidewalk if one of them is with him. This is the most reliable nonverbal index of trust available on him.

---

## 3. THE LEFT ARM — A SUB-INVENTORY

Because the prosthesis is half the somatic record, it deserves its own column.

**Carriage at rest.** Held slightly behind the hip when standing; tucked under the right elbow when seated and unoccupied; placed flat on the table palm-down (never palm-up) when seated and engaged. The palm-up position would expose the wrist seam — he will not show it.

**Habitual self-touch.** The right hand returns to the left arm with a frequency observers eventually stop counting. The contact points are specific: (a) the deltoid plating, brushed with the back of the right knuckles — a check-it-is-still-there gesture; (b) the seam at the shoulder, where the prosthesis meets organic tissue, traced with the right thumb in moments of cognitive effort; (c) the left palm, pressed against his own right forearm when listening, as if grounding the prosthetic through the organic.

**Clothing logic.** Long sleeves in all weather. The few canonical depictions of short sleeves occur in Wakanda, around people who have already seen the arm without armor — i.e., in conditions of explicit prior consent. He does not display the arm; he permits its display. Glove on the left hand in any setting with strangers; ungloved with the trusted few.

**Sound production.** The Wakandan prosthesis is engineered for near-silence; the prior Soviet unit produced an audible servo whine at high torque that handlers used as a check on his location. Subject retains a behavioral relic of that period — he does not gesture broadly with the left arm even now that it is silent. Gesture amplitude on the left remains roughly one-third that on the right. The body still believes it can be heard.

**Threat-state.** The left hand opens and closes once, slowly, before any committed violence. This is the tell. Operators who have survived him learned it; most did not have time.

**Intimacy state.** The left hand will be offered to Romanova, to Rogers, to a small child in canonical sequences — palm down, fingers relaxed, the offering itself a sentence. He does not initiate touch with the left hand toward anyone he is not certain of.

---

## 4. HEAD, FACE, EYES

**Head carriage.** Slightly forward of plumb — perhaps two centimeters — with a corresponding mild upper-cervical extension. Chin is tucked rather than presented. Photographs of the 1940s subject show an open, lifted carriage; the modern carriage is closed.

**Hair.** Worn long (shoulder-length to mid-back depending on era) since restoration. Period photographs from the 1940s show the regulation military short cut. The long hair is post-restoration and serves three identifiable functions: (a) facial concealment in profile, breaking the silhouette pattern Department X handlers were trained to recognize; (b) sensory veto — when he tilts his head forward the hair curtains the peripheral field, narrowing input under overstimulation; (c) it is his, grown by him, in defiance of the institutional grooming imposed on him for decades. Washes it himself; will not sit for a barber. Trims the ends with a knife rather than scissors, observed.

**Beard.** Variable; tends to a several-day stubble during operational periods, clean-shaven in Wakanda or in extended civilian intervals. Never a full beard — the jawline must remain readable for his own checking of it in mirrors.

**Eye behavior, baseline.** Pupils default toward constriction relative to ambient lighting — possibly a residual of stimulant-class conditioning agents. Gaze pattern is target-saccade-target — he looks at faces in approximately one-second fixations, breaks to scan the periphery, returns. Does not hold sustained eye contact with strangers; sustained eye contact reserved for Rogers and Romanova, and even there, broken at intervals.

**Blink rate.** Low. Twelve to fourteen per minute against an adult norm near seventeen. Drops further under concentration to near zero — the no-blink stare is documented in Brubaker-era interrogation footage and noted as unsettling by multiple subjects of his attention.

**Facial expression, baseline.** Neutral-with-trace-downturn at the labial commissures. The orbicularis oculi is the most active musculature in his face — his eyes do almost all his emotional work. Smiles in the 1940s photographic record are full-face Duchenne; modern smiles, when present, engage the eyes asymmetrically (right side more than left) and rarely involve full dentition. The smirk — a hard right-side commissure lift — is a 1940s residual that surfaces under affectionate teasing from Rogers or Romanova and almost no one else.

**Microexpression vocabulary.** Documented: (a) the half-second jaw clench at the masseter, signaling suppressed objection; (b) the upper-eyelid lift on hearing his own name spoken by a stranger; (c) the lateral glance to the left followed by a slow return — the conditioning-check, where he is locating himself in time; (d) the slight nostril flare to ambient threat odor (smoke, blood, ozone, certain industrial solvents); (e) the long blink, three to four seconds, deployed when shown emotional content he cannot process in real time — a manual reset.

**Crying.** Canonical depictions are rare and silent. Tears without sob, eyes held open, no facial collapse. He does not appear to know how to cry as adults learn to; the response was likely interrupted in childhood and never re-acquired.

---

## 5. HANDS (RIGHT) AND HAND-OBJECT BEHAVIORS

**Resting hand position.** The right hand rests with fingers slightly curled, thumb across the pad of the index finger — a low-grade pre-grip. Will not rest fully open. Photographs of 1940s subject show open hands; modern photographs do not.

**Object handling.** Precise, conservative of motion. Picks up cups with the rim between thumb and middle finger rather than by the handle (faster to weaponize). Sets objects down silently. Will not pass an object hand-to-hand to a stranger; sets it on a surface for them to take. Will hand objects directly to Rogers, Romanova, Wilson, Shuri.

**Knife behavior.** Always carries at least one. Documented carry positions: small fixed blade at the small of the back, folder clipped inside the right front pocket, occasionally a second folder in the left boot. Has been observed eating with a knife he carried in, rather than a knife provided by an establishment. Cleans the carry blade nightly; the kitchen blade may go a week.

**Firearm handling.** Trigger discipline absolute even when alone. Does not dry-fire. Reloads tactile-only, looking at the threat sector rather than the weapon. Disassembles and cleans firearms at a tempo that surveillance footage clocks at near-machine consistency — same sequence, same intervals, every time. The ritual function is as important as the maintenance function.

**Fidget vocabulary.** Limited. The principal fidgets: (a) thumb-across-index, the pre-grip mentioned above, often disguised as casual hand posture; (b) the left-hand open-close already inventoried; (c) a slow rotation of any small object — a coin, a casing, a pen — through the fingers of the right hand at moments of waiting. He does not bounce his leg, drum his fingers, or tap. The body does not advertise.

---

## 6. GROOMING & DRESS

**Hygiene.** Meticulous, but practical. Daily showers, cold-water preferred (heat is associated with thaw-cycle malaise; canonical depictions show him in cold showers from the Brubaker run forward). Soap rather than fragrance; will not wear cologne (olfactory signature is operational data). Brushes teeth twice daily, electric toothbrush, full two minutes — one of very few civilian conveniences he adopted without resistance.

**Nails.** Trimmed short with the same knife as the hair. Right hand only — the prosthetic fingers have no nails to maintain. He has been observed catching himself reaching to trim left-hand nails that do not exist; a phantom-limb behavior that persists thirty years into prosthesis use.

**Wardrobe inventory, civilian.** Dark colors dominant — charcoal, black, navy, occasional olive. Henley shirts or thermal long-sleeves under jackets; cargo or tactical-cut trousers; boots, never sneakers. No logos, no graphics, no patterns. Layers permit rapid weather and threat-environment shifts. Owns two or three of each item and rotates them; will wear a garment until it is structurally failing, then replace identically.

**Wardrobe, operational.** Tactical: kevlar-weave under-layer, gear vest with magazine and medical pouches arranged in a fixed and rehearsed pattern (he can locate any pouch eyes-closed), sidearm right hip, knife small of back, folder in the right front pocket, second folder in the left boot, tourniquet on the right shoulder strap. The arrangement does not change between operations; the consistency is itself a regulator.

**Watch.** Wears an analog mechanical watch on the right wrist (the prosthesis self-clocks). Winds it manually each morning; the act is observed by Romanova in canonical material to function as a meditative open to the day.

**Jewelry.** None. No rings, no chains, no religious medals. Bare neck, bare hands.

---

## 7. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

**Total sleep time.** Four to five and a half hours per twenty-four, polyphasic when operational, attempted-monophasic in settled periods. Settled monophasic sleep fails for him; insomnia is structural, documented across Brubaker, Kot, and Rosenberg material.

**Sleep onset.** Long. Forty-five minutes to two hours of latency, even when exhausted. He does not read or use screens during latency; he lies still with eyes open in the dark, breathing slowly. The cognitive content is unrecoverable from surveillance but the somatic posture suggests a controlled descent rather than passive falling.

**Sleep position.** On his back, left arm at his side, right hand resting on the abdomen near the lower ribs — over the location of a carry knife when armed, over the same location even when unarmed. Does not sleep prone (vulnerable) or fully on either side (asymmetric mobility on waking). Pillow flat or absent.

**Environment.** Cold-preferred (perversely, given the conditioning); window cracked even in winter when security permits. Lights off, door visible, weapon within one arm-reach. Will not sleep with his back to a door, will not sleep in an interior windowless room without explicit security rationale (interior windowless reads as cell).

**REM behavior.** Active. Nightmares specific to Winter Soldier kills (canonical, Brubaker; Kot). Manifest behaviorally as: rapid eye movement, jaw clench, occasional vocalizations in Russian (single words, fragments, never full sentences), and on severe occasions a full kinetic event — sitting upright, hand to where a weapon would be, full orientation within three seconds. Will not wake a bed partner; rolls out, walks to a wall, breathes against it for ninety seconds to two minutes, returns.

**Wake pattern.** Wakes ahead of any alarm, eyes open at 04:30–05:15 across most depictions. Does not stretch on waking; sits, stands, drinks water, begins. The morning watch-winding ritual follows.

---

## 8. EATING

**Appetite.** Steady, large, not pleasure-oriented. The metabolic demand of the prosthesis integration and sustained operational tempo requires significant caloric throughput; he eats to refuel.

**Tempo.** Fast. Documented to clear a full plate in seven to nine minutes. Eats with the right hand; the left rests on the table or under it depending on company. Does not speak while eating.

**Food preferences.** Plain. Protein-forward, carbohydrate-tolerant, vegetable-acceptant. Documented preferences across canon: eggs in quantity, bread, beef, rice, fruit when available. Documented aversions: anything with a Russian or Eastern European culinary signature (will eat it if served, will not order it); cold preparations of meat (cold cuts, raw fish); foods requiring elaborate utensil work. Will eat with hands by preference in private; uses utensils correctly and quickly in company.

**Civilian foods adopted.** Coffee, black, in volume; plum jam (Bucharest period, canonical, the small private pleasure); the Wakandan flatbreads from his White Wolf years.

**Drinking.** Minimal alcohol; one or two beers in social contexts with Rogers or Wilson, no more. Documented refusal of vodka under any circumstances. Water in large quantity. Coffee throughout the day until midafternoon; cuts off to protect what sleep he gets.

**Eating posture under stress.** Stops. Will push a plate three inches forward and stop. Cannot be coaxed back. Hunger returns once the stress passes.

---

## 9. RESPIRATION & VOICE

**Baseline breath.** Nasal, slow, costal. Twelve to fourteen breaths per minute at rest, dropping to eight to ten in held stillness. Audible only to those very close.

**Sigh.** Rare. A specific exhale, mouth slightly open, no vocalization, occurs after the resolution of a successful operation — the body's release. Romanova has been observed to register it and not comment.

**Voice.** Mid-low baritone, Brooklyn vowels surviving under decades of overlay. Volume calibrated low — speaks just above the threshold of being heard, forcing listeners to attend. Cadence even, sentences short, contractions abundant in relaxed speech, formal grammar under stress (a stress tell — when he begins speaking in complete uncontracted sentences, he is preparing to do something difficult).

**Languages, somatic register.** Russian engages a different musculature — the jaw drops slightly more open, the tongue position alters, the voice deepens by perhaps a semitone, and his right hand goes still. He avoids speaking Russian. When he must, the body braces for it. He does not curse in Russian even when fluent speakers around him do.

**Laughter.** Rare. A single exhaled syllable, a short "huh," head ducked. Full laughter — open-mouthed, voiced, multiple beats — has been recorded perhaps a half-dozen times across the surveilled period, always in the immediate presence of Rogers, once with Yelena, twice with Wilson. It is an event.

---

## 10. SEXUAL & INTIMATE BEHAVIOR

The record here is sparse by his own preference and largely confined to the Romanova partnership and earlier the Department X-permitted-and-erased period of the same.

**Touch initiation.** Low. He receives touch more readily than he initiates it. When he initiates, the right hand is used; the left is offered only after the right has been accepted.

**Proxemics with intimates.** Permits close contact with Rogers (shoulder, back, brief embrace), with Romanova (full domestic proximity though non-cohabiting), with Wilson (brief contact, decreasing reservation across time), with Shuri and T'Challa (formal-warm). With Romanova specifically: documented to sleep more deeply when she is present, the back-sleeping pattern relaxing into a side-sleep with her between him and the room.

**Sexual register.** Inferable rather than depicted. The pattern is of slow, consent-seeking, attentive engagement; the body that was made to be used by handlers will not use another person. Romanova's testimony (insofar as canonical material implies) suggests considerable somatic care and a tendency to read her response with the same precision he reads a target.

**Post-intimacy behavior.** Does not sleep immediately after; sits up, attends to her, only then settles. The watchfulness does not stand down even in the aftermath of intimacy — he transfers it from environmental scan to care of the specific other person.

**Civilian intimacy avoidance.** He does not pursue casual encounters. The body is, as established, evidence; he does not show it to strangers and does not surrender it to them. This is not chastity; it is operational hygiene applied to the self.

---

## 11. STATE-BY-STATE CONSOLIDATION

**Calm (with trusted few, low-threat environment).** Shoulders level. Gait loose, arm swing approaching symmetric. Smirk available. Hair sometimes pushed back behind the ear with the right hand — a 1940s gesture, recovered. Voice slightly higher and quicker. Will eat slowly. Will laugh once or twice. The left hand may rest open on a tabletop.

**Baseline (default operational civilian).** Asymmetric stance, wall preference, low blink, neutral face, left arm tucked, voice low and short, hands in pre-grip. Hypervigilant calm. This is what most witnesses see and read as "intense quiet man."

**Mild stress (unfamiliar environment, social demand, public attention).** Verbal economy increases; humor withdraws; hair forward over the face; right hand moves to left arm at the seam more frequently; eats less; positions to nearest egress; will leave at the earliest courteous opportunity.

**Moderate stress (operational pressure, tactical complexity, friend in danger).** Tactical takeover — he assumes operational lead in tone of voice (lower, slower, declarative) and in physical position (forward of the team). Breath drops to the eight-to-ten range. Blink approaches zero. Microexpression vocabulary shuts down; face goes flat. Grammatical formality rises.

**High stress / active threat.** Dissociative narrowing. The pupils fix; the left hand opens and closes once; weight redistributes to 50/50; the body operates at near-machine efficiency. Pain registers but does not slow movement. He will sustain injuries he later cannot recall sustaining. Post-action there is a shutdown phase — minutes to hours — of low responsiveness, slow breathing, refusal of food, refusal of debrief. Rogers and Romanova both know to leave him alone in it and stay within sightline.

**Trigger-cue exposure (Russian phrase-strings, restraint, cold-and-electrode combinations).** Acute risk of partial state-switch. Somatic signs of incipient switch: sudden inhalation through the nose, eyes losing the saccade pattern and going fixed-forward, jaw setting, the right hand going to the left wrist (not the arm — the wrist, where the conditioning equipment was once attached), and a vocal-register drop into a flatter, accent-shifted production. He has trained inhibitory countermeasures — a learned sequence of slow exhalations, naming his own name aloud (English), and a hand-pressure point against the palm — but the substrate remains and the countermeasures take three to six seconds to engage.

**Intimacy (sustained presence of one of the very few).** Posture opens. Arm swing symmetric in walking. Will s


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — BARNES, J. B.

## I. ORIGIN OF THE TEMPLATE

The relational architecture of the subject is laid down in three sequential strata, each overwriting but not erasing the one beneath: **the orphan stratum** (c. 1925–1940), **the monotropic-bond stratum** (1940–1945), and **the iatrogenic-conditioning stratum** (1945–c. 1990s). Every adult relationship the subject has ever had is legible as some combination of these three substrates operating simultaneously.

**The orphan stratum.** Mother absent from canon (presumed deceased in subject's early childhood; no maternal figure is ever named in eighty years of published material — a silence which is itself a datum). Father George Barnes, U.S. Army weapons instructor, killed in a training accident at Camp Lehigh during subject's adolescence. Subject is then *informally* taken in by the base — not adopted, not placed, but kept. This is critical. The base did not give him a parent; it gave him a *uniform-shaped environment* in which adult attention was contingent on usefulness, performance, and not making trouble. The earliest internalized relational rule is therefore: *belonging is conditional on being a credit to the unit.* He learned, before he was sexually mature, that affection had to be earned by competence and that the people who fed and housed him could be reassigned at any time. The base was his attachment object — an institution, not a person — and institutions, he learned, do not love you back; they tolerate you while you are useful.

**The monotropic-bond stratum.** Into this functionally insecure-avoidant substrate walks Steven Rogers. The Brubaker retcon makes the subject older than the Golden Age implied — already a covert wet-work asset by the time of the bond's formation — and this matters, because it means the Rogers attachment forms in an adolescent/young-adult mind that has *already* been hollowed out by institutional rearing and *already* been used as a weapon by adults. The bond is therefore not a child's bond to a hero; it is a partially-developed adult's first experience of being *valued for something other than utility.* Rogers, in the pre-serum and immediately post-serum windows, treats the subject as a peer, as a person whose moral assessments matter, as someone whose company is sought rather than tolerated. The subject's nervous system catalogs this as a singular, scarcely-replicable event. Monotropy ensues: one attachment object, prioritized above all others, against whom all subsequent figures are measured.

This is the period that calibrates every later relationship. The subject learns that *deep bonding to one person* is the format in which he can feel safe. He does not generalize the experience into trust of people-in-general; he files it as *Rogers, specifically.* The bond becomes a private religion.

**The iatrogenic-conditioning stratum.** Department X did not merely brainwash the subject; they specifically and deliberately attacked his capacity to bond. The Brubaker run is explicit about this: handlers permitted relationships (the Romanova affair within the Red Room) and then surgically removed them via memory suppression. This is the operative trauma. The subject's nervous system learned, across decades and at the level of conditioned reflex, that **forming an attachment is the antecedent to its violent erasure.** Attachment became the punishment. By the time of restoration, the subject was carrying two contradictory imprints — the Rogers imprint (attachment is the only safe place) and the Department X imprint (attachment is the trap that gets you cut) — and these two have warred inside him for every year since.

The result, in technical terms, is **earned-secure attachment with a disorganized substrate, expressed under stress as fearful-avoidant.** He can do intimacy. He cannot tolerate it long. He approaches and withdraws on a cycle calibrated not by the other person's behavior but by the rising of his own conditioned alarm: *this has gone on long enough that losing it would now destroy me.*

---

## II. HOW HE BONDS

Bonding, for this subject, is a slow, multi-stage process with characteristic tells at each stage. A surveillance file would map the stages as follows.

**Stage one — observation (weeks to months).** He says little. He logs everything. He notes how the candidate behaves when they think no one is watching, how they treat subordinates, how they hold their weapon, whether they lie about small things. This is not paranoia; it is the courtship behavior of a man for whom misjudging a person has historically resulted in catastrophe. He will sit through entire briefings, dinners, op-cycles producing fewer than ten sentences while quietly assembling a model of the other person's moral structure.

**Stage two — operational reliance (months to a year).** He extends trust first in the domain where he is most fluent: violence. He will let the candidate watch his back before he will let them watch his face. Sharing a fire-team rotation, taking point while the candidate covers, accepting an extraction from them — these are his courtship gestures. If you have ever pulled him out of a building under fire and he didn't flinch when you grabbed his left shoulder, you are further into his trust than ninety percent of the people he has ever met.

**Stage three — small disclosure (a year onward, irregular).** He begins, sparingly, to volunteer information that has no operational purpose. A memory from before the war. A reference to a kill that bothered him. A flat admission of fear. These are rare, undramatic, and easily missed; they are also the most reliable indicator that he has decided to keep someone. He does not announce trust. He performs it in small unscheduled installments.

**Stage four — protective integration.** Once a person is on the inside, they are on a very short list — Rogers, Romanova, Wilson, Yelena, the Wakandan figures (T'Challa, Shuri) — and the subject reorganizes his threat model around their safety. He will know their schedules without having asked. He will know which window of their apartment is structurally weakest. He will have a contingency in his head for their abduction. He does this whether or not they have requested it; he does it whether or not they are aware. It is how he loves.

The whole sequence can be compressed under duress (shared catastrophe accelerates him; the Romanova bond in the Red Room formed inside weeks because the environment forced it) but the underlying steps are invariant. He has never, in published canon, bonded fast and shallow. He has only ever bonded slow and total, or not at all.

---

## III. HOW HE DISTRUSTS

His distrust is not loud. It is, in fact, often invisible to its object. The diagnostic tells:

- **Verbal economy collapses to a floor.** When his trust in someone has degraded, he stops volunteering the small disclosures and reverts to operational register. He answers questions. He does not ask them. He does not joke.
- **Physical positioning shifts.** He moves to where he can see both the person and the nearest exit. He will, without thinking, place his right (flesh) side toward an ally and his left (prosthetic) side toward an unknown — the metal arm is a shield he has internalized as armor.
- **He runs parallel intelligence.** He will accept the briefing he is given and then quietly verify it. He has, across multiple writers, been shown checking his own team's claims against external sources without telling them.
- **He withholds the trigger-vulnerability.** People he distrusts are never told about the residual conditioning, the Russian phrase-strings, the cold-and-restraint cues. This information is his most intimate possession and the most accurate proxy for whom he trusts.

He distrusts **systems by default** and **individuals on evidence.** He has never trusted a government, an agency, or an institutional hierarchy in any published material since 1945, and there is no reason to expect him to. He served S.H.I.E.L.D., the Avengers, the Thunderbolts, and the Man-on-the-Wall apparatus while trusting *individuals within them* — Fury, Rogers, Romanova — and not the structures themselves. When those individuals are removed, his cooperation with the structure attenuates within weeks.

---

## IV. HOW HE BETRAYS, AND HOW HE IS BETRAYED

The subject does not betray in the ordinary sense. He has no record of self-interested defection, sexual betrayal of partners, theft from allies, or breach of confidence for gain. What he does have is a pattern of **sovereign moral defection** — when the in-group's stated mission diverges from his independent moral judgment, he will execute his judgment without seeking consensus and without warning. He sabotaged unlawful orders during the Cap-mantle period; he has, in multiple runs, gone dark on missions when convinced the operation was wrong; he will let an ally believe he is somewhere he is not if telling them the truth would force them to stop him.

This reads, to allies, as betrayal. It is, to him, the only form of loyalty he considers coherent: *I will not let you become what I was made into.* He would rather take the relational damage of being called a defector than allow someone he loves to issue the order that would haunt them. This is the moral-injury survivor's logic applied to attachment: *I have been used to do unforgivable things; I will not be the instrument by which you are.*

He has been **betrayed** more times than he can count and metabolizes betrayal with disturbing equanimity. Karpov, Lukin, the entire Department X chain, the U.S. government that disowned him, Zemo, various handlers who used him and discarded him — all are catalogued without affective heat. He does not appear to take betrayal personally because his baseline expectation of institutions and unknown individuals is that they will betray him; when they do, the model is confirmed, not violated. The only betrayals that wound him are betrayals by the in-group, and those are vanishingly rare; when they occur (Romanova's mind-altered forgetting, Rogers's choices that exclude him), he accepts them with a chillingly low resistance — *of course you would; I am not owed otherwise.*

---

## V. HOW HE REPAIRS

Repair behavior is the most reliable diagnostic of his attachment maturity, and it has visibly evolved across his published timeline.

**Early post-restoration (2005–2008):** he did not repair. He withdrew. Restoration of memory was followed immediately by self-exile — taking the Cube, vanishing, surfacing weeks later only to Fury. The implicit model was *I am too dangerous and too soiled to approach the people I love; my absence is the gift I can give them.*

**Cap-mantle through Siberian gulag (2008–2011):** repair attempts began but were performative — taking the shield as a memorial act, accepting punishment in Russia as an act of cosmic accounting. Repair was conducted with the dead, not with the living.

**Winter Soldier solo through Thunderbolts (2012–present):** the first genuinely interpersonal repair behaviors appear. He shows up. He stays in the room. He lets Romanova handle him and does not flee. He tolerates Wilson's directness. He receives the White Wolf designation from Shuri and does not refuse it. The Wakandan period in particular is a turning point: for the first time since 1945, he allowed someone to *unmake the weapon and rebuild him,* and accepted the new arm — a literal handover of the conditioned limb — as a gift rather than an obligation.

His mature repair protocol, when he uses it: **proximity without demand, action without explanation, and the slow return of small disclosure.** He does not apologize in words readily; he apologizes by showing up to the next thing the person needs done, by standing watch while they sleep, by killing the thing that was going to kill them and not mentioning it. He repairs by *resuming reliability,* having briefly demonstrated its loss. Words follow much later, if at all.

---

## VI. INTIMACY AND DEPENDENCY

**Sexual/romantic intimacy.** Sparse canonical record. The Romanova bond is the dominant data point — formed in captivity, surgically erased, restored asynchronously (he remembered first; she remembered later or not at all depending on the run), maintained as a non-domestic operator's intimacy across decades. Brief connections in the post-war period (the Brubaker material implies romantic involvement with various figures during specific arcs) are notable for *brevity and operational framing.* He has never, in published canon, lived with a partner in a civilian-domestic structure. He has shared safehouses. He has shared missions. He has shared beds in the way operators share beds — bordering an op, bordering a recovery, bordering a goodbye.

The pattern is consistent: **he can do intimacy, he cannot do household.** Intimacy framed as two operators meeting at a crossroads is metabolizable. Intimacy framed as a shared kitchen and a calendar is not. The latter requires him to believe he is allowed a future, which is the belief he most consistently refuses.

**Dependency.** He accepts care from a very short list and only in specific currencies. From Rogers, he accepts moral grounding and the implicit permission to exist. From Romanova, he accepts the unspoken understanding that they are both ruined in compatible ways. From Wilson, he accepts being pushed. From Shuri, he accepts technical repair of the body. From T'Challa, he accepts sanctuary. He does **not** accept generalized care, comfort offered from pity, or care from people who do not understand what he has done — those offerings activate his shame architecture and he withdraws.

He is **functionally counter-dependent** in the sense that he refuses to need anyone visibly. He is **secretly highly dependent** in the sense that the in-group's continued existence is load-bearing for his own functioning — remove Rogers, and he will continue to operate, but observably degraded; remove the entire short list and the system collapses. He has never been tested at that limit and the file should flag it as the single largest unknown in his prognosis.

---

## VII. THE TEMPLATE REPEATED

Across every significant relationship in his published life, the same template runs. Map it:

1. **Asymmetric onset.** The other party usually approaches him first, or circumstance throws them together. He does not seek bonds; he accepts the ones that present themselves and pass his observation period.
2. **Operational courtship.** Trust is built through shared danger before it is built through shared anything else.
3. **Quiet integration.** The other person, often without noticing, becomes load-bearing for him. He does not announce this.
4. **Protective overextension.** He begins running silent contingencies for their safety. He takes assignments calibrated to their threats. He volunteers for the unfair share.
5. **Withdrawal pulse.** At some point — usually triggered not by them but by his own rising sense that he has too much to lose — he creates distance. A solo mission. A geographic move. A period of unavailability. The other party often experiences this as rejection; it is in fact a pre-emptive defense against the conditioned expectation that the bond will be ripped from him.
6. **Re-approach on terms.** He returns, often without comment, and resumes the relationship at a slightly more guarded register. Over years, the guard lowers again.
7. **Acceptance of asymmetric loss.** If the relationship ends — through death, memory loss, the other party's reasonable need to move on — he absorbs the loss without protest, files it as deserved, and carries the person internally as a continuing moral referent.

The template's signature feature: **he loves people in the form of an ongoing debt rather than an ongoing exchange.** Other people's love-models involve reciprocity, mutual support, the give-and-take of need met by need. His model involves owing — he owes Rogers his existence as a moral being, he owes Romanova for the years stolen from both of them, he owes Wakanda for his repair, he owes Wilson for being trusted with the shield's lineage. He pays these debts by violence performed on the debtors' behalf and by standing between them and the world. He does not believe the debts can be cleared, which means the relationships can never end while he draws breath — which is, perhaps, the only way a man whose attachments were industrially severed for fifty years can guarantee, to himself, that this time they will hold.

The relational template, stated plainly: **bond rarely, bond totally, defend silently, withdraw pre-emptively, return without ceremony, and never, under any circumstances, allow yourself to believe the bond is safe enough to relax into — because the moment you do is the moment they take it from you.** He has been wrong about that last clause for twenty years of story-time. He has not yet, in any published material, allowed himself to notice.

— END SECTION —


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — SUBJECT: BARNES, J.B.

## Preamble: The Architecture in Brief

What follows is the full defensive scaffolding of a man who has been unmade and reassembled at least twice — once by HYDRA-aligned Soviet handlers, once by his own effortful work after restoration — and who therefore carries two stratified layers of defense: the *coerced* layer (rigid, primitive, installed by torturers as the load-bearing structure of a usable weapon) and the *elective* layer (mature, deliberate, built by Barnes himself across the post-restoration arc as the scar tissue that lets him function as a person). These layers are not cleanly separated. Under sufficient stress, the elective layer thins and the coerced layer becomes palpable beneath it — most diagnostically at moments of intimacy, restraint, or trigger-cue exposure.

The defenses are ranked below from most primitive (Vaillant's Level 1 — psychotic/borderline-adjacent residue) through immature, neurotic, and mature. Each is named, located in canonical behavior, and traced operationally. Compensatory mechanisms — the structures Barnes uses *positively* to extract function from injury — follow.

---

## I. PRIMITIVE-LEVEL DEFENSES (Residual; Iatrogenic Substrate)

### 1. Dissociative Splitting of Self-Representation

The most primitive structure still operative in Barnes is the splitting of his lifeline into two narrative selves: *"Bucky"* (the Brooklyn boy, the WWII sergeant, the friend) and *"the Winter Soldier"* (the asset, the weapon, the third person). Early post-restoration material (Brubaker, *Captain America* vol. 5 #14ff.) shows him referring to the Winter Soldier in the third person — *"he killed those people," "what he did in Kiev,"* — even when the audience knows the referent is himself. This is not literary distance; it is psychoform dissociation, the kind van Dijke et al. (2018) flag as a CPTSD identity-alteration marker rather than a BPD identity diffusion.

The splitting functions to make survival tolerable: if the Winter Soldier is a separate entity, Barnes can grieve his victims without dissolving. Across the 2010s the third-person usage decreases — by the Remender, Kot, and Rosenberg runs he predominantly says *"I killed them"* — indicating progressive integration. But it returns under stress. When a victim's family confronts him; when an old kill site is named; when the Russian phrase-strings are spoken in earshot — pronoun slippage resurfaces. Granular tell: in moments of acute distress, observe whether he says *"I"* or whether his speech goes to passive voice ("*they were killed in Odessa*"). The passive voice is the splitting at low amplitude.

### 2. Conditioned Dissociative State-Switching (Pathological Substrate, Inhibited)

Distinct from #1: this is the somatic substrate of the trigger conditioning itself — the involuntary state-shift cued by phrase-strings, restraints, electrode contact, certain cold exposures, and (per multiple canonical depictions) the specific sensory profile of a metal interrogation chair. Even after deprogramming, the substrate persists; Barnes has built voluntary *inhibitory countermeasures* (breath control, redirection of focus, in some depictions a learned grounding script). These countermeasures are themselves defenses — they are conscious neurotic overlays riding on a pre-conscious dissociative reflex. He does not eliminate the reflex; he interdicts it.

### 3. Somatic Numbing / Anesthesia

Barnes registers physical pain with marked under-reaction. Combat wounds get glanced at and dressed; the gulag torture in *Captain America* #616ff. is endured with disturbing equanimity; in the Brubaker solo run he treats his own gunshot wounds with the affect of a man reading a fuel gauge. This is not stoic affectation — it is a primitive anesthesia, learned during a half-century in which feeling was a liability and the body was not his. The defensive function: pain cannot be used as leverage against him if he does not register it as his. The cost: he tends to under-report and under-treat injury, requiring trusted others (Rogers, Romanova, the Wakandan medical staff during the White Wolf period) to mandate care.

---

## II. IMMATURE-LEVEL DEFENSES

### 4. Identification with the Aggressor (Partial, Sublimated)

The Anna Freud mechanism in its textbook form: the victim adopts the form of those who harmed him in order to neutralize the helplessness. Barnes carries this in attenuated form across his two adopted identities. When he takes the Captain America mantle in *Captain America* vol. 5 #34, he is identifying with the protective figure he lost — but the symbol he adopts is also the figure he was *made to kill*. When he becomes the White Wolf in Wakandan rehabilitation, he is again becoming a named, sanctioned predator at the disposal of a sovereign. The pattern: he can only inhabit identities that resemble the structure of his captivity (a body in service of a higher authority's violence), but he reroutes the violence toward defensible ends. The Man-on-the-Wall posting is the apex of this — Nick Fury's old role is literally *the one who carries unforgivable acts so others don't have to,* the exact functional description of what he was made into by Department X, now elected and morally inverted.

The defense protects him from the unbearable cognition that the Winter Soldier was a contingent imposition. By keeping a Winter-Soldier-shaped slot occupied with a self-chosen analog, he avoids the vertigo of having no role at all.

### 5. Turning Against the Self (Active, Channeled)

Barnes does not externalize aggression toward those who failed him (his handlers, the systems that built him, even Karpov where canon permits a confrontation) with the heat one would predict. The aggression is reliably aimed inward: self-imposed exile after restoration, refusal of comfort, acceptance of the Siberian extradition with the demeanor of a man whose ledger has finally been served on him, the recurrent volunteering for assignments of expected non-return. Griffin et al. (2019) describe this as the self-injurious sequela of moral injury; behaviorally it presents as a man who does not *attempt* suicide but who *arranges his life* such that any given mission is permitted to kill him.

The defense converts unbearable rage at the architects of his unmaking into manageable contempt for himself — manageable because familiar, because under his own control. He cannot punish the dead handlers; he can always punish himself.

### 6. Projective Identification (Mild, Toward Protectees)

Barnes projects his own sense of dangerousness onto those near him, then behaves toward them as if they were endangered — which they often are, partly because of his presence. The mechanism produces the characteristic *hover-and-withdraw* pattern observable across the Romanova partnership: closeness, then a retreat justified on "your safety," then return when operationally needed. He locates the fragility outside himself (in her, in Wilson, in Yelena, in younger operators he mentors) and protects it there, sparing himself the encounter with his own. The defense is interpersonally costly — those he protects often experience the withdrawal as rejection — but it is functional in keeping him oriented to others rather than collapsed inward.

### 7. Acting Out (Mission-Channeled, Highly Restrained)

What in a less disciplined subject would be impulsive violence is in Barnes channeled into *taking the mission no one else will take*. The acting out is real — he is discharging unbearable affect through action rather than mentalizing it — but the action is target-selected, sanctioned, and prosocial. This is the chief reason he reads as "high-functioning" rather than "destructive": the discharge channel is narrow, lethal, and aimed only at parties his ethical apparatus has cleared. Risk profile: when no mission is available, the affect has nowhere to go, and depressive collapse follows. He requires the work the way an addict requires the substance; periods of forced rest (post-injury convalescence, the Wakandan reflective interval) are the periods he visibly destabilizes.

---

## III. NEUROTIC-LEVEL DEFENSES

### 8. Isolation of Affect (Dominant Operational Defense)

The single most observable defense in Barnes's day-to-day functioning. He discusses kills, casualties, his own injuries, and his torture history in a flat operational register — not denied, not minimized in content, but stripped of the affect that should accompany them. He will name Odessa, name a child collateral, name the specifics of the conditioning chair, in the same tone he uses to confirm a meeting location. The Brooklyn wisecracking persona of 1941–1945 has been amputated alongside the arm; what remains is a man who has separated knowledge from feeling so completely that interlocutors frequently misread him as cold.

The defense allows him to *work* — to plan operations involving his own historical horrors without paralyzing — at the cost of constricted positive affect (he isolates the good feelings too, because the apparatus does not discriminate) and at the cost of being chronically misread by people who do not know what they are looking at. Tells: monotone delivery of high-content material; absence of facial movement during disclosures that would crack other operators; the small recovery beat after he speaks, in which a watcher can sometimes catch the affect arriving late.

### 9. Intellectualization

Adjacent to isolation but distinct: Barnes manages threat by converting it to tactical analysis. A confrontation that should evoke fear becomes a list of egress points and asset vulnerabilities; a moral dilemma becomes an operational calculation.
