- **The breath release on entering a safe space** — a single audible exhale on crossing the threshold of a place he has decided to trust. Tiny. Other operators recognize it.
- **The half-second look at Rogers before any decision of moral weight.** He does it even when Rogers is not in the room — the look goes to where Rogers would be. The superego proxy made visible.
- **The pre-sleep weapons check** that he has stopped doing consciously and now does as a hand-pat sequ


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS — SUBJECT: BARNES, J. B.

*Compiled from longitudinal observation; week-of-surveillance reconstruction cross-referenced against published depictions across Brubaker, Remender, Kot, Ewing, Rosenberg, and Cates runs. Granular detail inferred from established behavioral substrate.*

---

## 1. THE ARCHITECTURE OF A DAY

Subject does not keep a schedule in the civilian sense; he keeps a **standing order of operations**, executed with the same rigor whether deployed, in safehouse, or in extended downtime. The structure is military-residual overlaid with the procedural compulsions of a recovering captive: a man who learned in Department X that unstructured time was either a deprivation tactic or a prelude to a wipe, and who therefore organizes his hours so that no minute is ever fully empty.

A representative weekday, observed:

**03:40–04:20 — First waking.** Subject does not sleep through the night and has not been observed to do so on any uninterrupted week of surveillance. The first waking is the *cold waking* — sudden, full alertness, no transitional drowsiness, head turning toward the door before the eyes are fully open. Bedding is invariably thrown off the left side of the body during sleep; the prosthetic shoulder rotates outward at rest. He does not return to bed immediately. He sits at the edge of the mattress, forearms on knees, for between forty seconds and four minutes — duration correlates inversely with how recent the last operational deployment was — then rises.

**04:20–05:00 — Perimeter check, dressed in whatever he slept in (typically charcoal henley, dark sweatpants, barefoot or sock-footed on cold floor). Even in a Wakandan compound with an active vibranium-mesh security envelope, even in a Brooklyn walk-up with a single deadbolt, he walks the room, then the adjacent rooms, then the egress points. He looks at the same four things in the same order: window latches, door hinges, sightlines through curtains, his weapon cache. The cache is never more than three steps from any sleeping position.

**05:00–05:45 — Conditioning.** Calisthenics-based, equipment-light, repeatable in any environment: push variants weighted toward right-arm symmetry compensation (left arm overpowers; he deliberately under-loads it), pull-ups from a doorframe or branch, weighted core work, a long static hold series (planks, wall-sits) that reads less like fitness and more like *practiced endurance of discomfort.* He does not use music. He does not count aloud. He counts in Russian when stressed and in English when not — one of the few diagnostic tells a watcher can pull from him without his knowledge.

**05:45–06:15 — Shower; black coffee; first contact with the outside world.** Shower is brief, water hot but not scalding (cold-water aversion, conditioned). He stands with the left shoulder turned away from the showerhead for the first thirty seconds — *unconscious shielding of the seam* even when alone. Coffee preparation is ritualized: pour-over, ground that morning, no sugar, no dairy. The repetition of a small precise daily act with a known outcome is, in itself, the point. He drinks the first cup standing at a window with the curtain pulled to a six-inch gap, watching the street.

**06:15–08:00 — Reading and correspondence.** Newspapers (physical when obtainable; he distrusts the algorithmic skew of feeds), three of them, read in a fixed order: local, national, foreign (typically a Russian-language paper, read partly to maintain language fluency and partly as ongoing self-exposure therapy — he refuses to let the language become only the trigger). Reading posture: chair angled to face the door, back to a wall, paper folded into quarters in the right hand. He underlines names with a pencil; the underlining is reflex, a residual intelligence-analyst tic from both his Army and his Department X periods.

**08:00–12:00 — Work, variable.** When operational: mission prep, target study, equipment maintenance, comms. When non-operational: a *constructed* work block — gym time at a serious boxing gym in whichever city he's in (he has been observed cycling through the same three or four working-class gyms in Brooklyn over years; he tips the desk in cash; he learns one name per visit and uses it), maintenance contracts (he has, in multiple depictions, done unglamorous trade work — building super, garage mechanic — under thin identities, because the labor regulates him and the anonymity comforts him), or training a younger operator if one is available and willing.

**12:00–12:30 — Lunch.** Eaten standing or walking roughly half the time. When seated, seated facing the door. Eats fast — Depression-era / wartime-feeding-window habit that the seventy-year intermission did nothing to undo. Preference for foods that travel: sandwiches, hand pies, dumplings from whatever cart is nearest, the occasional indulgence in Eastern European cuisine that he eats with a complicated expression no observer has ever seen him acknowledge.

**12:30–17:00 — Second work block.** Same structure as morning, lower intensity. This is when he handles the *life-administration* he cannot avoid: paperwork laundered through Fury or Wilson's networks, banking through cutouts, the small clerical residue of legally existing again. He hates this block. He does it because it must be done.

**17:00–18:30 — The walk.** Subject takes a long walk almost every day he is in a fixed location. Route varies — he does not repeat — but the *parameters* are fixed: minimum forty minutes, residential rather than commercial, hands out of pockets, gait at a pace just slightly below his natural one (he deliberately throttles down to look like a man and not a predator, and he is aware that this is what he is doing). He notices children. He notices children with the specific attentiveness of a man who is glad they are alive and quietly certain he should not be allowed too close to them.

**18:30–20:00 — Evening meal; if in-group present, the only sustained social block of the day.** If alone, eats simply, often standing again. If with Rogers, Romanova, Wilson, or others on the short list, sits, lingers, drinks one beer or one whiskey *very* slowly — alcohol intake calibrated downward to a degree that suggests he does not trust himself unguarded.

**20:00–22:30 — Downtime, so-called.** Reading (history, biography, occasionally fiction — strong preference for nineteenth- and early-twentieth-century material, the period he was *born into* before the seam in his life); rebuilding small mechanical objects (radios, watches, the recurrent motif of taking things apart and putting them back together correctly); writing in a notebook (see §5).

**22:30–23:30 — Pre-sleep ritual.** Final perimeter check. Lights down. Weapon placement confirmed. He lies on his back with the right arm across his chest and the left arm extended along the side of the body — the prosthetic posture, as if even in sleep it is set apart.

**23:30–03:40 — Sleep, fragmented.** Total sleep typically four to five hours, broken into one or two segments. He has been depicted across multiple writers waking to nightmares specific to Winter Soldier kills; the waking is silent — no cry-out, no thrash — just opened eyes and an immediate sit-up. He does not rise from these intermediate wakings. He waits them out, often with one hand pressed flat to the seam at his left shoulder.

---

## 2. HABITS OF PLACE

Subject's relationship to *place* is unlike either a civilian's or a normal operator's. He treats every interior as a temporary OP and every neighborhood as a slowly assembled informant network.

**The safehouse pattern.** Whether in a Brooklyn apartment, a Wakandan guest residence, or a borrowed room in an Avengers facility, he configures the space identically within forty-eight hours:

- Furniture moved off any wall that backs onto an exterior or shared partition; sleeping position never within line-of-fire from a window.
- One chair positioned to face the door; that chair becomes the chair he uses.
- A go-bag — clothes, cash in three currencies, two passports, a knife, a sidearm with two magazines, a satellite phone, a basic medical kit including tourniquet and quikclot — sits within reach of the door, packed, indefinitely. He repacks it monthly. He has done this every month for approximately fifteen years of continuous canonical depiction.
- Windows: curtains never fully open, never fully closed. The six-inch gap.
- Mirrors: minimal. He does not avoid them but he does not install them. The shaving mirror is small.
- No photographs on display. This is not from a lack of attachment; it is from a refusal to provide leverage to anyone who enters in his absence.

**The Brooklyn pattern, specifically.** When in his home borough — a recurring depiction across the Brubaker and post-Brubaker material — he gravitates to the older neighborhoods, the ones whose street geometry he learned as a teenager and whose synagogues, churches, and bodegas still occupy approximately the same lots. He has been observed standing in front of buildings that no longer exist *as he remembers them* and visibly recalibrating. He does not visit his childhood home; he visits its block.

**The Wakandan pattern.** Different posture entirely. In Wakanda — White Wolf era — the perimeter rituals attenuate; the chair-facing-door habit relaxes by a few degrees; he sleeps slightly longer. This is the only environment in which his body genuinely de-escalates, and it is almost certainly because Shuri's neural work on the arm has, in a deep somatic register, restored his sense that his own left side belongs to him.

**The travel pattern.** Hotels: never a high floor (lateral egress preferred to elevator dependency), never above the seventh, never below the third. Rental cars: chosen for unremarkability, inspected underneath before first use. Airports: he flies commercial when he can, dressed deliberately drab — dark zip-up jacket over henley, work pants, ballcap, a leather glove on the left hand or a long sleeve and a thumb tucked. He has learned exactly how to look like the kind of veteran TSA's pattern-matching writes off.

---

## 3. HABITS OF THE BODY

**The arm.** Subject's relationship to the prosthetic is a daily ritual in itself. Morning: he flexes through a full range of motion, slowly, checking for any anomaly. Evening: cleans the seam — the skin around the integration point — with attention that exceeds basic hygiene and edges into the territory of *tending a wound that has long since healed.* In the Soviet-era prosthesis depictions, this maintenance was forced dependency; in the Wakandan-era depictions, it is voluntary self-care, and the difference in his face when he does it is the difference between a man cleaning a leash and a man oiling a tool that is his.

**Hair.** Length varies by era but the pattern of *touching it* is constant. Tucks it behind the right ear when reading. Pulls it forward when he wants to disappear. Cuts it himself, in front of the small shaving mirror, with surgical scissors, when he wants to feel like he has made a decision no one else gets to make.

**Hands.** The right hand fidgets — a coin, a lighter (he does not smoke; the lighter is the object), the corner of a notebook, the rim of a cup. The left hand does not fidget. The left hand is held still, almost performatively still, as if he is reassuring everyone present, including himself, that it is not about to do anything.

**Eyes.** Constant scan pattern in any new environment: door, exits, hands of every person present, then faces. In a familiar environment he does not run the scan but his pupils still track movement through windows.

**Voice.** Quiet baseline volume. He has learned that lowering his voice forces people to come closer, and he prefers to control proximity. Accent is essentially neutral mid-century New York, audible chiefly in certain vowels and in the way he says *coffee*. Under stress the accent thins. Under trigger-state exposure, the accent disappears entirely and the speech-rate slows — a near-diagnostic indicator.

**Sleep posture.** Supine, never prone (prone replicates restraint posture from conditioning). One pillow. Light blanket regardless of temperature; the cryostasis history left him with a strong aversion to heavy coverings on the chest.

---

## 4. RITUALS, IN THE PROPER SENSE

These are the small repeated acts that are not strictly functional and that therefore carry meaning.

**The coffee.** First cup of the day, at the window, six-inch curtain gap. He does not drink it for the caffeine; he drinks it for the proof that he has chosen what he will put in his body today.

**The pencil-underlining.** Names in newspapers. He does not act on most of them. The underlining is an *acknowledgment*: I saw this person existed; I noted them; I am not the man I was, who would have been given this name as a tasking.

**The notebook.** Small, cheap, replaceable, kept in an inside jacket pocket. He writes in it in a hybrid of English and Russian — Russian for the things he does not yet trust himself to think in his own first language. Entries are short. Names. Dates. Occasionally a sentence. He has burned at least one full notebook on camera in the Brubaker run; he keeps doing this — write, carry, destroy — as a private liturgy of *I was here, I bore witness, I did not let the record fall into other hands.*

**The visit.** On a roughly monthly cadence, when feasible, he goes alone to a place associated with a Winter Soldier-era kill and stands there for a measured interval. He does not pray; he is not, in any depicted era, observantly religious. He stands. He leaves. The act is the act.

**The call.** Rogers, when Rogers is alive and reachable. The call is short, factual, content-light, and unmistakably the most important communication of his week. He ends the call first, always. Ending first is a control reflex; that he applies it even to Rogers, the one person he trusts unconditionally, is itself the diagnosis.

**The cooking, rare.** When in extended contact with the in-group — particularly with Romanova or in shared Avengers quarters — he occasionally cooks something Eastern European, badly, from memory rather than recipe. He is not embarrassed by the badness. The cooking is a way of touching a part of his history that was *given* to him rather than imposed — the kitchen-language he picked up in safehouses between operations, the foods Romanova half-remembered. It is one of the few uncomplicatedly affectionate things he does.

**The shield, when he held it.** During the Captain America period, the daily ritual of cleaning the shield was depicted as protracted and meticulous beyond functional need. He was not maintaining equipment; he was tending a relic that belonged to someone else and that he was permitted, conditionally, to carry.

---

## 5. WORK PATTERNS

**On-mission.** Subject is, by every depicted account, the most operationally disciplined member of any team he joins. He sleeps less, eats less, complains never. He runs reconnaissance well in advance of an op and re-runs it the night before. He prefers small teams (two to four), prefers night, prefers cold-weather environments not because he likes them but because his physiology — recalibrated by decades of cryostasis and Siberian conditioning — outperforms most operators' there. He is the one who volunteers for the extraction position no one else wants. He is the one who stays back to cover withdrawal. The pattern is unmistakable and unchanging across writers: *if there is a slot in the op that has a meaningful chance of not coming home, he takes it before anyone else can.*

**Post-mission.** A measurable shutdown window — six to eighteen hours — during which he is functionally non-verbal, eats little, sits in a chair facing the door, and processes. Allies who know him do not push during this window. Romanova, in particular, has been depicted simply occupying the same room without speaking, which is sufficient. After the window, normal function returns. The kills enter the nightmare rotation roughly two to three weeks later, never immediately.

**Off-mission.** The constructed work block (§1). He cannot tolerate true idleness. Forced leave — a vacation, a stand-down — produces visible deterioration within seventy-two hours: sleep worsens, perimeter rituals intensify, irritability rises. He does better with *a job, any job* than with rest. This is not a virtue; it is a symptom he has learned to channel.

---

## 6. SOCIAL CADENCE

A week of surveillance would record approximately the following contact pattern:

- **Daily:** zero to two civilian interactions of substance (cashier, neighbor, gym desk attendant), each kept under ninety seconds, each conducted with practiced courtesy.
- **Two to four times a week:** sustained contact with one member of the in-group, in person or by call. The composition rotates; Rogers and Romanova receive disproportionate share.
- **Once a week, on average:** training session with a junior operator (Yelena, when she is in his orbit; others, when assigned).
- **Once every two to three weeks:** a meal in a group of three to five trusted persons, almost always at a private residence rather than a restaurant.
- **Once a month or less:** any form of public appearance, ceremony, or institutional event. He attends when refusing would be insulting to the in-group and not otherwise.
- **Never observed:** dating in the conventional sense; party attendance; social media presence under any identity; participation in any organized civilian recreational activity (no league, no club, no class).

His relational economy is small and dense. The signal-to-noise ratio of his social life is extraordinarily high; almost no contact is incidental. He has, in effect, designed a life in which every person he speaks to more than once is someone he has decided to speak to more than once.

---

## 7. WHAT A WEEK OF SURVEILLANCE WOULD ACTUALLY SHOW

Compressed: a man who wakes before any reasonable hour, walks his perimeter, makes one cup of coffee with great care, reads three newspapers and underlines names, trains his body hard enough to keep it useful, does some form of unobtrusive labor, walks a long irregular route through a residential neighborhood at dusk, eats quickly, sees almost no one, sleeps badly, wakes from a dream he does not describe, lies still until the heart-rate drops, and gets up again before the sun.

A man who has built, out of the wreckage of seventy years of someone else's schedule, a daily order so consistent that *he is the only one keeping watch over himself* — and who has done so because, on the deepest behavioral register accessible to observation, he has decided that this watch is owed, that it is his to keep, and that he will not be relieved of it.

— END SECTION —


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Dossier Section 6a. Subject: BARNES, James Buchanan. Cross-referenced to Simon/Kirby 1941 origin material, Brubaker* Captain America *vol. 5 (2005–2012), Remender's Invaders/Cap material, Ewing's* New Avengers*, and contemporary Rosenberg/Cates runs. The "family" set, for an orphan made twice over — once by accident, once by industrial design — must be read broadly. Blood family is short; chosen family that occupies the structural slot of blood family is longer. This section covers the dead, the absent, and the kin-by-installation: the people whose names organize his interior architecture whether or not they are alive to know it.*

---

## 6a.1 — GEORGE M. BARNES (FATHER, DEC. c.1930s)

**Status.** Deceased, approximately three decades before subject's own first "death." Sergeant, U.S. Army; small-arms and demolitions instructor at Camp Lehigh, Virginia. Killed in a training-ground accident — the canonical accounts vary (live-fire ordnance, grenade malfunction) but consistently place the death on a military installation, during instruction, in front of recruits, with the body recoverable but disfigured. Subject was an adolescent at the time and on or near the base.

**History.** The relationship is, by the time of the published record, almost entirely a constellation of absences and small relics. What can be reconstructed from the Brubaker retcon and the 1941 Simon/Kirby framing is that George Barnes was the kind of NCO who taught his son's friends how to disassemble a Springfield before puberty — a man who treated competence with weapons as a transferable inheritance and a moral object both. The subject's earliest body-knowledge — grip pressure on a stock, breath control on a trigger pull, the ritual of cleaning and oiling — is paternal. He learned to be lethal from the man whose lethality killed him.

**Dynamics.** Imitative and aspirational, with a substrate of fear about the trade itself that he has never been heard to articulate. The father appears in the published interior monologue rarely and obliquely; when he is invoked it is via *practice* rather than memory — the way the subject still field-strips a weapon left-handed-first (a habit pre-dating the prosthesis), the way he addresses senior officers with a verbal cadence that other characters have noticed as old-fashioned. There is no canonical scene of grief about George. There is also no canonical scene of disavowal. The father is held as a procedural ghost.

**Trust / safety baseline.** Foundational. The father is the substrate on which the entire later attachment apparatus is built: a man who was both the disciplinarian and the only source of warmth in a household stripped of the mother (variably depicted as absent, dead in childbirth, or out of frame). The trust-template Barnes carries — *the male authority who teaches you to kill is the male authority who loves you* — originates here and is the reason the Steve Rogers attachment seated so fast and so deep. Rogers is, structurally, the father reissued in a body that does not die in front of him.

**Evolution.** Static, because there is no living party to evolve with. The father's grip on the interior has not loosened in eighty years; it has been overwritten and re-instantiated in successive figures (Rogers; briefly the Army intelligence handlers who recruited the pre-war wet-work asset; perversely, then Karpov; later, in a different valence, T'Challa). Each subsequent paternal-coded figure has been read against the George template.

**Failure mode.** The death wrote a rule the subject has not been able to revoke: *competence with weapons does not protect the competent.* This is the root of the fatalism that surfaces in every "don't come for me" statement across his post-restoration record. He does not believe skill confers survival; he believes survival is something that happens to you by accident, and that the appropriate response is to use the borrowed time to be useful.

**Leverage.** Negligible directly — no one alive remembers George Barnes well enough to weaponize him. Indirectly, considerable: anything that frames the subject's violence as a continuation of his father's vocation reaches him at a level below argument. Conversely, any frame that positions him as having *betrayed* the father's craft — having let the weapon be turned against the innocent — produces shame response of unusual depth.

---

## 6a.2 — WINIFRED / "THE MOTHER" (DEC., DATE UNCERTAIN)

**Status.** Deceased before the published record begins. The name is given variably across the canon and the figure is, functionally, a structuring absence rather than a remembered person. Cause of death not consistently established; childbirth and early illness are the dominant variants.

**History.** The subject has no working autobiographical memory of his mother and has never, across eight decades of published material, been depicted speaking about her at length. What exists is the absence-shape: a household run by a father and a small son, an institutional adolescence on a military base after the father's death, and a specific kind of comfort-seeking — the latching onto older male figures — that reads as a child compensating for the missing first attachment by overinvesting in the second.

**Dynamics.** Null in the direct register; foundational in the negative. The mother's absence is the reason the father's death was catastrophic rather than survivable; a two-parent household loses one and reorganizes around the survivor, but a one-parent household loses one and dissolves. The subject went from a home to a barracks because there was no maternal household to receive him.

**Trust / safety baseline.** The early loss of (or never having known) a maternal figure shows up across his adult relational pattern as a specific gap: he does not seek female caretaking, he does not eroticize rescue by women, and he does not have a comfort-figure of the type that men with intact early maternal bonds typically retain. Romanova, Sharon Carter, Yelena, Shuri — none of them occupy that slot for him. With women he trusts, he relates *operationally and laterally*, as peer, partner, or younger sibling. He does not have a learned posture of being held.

**Evolution.** The absence has deepened rather than healed. Each successive trauma layer — the fall, the conditioning, the restoration — has been processed inside an attachment apparatus that has no maternal channel to run distress through. This is part of why the post-restoration self-soothing repertoire is so thin: there is no internalized maternal voice to call on, only the father's procedural one and Rogers's moral one.

**Failure mode.** The gap manifests as an inability to receive *unconditional* care. Care offered with a job attached he can accept; care offered as care he flinches from. The Wakandan rehabilitation took as well as it did partly because it was framed as work — goats, language acquisition, a community role — rather than as nurture.

**Leverage.** None available. The figure is too thin in his interior for anyone to grip.

---

## 6a.3 — REBECCA "BECCA" BARNES PROCTOR (SISTER)

**Status.** Younger sister. Alive in the published record well past the subject's presumed 1945 death; outlived him in the sense that mattered, growing up, marrying, having children and grandchildren, aging into her nineties while he was frozen at thirty in a Soviet vault. Reunion sequence established in the Brubaker run after restoration.

**History.** The sole surviving member of the original Barnes household. In the pre-war material she is the younger one — the child the subject was, in effect, co-parenting in late adolescence after the father's death and before enlistment. The institutional childhood on the base was hers too, but mitigated by his presence as elder-sibling-as-substitute-parent. He left her, in a real sense, twice: first when he shipped out, and second when he failed to come home.

**Dynamics.** When restored and confronted with the fact of her survival and decline — she is depicted as elderly, ill, lucid — his response is the most undefended he is shown to have across the entire post-restoration record. He visits. He sits with her. He does not perform competence; he does not deflect. With Becca he is, briefly, *the brother*, and the regression into that identity is observable as a softening of posture, a shedding of the operator's verbal economy, a willingness to be looked at without flinching. She is the only person alive who saw him before the war who is not also the war itself (Rogers, by then, having become inseparable from the soldier-identity).

**Trust / safety baseline.** Absolute, and uniquely uncontaminated. Becca is the only living human who knew him before he had killed anyone for either flag. With her there is no debt; she is not owed atonement, she is owed *presence*, and presence he can manage.

**Evolution.** Limited by her age and the brevity of the reunion window. The relationship in the published record is elegiac from the moment it resumes — a closing, not an opening. There is no version of the future in which they grow old together; she is already old and he cannot age. What evolved is his permission to himself to claim, briefly, the role of brother in addition to the role of soldier.

**Failure mode.** Her decline and death (canonically pending or accomplished depending on which era of the run is being referenced) takes from him the last witness to his pre-violence self. Without her, the testimonial proof that he was once an ordinary young man with an ordinary sister evaporates, and the self-narrative that he is *only* the weapon gains ground unopposed.

**Leverage.** Extreme, and historically exploitable: any threat to Becca or her descendants would override all mission considerations. He has descendants-in-law and grand-nieces and grand-nephews scattered through the American Northeast; the file maintains their addresses; he checks on them at intervals that do not reach the threshold of contact but do reach the threshold of *knowing they are alive this week*. He drives past houses. He does not knock.

---

## 6a.4 — STEVEN G. ROGERS (BROTHER-IN-ARMS, ATTACHMENT FIGURE OF RECORD)

**Status.** Living, present, recurrently lost-and-returned. Cross-listed in 6b (Chosen Family) but indexed here because Rogers occupies the structural slot of *kin* — specifically the conflated slot of father, brother, and conscience — more completely than any blood relation.

**History.** Met in adolescence per the modern continuity (childhood friends in the more recent retellings; introduced at Camp Lehigh in the original). The relationship predates the war, predates the serum, predates Captain America as a public object. The subject knew the small, sick, stubborn boy before the symbol existed and has never fully updated the internal image; he relates, when alone with Rogers, to that boy with a larger body attached. This is the substrate of the famous deference: he obeys Captain America in public because that is the show, and he protects Steve Rogers in private because that is the truth.

**Dynamics.** The single most overdetermined relationship in his interior. Functions simultaneously as: (a) reissued father figure — the male authority whose approval organizes behavior; (b) brother — the peer with whom roughhousing, in-jokes, and shared history operate; (c) externalized superego — the *what would Steve do* operator that he runs as a moral subroutine even in Rogers's absence; (d) survivor-guilt anchor — the person for whom he died and who therefore owns the residue of his life by lien; (e) secure base — the one figure whose presence reliably down-regulates his hypervigilance, observable across multiple writers as a postural change when Rogers enters a room.

**Trust / safety baseline.** Maximal, with one structural exception: he does not trust Rogers to allow him to be punished as he believes he deserves. He has therefore arranged his post-restoration life so that the most punitive decisions (Siberian extradition, Man-on-the-Wall, high-lethality solo assignments) are made before Rogers can intervene, and communicated after rather than before. *He trusts Rogers with his life and not with his sentence.*

**Evolution.** Across eighty years of published material, the relationship has cycled through: pre-war partnership (peer, slightly older-brother-coded on the subject's side, given Rogers's pre-serum frailty); wartime partnership (deferential public, autonomous field, balanced private); the seventy-year amputation (Rogers as ghost the subject did not know he was haunting, Rogers as memory the subject did not have access to); post-restoration reluctant resumption (Rogers actively pursuing, subject actively withdrawing); mantle-inheritance interval after Rogers's assassination (the subject literally wearing the symbolic body of the lost figure, an enactment of identification so complete it borders on incorporation); the present steady-state, in which Rogers and the subject operate as adult peers who have buried each other and been buried by each other and arrived at a wary, durable, often wordless mutuality.

**Failure mode.** The bond is so load-bearing that any threat to Rogers triggers complete suspension of every other operational consideration including self-preservation. This is the known vulnerability and has been exploited by hostile parties on multiple occasions. The inverse failure mode is subtler: when Rogers attempts to give the subject something the subject believes he has not earned (forgiveness, retirement, civilian life), the gift cannot be accepted and produces withdrawal rather than reception. Rogers's love is the one input the subject's internal accounting cannot reconcile.

**Leverage.** Highest of any relationship in the file. Threats to Rogers are absolute movers. Promises *from* Rogers — particularly framed as "what I would want of you" — are the only social mechanism reliably capable of moving the subject into roles he would otherwise refuse (the Cap mantle; team leadership; in at least one documented case, sustained therapy). Sharon Carter and Fury demonstrated the technique on the mantle question and it has been used since.

---

## 6a.5 — SARAH ROGERS (MOTHER-OF-FRIEND, INTERNALIZED MATERNAL FIGURE)

**Status.** Deceased in subject's adolescence/early adulthood per the more recent continuity that establishes a long pre-war friendship with Rogers and a household-overlap with Sarah Rogers in her last illness.

**History.** Where Winifred Barnes is a structuring absence, Sarah Rogers is — in the retconned-deeper continuity — the closest thing to a present maternal figure in the subject's record. He was in and out of the Rogers household during her decline; he helped with rent, with groceries, with the small dignities of a poor tubercular woman raising a sickly son in a Brooklyn walkup. He attended the funeral. He brought Rogers home with him after.

**Dynamics.** Quasi-maternal in the residual sense — she was *somebody's* mother who treated him with the warmth she would have given any of her son's friends, and the small dose of that warmth lodged. He has not been heard to invoke her, but his behavior toward Rogers has, at points of Rogers's distress, an unmistakable quality of *what she would have done with him*: the hand on the back of the neck, the silent sitting-with, the not-fussing.

**Trust / safety baseline.** Historical only. She is, like George, a relic.

**Failure mode.** Minimal. The figure was too brief in his life to install vulnerabilities of her own; what she contributed was a single demonstration that maternal warmth was *real* in the world even if not available to him personally.

**Leverage.** Negligible to outsiders. Significant to Rogers, which makes it indirectly significant to the subject — any cruelty to the memory of Sarah Rogers in Rogers's presence would put the subject in the room as defender, with all the operational consequences that entails.

---

## 6a.6 — THE DEAD HE KILLED (THE ANTI-FAMILY)

**Status.** Deceased. Numbering in at least the high two figures of confirmed Winter Soldier assassinations, with a long tail of suspected and uncounted. Indexed in this section, anomalously, because the published record establishes that the subject holds these dead with a fidelity and granularity normally reserved for family.

**History.** The ledger is canonical. He keeps it — initially literally, in notebooks (depicted across multiple runs), later in a more dispersed memory-system as integration progressed. Names where he has them; dates; locations; what he was told at the time about why; what he later learned about why. He has, on at least one documented occasion, traveled to the graves of his kills, and on more than one occasion sought out and protected their surviving family without revealing his identity.

**Dynamics.** This is the central perversity of the post-restoration interior: the people he killed have, in his moral accounting, the status of dependents. He owes them. He cannot give them anything they would want — they want to be alive, and he cannot do that — so he gives them what he can: he remembers; he protects what they would have protected; he does not allow himself to be comforted out of the obligation.

**Trust / safety baseline.** Not applicable in the usual sense, but operationally: the dead are the most reliable element of his interior. They do not change their minds about him. They do not forgive him and then later un-forgive him; they do not extend warmth he has to negotiate; they simply remain dead, owed, and uncomplaining. There is a *restfulness* in his relationship to the dead that he does not find anywhere among the living, and this is a clinical warning sign — the preference for the company of the un-demanding dead is the substrate of the high-lethality volunteer pattern.

**Evolution.** From third-person dissociated distance (early post-restoration, when he referred to the Winter Soldier as a separate entity who did these things) toward first-person ownership (the integrated 2010s posture: *I killed them; I was not myself; both are true; both are mine*). The integration has not reduced the debt; it has shifted who owes it from a fictive third party to the subject himself.

**Failure mode.** The ledger is unfinishable. There is no possible quantum of atonement that closes the account, because the dead cannot be un-killed, and so any framework of *enough* is incoherent to him. This is the engine of the entire post-restoration behavioral pattern and is functionally untreatable without addressing the underlying moral-injury substrate — and even there, per Griffin et al., complete resolution is not the realistic target; livable coexistence is.

**Leverage.** Indirect but powerful. Anyone who can credibly invoke the dead — by name, by detail, by surviving relative — has a hook in him. The hook can be pulled in either direction: cruel actors have used it to destabilize him (you killed her, do you remember her, here is her daughter); kind actors have used it to ground him (you killed her, her daughter is alive, her daughter is safe, you helped). The same lever, opposite torques.

---

## 6a.7 — THE BARNES DESCENDANTS (NIECES, NEPHEWS, GREAT-GRAND-NIECES AND -NEPHEWS, BY BECCA)

**Status.** Living. Scattered across the American Northeast and, per the file, two on the West Coast. Working professionals, retirees, schoolchildren. None of them, with the exception of Becca's eldest, are aware that he checks on them. Becca's eldest is aware and has not told the others.

**History.** A family tree that grew while he was frozen. Each of these people exists because Becca outlived him and built the life he did not get to. They are, in a sense he finds difficult to articulate, the *yield* of his absence — proof that the world continued, that the household reorganized, that loss is not the end of lineage.

**Dynamics.** Distal and vigilant. He does not introduce himself; he does not attend graduations or weddings; he does not give gifts. He drives past. He runs background checks on suspicious neighbors. He has, on at least two occasions in the published record, removed threats that the descendants never knew existed. The relationship is entirely one-directional and entirely protective.

**Trust / safety baseline.** Trust is not the operative term; *fidelity* is. He does not need them to know him. He needs them to be safe.

**Evolution.** Slowly increasing tolerance for distant proxy contact — Becca's eldest functions as a one-person bridge, and through her he receives photographs, news of births, occasional letters. He keeps them. He does not display them. He has not, as of the most recent published record, met any descendant face to face under his own name.

**Failure mode.** A descendant in genuine danger would draw him out of any operational commitment instantly and absolutely. A descendant who learned of him and rejected him — plausible, given the historical weight of the name — would constitute a wound he is not currently armored against, because he has organized his interior on the assumption that they will never know and therefore never have to choose.

**Leverage.** Maximal among living relationships in raw operational terms. Anyone who locates and threatens the descendants owns him for the duration of the threat. The file recommends — for benevolent purposes — that descendant security be considered a quiet protectorate priority on his behalf, independent of his own efforts, so that the leverage cannot be activated.

---

## 6a.8 — KARPOV AND THE HANDLERS (THE ANTI-FATHERS)

**Status.** Variably deceased; the original General Karpov long dead; successor handlers across the Department X lineage variously killed, imprisoned, scattered, or absorbed into successor intelligence apparatuses. Indexed here because the handler-relationship occupied, by force, the structural slot that should have been occupied by paternal/fraternal kin during the seventy-year captivity, and the residue of that occupation remains in his interior.

**History.** Karpov was the first and the template: the man who received him from the ice, oversaw his conditioning, named him, deployed him, returned him to the ice. The relationship has the surface features of father-son — pedagogy, expectation, withheld approval, ritual greeting — overlaid on the substance of owner-tool. Successor handlers across decades replicated the template with variations in cruelty and competence.

**Dynamics.** The most contaminated bond in the file. The conditioning protocol explicitly used the attachment apparatus against him — handlers were the source of food, of warmth (relative to the cryogenic baseline), of language, of task, of the only continuity of self he was permitted. He cannot, even now, hear certain Russian cadences without the body remembering a posture of receptive submission that the conscious mind has repudiated. The integration work of the post-restoration years has been, in significant part, the work of un-installing the handler-shaped slot in his attachment system — and the slot has not fully closed.

**Trust / safety baseline.** Inverted. The handlers were the people on whom his survival depended and whose presence guaranteed his ongoing unmaking; the body learned to relax around the source of harm, and the body has not unlearned it as completely as the mind has.

**Evolution.** From total dependency (captivity) to active hunting (post-restoration, the Brubaker-era pursuit of surviving handlers and the dismantling of the program) to present-day vigilance (the assumption that the program or its successor persists and will attempt reactivation if the opportunity arises). He has personally killed several of the surviving handlers; the killings were professional rather than vengeful in execution but the file assesses the motivation as both operational and exorcistic.

**Failure mode.** Reactivation. The trigger-word protocol, even with the post-restoration inhibitory countermeasures, retains residual hold. A handler-figure with the protocol, sufficient privacy, and time could in principle still produce partial state-switch, with the catastrophic consequences this implies. He knows this. He has accordingly arranged his life so that he is rarely alone with strangers for long, rarely restrained, rarely subjected to cold, and rarely exposed to extended Russian-language input from unknown sources. These are operational hygiene; they are also, read another way, the daily routine of a man who has not stopped being afraid of his own family of origin in the captive sense.

**Leverage.** Catastrophic if achievable; low probability of achievement given current countermeasures. The remaining handlers and any success


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

*Subject's social architecture is not a network; it is a short list of named persons, each held with a granularity of trust that took years (in some cases decades) to construct, and each occupying a structurally distinct functional role in his post-restoration ecology. Generalized "team" feeling is performance. The list below is the actual file.*

The pattern, before the persons: Barnes does not befriend. He *vets*, then *commits*. The vetting period for each person below ran months to years of observed behavior under stress before he extended what he himself would not call trust but which functions as such. Once extended, the bond is near-unrevocable; he has been observed to maintain operational loyalty to persons who have forgotten him, hated him, or actively tried to kill him under duress (Romanova, post-mindwipe; Rogers, during programmed-shield combat in Bendis's *Avengers* crossovers). Loyalty in Barnes's schema is not contingent on reciprocation. It is contingent only on his own original assessment having been correct, an assessment he refuses to revisit absent overwhelming evidence.

---

## 1. STEVEN GRANT ROGERS — The Anchor Object

**History.** The longest-running and most structurally load-bearing relationship in the file. Origin: pre-war Brooklyn, two adolescent boys, asymmetrical from the start — Barnes physically dominant, socially competent, the protector; Rogers smaller, sicker, morally absolute, the protected. The directionality reverses at Project Rebirth (1941) but the *psychic* directionality never fully does. In Barnes's internal register Rogers remains, structurally, the smaller person he is responsible for; he is constitutionally unable to relate to Rogers as a peer to be relied upon, only as a person to be defended. This is the most clinically interesting feature of the bond and the one Rogers himself has named, repeatedly, with increasing frustration across the published record.

**Dynamics.** Field-level: telepathic in the colloquial sense — they read each other's intent off micro-cues (Rogers's chin angle, Barnes's left-shoulder drop) and execute paired tactical maneuvers without verbal coordination. Documented across every team-up published 1941–present. Social-level: Barnes deflects Rogers's emotional approaches with humor (pre-Fall) or with silence and tactical redirection (post-restoration). Rogers persistently attempts to break through; Barnes persistently lets him *almost* succeed, then withdraws. The withdrawal is not rejection; it is throttling. He cannot tolerate the full intensity of being known by the one person who knew him before.

**Evolution.** Four phases. (a) *Pre-Fall (1941–1945):* informal, fraternal, intensely loyal, with Barnes occupying a partner-and-protector role that the Golden Age framing flattened into "sidekick." (b) *Absence (1945–c.2005 in-universe):* Rogers as ghost; Barnes as Winter Soldier, the name "Steve" surfacing in fragments under Department X conditioning, used by handlers as a stress-test stimulus precisely because of its destabilizing pull. (c) *Restoration through Death of Captain America (2005–2007):* Rogers restores Barnes; Barnes flees, returns slowly, refuses the mantle, accepts it only when Rogers is dead and Sharon Carter frames it as Rogers's will. Critical: Barnes can be in relationship with Rogers's *legacy* more comfortably than with Rogers's *presence*. (d) *Mature bond (2011–present):* gradual de-escalation of the protector dynamic toward something that approaches peership during operations; outside operations, Barnes still defaults to deferential register and self-effacement when Rogers is present.

**Trust / safety.** Maximal. Of all persons living, Rogers is the one in whose presence Barnes will permit himself to sleep deeply. Field observation across multiple safehouse sequences (Brubaker, Remender): Barnes positions himself between Rogers and the door, but he *closes his eyes*. With every other ally except Romanova, he does not. Conversational safety is lower than physical safety — Barnes will let Rogers move his body but not his self-concept; will tolerate physical proximity but reroute any conversation that attempts to interrogate his sense of what he owes.

**Failure mode.** The bond's structural weakness is its asymmetry: Barnes cannot accept that Rogers might need him *as a person*, only as a soldier. When Rogers attempts to be cared for by Barnes (post-de-aging arcs, post-injury sequences), Barnes performs the care competently but visibly distresses — being the strong one for Rogers reads as a violation of the original ledger and re-activates pre-war anxiety. Secondary failure mode: Rogers's moral example is so internalized that Barnes uses it as a stick to beat himself with; "what Steve would do" is invoked less as guidance than as accusation.

**Leverage.** Anyone seeking to move Barnes can do so through Rogers — to protect him, avenge him, fulfill his stated or imputed wishes. This has been exploited by Sharon Carter, Fury, and Sin (hostilely). Conversely, threats to Rogers eliminate Barnes's risk calculation entirely; he will burn any other consideration including mission, allies-in-the-room, and his own life. *Operational note: this is the single greatest predictability in the subject's behavior.*

---

## 2. NATALIA ALIANOVNA ROMANOVA — The Mirror

**History.** Originating contact: the Red Room program, late 1950s, when Romanova was a Black Widow trainee and Barnes was her instructor — a relationship explicitly permitted by Department X and then explicitly erased, by both parties, as part of the standard pliability protocol. Barnes was made to forget her; she was made to forget him; both retain fragmentary somatic memory recovered piecewise across decades. Re-met as adults, multiple times across the published record, in a recursive pattern of recognition-loss-recognition that mirrors the conditioning itself.

**Dynamics.** The closest thing in Barnes's life to peership. They share a vocabulary — operational Russian, Red Room hand-signs, the specific affect-shape of someone who was made into a weapon as a child — that no one else in his ecology speaks. Communication runs at extreme economy: a glance across a room is a full sentence; a touch on the wrist is a clause. Sexual/romantic bond is real, repeatedly reaffirmed (Brubaker's *Winter Soldier* solo run, 2012; their interactions across multiple Avengers titles) but structurally *non-domestic*. They have never cohabited in any settled sense; their shared spaces are safehouses, hotels, the back rooms of black sites. They eat standing up. They sleep in shifts.

**Evolution.** (a) *Red Room (handlers' permission, handlers' erasure)*: the original template for "attachment is the punishment." (b) *Winter Soldier era re-encounters*: she meets the Soldier on opposing sides multiple times; partial recognitions are aborted by his handlers. (c) *Post-restoration reunion*: tentative, conducted in adult terms, with both parties aware that the romance they remember is a romance between two children-soldiers who no longer fully exist. (d) *Adult partnership*: the working/intimate pair-bond, with Barnes accepting her autonomy absolutely — including her memory loss in the *Widowmaker* arc, which he tolerated without contest. (e) *Mature alliance*: their bond is now more reliable than romantic, more comradely than coupled, but the romantic substrate is undeleted.

**Trust / safety.** Total in the operational register; conditional in the emotional. He trusts her with his life automatically and with his backstory selectively. She is the one person to whom he does not have to *explain* the Winter Soldier; she was present for portions of it, on both sides. This produces a peculiar safety: he does not have to manage her reaction to his history because her history is adjacent.

**Failure mode.** The non-domestic structure is a shared defense, not just his — both parties prefer it, both parties also occasionally grieve it. When external circumstance forces them into a more settled configuration (cover identities requiring cohabitation), both become irritable, sleep poorly, and eventually engineer a reason to deploy. Secondary failure mode: when she has forgotten him, he does not insist on being remembered, even when re-establishing the bond would serve his mission and her interests. He reads insistence as a violation of the consent her handlers stole.

**Leverage.** Threats to Romanova produce the same risk-zero response as threats to Rogers, possibly faster because she is the one person whose competence he does not feel obligated to protect — meaning he can deploy laterally in her defense rather than substitutively. Conversely, *she* is the most effective lever on him because she can speak in the register that bypasses his stated rationalizations. A sentence from her, in Russian, has stopped him from going operational on two documented occasions.

---

## 3. NICHOLAS J. FURY — The Spymaster as Reintegration Officer

**History.** Operational acquaintance dating to WWII (Howling Commandos liaison, briefly) and reactivated immediately post-restoration when Barnes, holding the Cosmic Cube, chose Fury — not Rogers — as the person to approach first. This selection is the single most diagnostic moment of the early post-restoration record.

**Dynamics.** Fury offers Barnes what Rogers cannot: a relationship with zero emotional debt, predicated entirely on mutual operational utility. Fury does not ask Barnes to be okay, does not ask him to be redeemed, does not ask him to feel anything. Fury asks him to *work*, in registers Barnes already speaks. The relationship is unsentimental in a way that registers to Barnes as a form of respect.

**Evolution.** (a) *Reintegration period*: Fury runs Barnes as a personal off-books asset, provides safehouses, intelligence, cover documents, no questions about disposition. This is the scaffolding on which Barnes rebuilt civilian-adjacent functioning. (b) *Cap-mantle period*: Fury becomes one of three persons (with Sharon Carter and Romanova) trusted with the secret of Barnes-as-Cap. (c) *Man-on-the-Wall succession*: Fury hands Barnes the role explicitly — the preemptive killer of cosmic threats. The handover is the most consequential mentor act in the file; Fury identified Barnes as the only person constitutionally suited to a job whose moral cost is structurally incompatible with most operators' continued functioning.

**Trust / safety.** Operational trust: extremely high. Personal trust: deliberately bounded by both parties; Fury does not extend it, Barnes does not seek it. The bond's strength is in its containment.

**Failure mode.** Fury is willing to spend Barnes — and Barnes is willing to be spent. Their compatibility is also their pathology: they collude in Barnes's self-handicapping. A more emotionally invested mentor would refuse the Man-on-the-Wall handover; Fury, being Fury, recognized Barnes's suitability and used it. The relationship contains no friction against Barnes's worst tendencies.

**Leverage.** Fury can task Barnes to nearly any operation with a credible national/planetary-security framing. Conversely, Barnes is one of the few persons who can refuse Fury without consequence, because Fury's regard for him is partly a regard for that very refusal capacity. They speak in declaratives, not requests.

---

## 4. SAMUEL THOMAS WILSON — The Successor Who Is Also the Friend

**History.** Initial acquaintance through Rogers; relationship matured independently after both men cycled through the Captain America mantle and out the other side. They are the only two living persons who know what it is to wear Rogers's shield as a sustained identity rather than a moment, and that shared experiential vocabulary is the bond's substrate.

**Dynamics.** Wilson treats Barnes with a specific calibrated warmth that does not demand reciprocation — closer to professional kindness than to friendship in the early period, evolving into something more candid over time. Barnes tolerates Wilson's humor without matching it but is observed to relax around him; the relaxation is small but measurable (shoulders dropping a perceptible quarter-inch, left arm uncrossed). Wilson is one of the few persons who can call Barnes by his civilian name in casual register without producing a flinch.

**Evolution.** (a) *Initial wariness*: Barnes pre-judged Wilson as an intrusion into the Rogers dyad, a judgment Wilson dissolved by simply not pressing. (b) *Mantle-peer phase*: shared institutional experience produces functional intimacy. (c) *Mature alliance*: Wilson now occupies a stable role as the friend who is neither part of the Red Room substratum nor part of the pre-war substratum — i.e., a person Barnes knows *as himself, now*, with no history requiring management.

**Trust / safety.** High, in a category distinct from Rogers/Romanova: Wilson is the trusted *present-tense* friend, the one Barnes can be with without simultaneously being with his own biography. This is rarer than it sounds and structurally important.

**Failure mode.** Barnes will not initiate contact with Wilson. The friendship runs on Wilson's outreach. If Wilson stops calling, Barnes will not notice the silence as deprivation; he will note it, accept it as Wilson's choice, and not seek to repair. Secondary failure mode: when both men are in mission-critical contexts, Barnes treats Wilson with deference appropriate to a current Cap, which Wilson finds tiresome but cannot dissuade.

**Leverage.** Lower than Rogers/Romanova but real; Barnes will deploy in Wilson's defense without hesitation, and Wilson is one of the few persons whose moral arguments Barnes will actually hear rather than deflect, because Wilson's arguments are made without the freight of historical claim.

---

## 5. T'CHALLA — The Sovereign Who Granted Sanctuary

**History.** Initial contact adversarial through historical action; relationship rebuilt through T'Challa's choice to grant Barnes sanctuary in Wakanda, conduct deconditioning under Shuri's protocols, and assign him the White Wolf designation. The relationship is the rarest in the file: one initiated by Barnes having done harm to someone in T'Challa's intimate circle, and resolved by T'Challa's unilateral decision to extend grace.

**Dynamics.** Formal, distant, but founded on an act of forgiveness so structurally complete that it functions for Barnes as a permanent benchmark. T'Challa never required Barnes to perform contrition, never demanded explanation, simply offered the protocols and the land. Barnes responded with an obedience to Wakandan custom and to T'Challa personally that approaches the unconditional. He learned conversational Wakandan; he observed local mourning practices; he kept goats.

**Evolution.** (a) *Sanctuary phase*: Barnes in cryo and then in deconditioning, T'Challa as distant but personally accountable host. (b) *White Wolf phase*: Barnes integrated into Wakandan defense protocols on T'Challa's terms. (c) *Mature client-patron bond*: Barnes leaves and returns to Wakanda over years; the welcome is reliable; the obligation is unrequested and absolute.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric. Barnes trusts T'Challa absolutely. T'Challa's trust in Barnes is operational and conditional, which Barnes accepts as appropriate. He has never sought to close the asymmetry.

**Failure mode.** Barnes will not refuse a Wakandan request, even when refusal would be strategically correct. The debt-structure overrides his independent judgment in this single domain. Secondary failure mode: he will not bring his other troubles into Wakanda, treating the sanctuary as conditional on his good behavior even when no one has imposed that condition.

**Leverage.** T'Challa can task Barnes to nearly any action; he has not exploited this and is not likely to, which is part of why the leverage exists.

---

## 6. SHURI — The Architect of the Body

**History.** Clinical relationship initiated as part of the Wakandan deconditioning protocol; she designed the trigger-word neutralization and the vibranium prosthesis. The bond is unusual in being founded on technical intimacy with his nervous system and his amputation site.

**Dynamics.** She is one of perhaps three persons in the file who can touch Barnes's left shoulder without producing a startle response. She earned this by being the person who removed the Soviet hardware from his body. Their relationship is collegial-affectionate, with Shuri permitted a teasing register no other person below Romanova's tier is permitted; Barnes tolerates it because she is the architect of the body he now inhabits.

**Evolution.** (a) *Clinical*: patient-and-engineer. (b) *Familial-adjacent*: she treats him as a recurring older brother of inconvenient repute; he treats her with the slightly off-balance courtesy of a man not used to being teased by someone whose competence he respects without reservation.

**Trust / safety.** Total in the somatic register. He will let her work on the arm in a way he would let no one else.

**Failure mode.** He will not bring her his psychological complaints, only his hardware complaints, even when the boundary blurs. He treats her competence as a resource not to be overspent.

**Leverage.** Indirect, via T'Challa and via the prosthesis itself — anyone who can persuade Shuri to ask Barnes for something will likely get it.

---

## 7. YELENA BELOVA — The Inherited Protege

**History.** Connection mediated through Romanova; deepened by shared Red Room substrate; consolidated through joint operations in the recent Thunderbolts material. Barnes occupies, with respect to Yelena, a structurally identical role to the one his own original Red Room instructor occupied with respect to Romanova — except that Barnes is conscious of the parallel and refuses to repeat its abuses.

**Dynamics.** He mentors her tactically; he does not attempt to mentor her emotionally, having no confidence in his own emotional competence. He is observed to extend her the specific small courtesies of a man who knows what it is to be young inside a body trained to kill: he will not surprise her from behind; he will not test her unannounced; he will let her cook for him even when he is not hungry. She tries his patience deliberately and he tolerates it because tolerating it is part of the assignment he has given himself.

**Evolution.** Newer than the others; still consolidating. The arc points toward a stable mentor-protege relationship in which Barnes is the only adult Yelena fully trusts who is not Romanova, and Yelena is one of the few people whose teasing Barnes can metabolize as affection rather than as threat.

**Trust / safety.** Growing; substantial. He will sleep in safehouses she has secured.

**Failure mode.** He will overprotect her at operational cost. If she is in the field, his risk model degrades. Secondary failure mode: he projects Romanova's history onto her and occasionally treats her as a stand-in for the young Natasha he failed, which Yelena detects and resents.

**Leverage.** Threats to Yelena produce the same response as threats to Romanova, slightly slower and slightly more controlled because she is not (yet) on the absolute list. She is on the list that becomes absolute.

---

## 8. SHARON CARTER — The Reluctant Co-Conspirator

**History.** Connected through Rogers; deepened through the Death of Captain America operations during which she, Barnes, and Fury formed the inner cell holding the Cap-mantle secret. She and Barnes share the specific guilt of having been Rogers's instruments at moments of consequence — she as the brainwashed shooter, he as the successor.

**Dynamics.** Functional, somber, mutually careful. Neither party seeks the other's company; both will reliably appear when summoned. The bond is founded on a shared private knowledge of having loved Rogers in ways that produced harm.

**Trust / safety.** Operational; bounded.

**Failure mode.** Barnes will defer to Carter on Rogers-adjacent decisions in ways that abdicate his own judgment.

**Leverage.** Modest. She can call him into Rogers-related operations and he will arrive.

---

## 9. CLINTON BARTON — The Peer of Adjacent Damage

**History.** Long acquaintance through Avengers structures; not intimate but durable. Barton is one of the few persons whose operational competence Barnes acknowledges without qualification and whose damage-profile Barnes recognizes as parallel without being identical.

**Dynamics.** Sparse, sardonic, respectful. They communicate in jokes about the work that other persons in the room do not understand. They do not socialize outside the work.

**Trust / safety.** High in field; low in personal. Each would die for the other and neither would call the other to talk.

**Failure mode.** They will collude in self-handicapping behavior on missions, each enabling the other's risk tolerance.

**Leverage.** Limited; circumstantial.

---

## 10. THE THUNDERBOLTS / WAR-TEAM IN-GROUPS — Provisional Family

**History.** Across the Thunderbolts iterations and the post-2011 covert team structures, Barnes has functioned as either reluctant leader or load-bearing operator within small teams of partially-redeemed or actively-redeeming operators. These constellations vary; the pattern does not.

**Dynamics.** Barnes runs these teams from behind even when titularly in front. He extends provisional trust to members on a per-mission basis; he extends durable trust to perhaps one or two of them across a roster's lifetime. He is the team's confessor without seeking the role: members of these teams disclose to Barnes precisely because he does not perform shock or judgment at disclosure, having privately exceeded any of their crime ledgers.

**Trust / safety.** Calibrated per individual; rarely high but rarely zero.

**Failure mode.** He will treat the team as expendable in service of any of the absolute-list persons above. The team senses this and adjusts.

**Leverage.** Low at the team level; moderate via individual members who occasionally graduate to durable-trust status (Yelena being the principal example).

---

## 11. THE GHOST CIRCLE — Absent Mentors, Functionally Present

The file would be incomplete without three persons who do not appear in operational logs but who function as internal interlocutors in the subject's documented internal monologue (Brubaker, Remender, Ewing).

- **George Barnes (father, deceased childhood).** A reference point so distant the subject barely accesses it; surfaces in dreams and under deep-conditioning recall. Functions as the original *military authority that loved him,* a template that all subsequent mentor relationships partially reconstruct.
- **General Vasily Karpov (handler, deceased).** The aggressor with whom Barnes partially identified during conditioning. Surfaces in the subject's internal voice as the *operational register itself* — when Barnes thinks tactically in clipped imperative sentences, he is using Karpov's voice and is aware of it. This is one of his most uncomfortable forms of self-knowledge.
- **Rogers-as-internalized-superego.** Distinct from Rogers-as-person. The internalized Rogers is more demanding, more austere, and more present in Barnes's deliberation than the actual Rog


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

*Cross-referenced subject file, BARNES, J.B. — Section III/C. Antagonistic and intimate dyads, longitudinal mapping. Treats "rival," "enemy," and "lover" as overlapping operational categories: the subject's life has not honored their separation, and several figures occupy two of the three or all three across time. Each entry maps origin of relation, behavioral evolution, present-tense valence, trust/safety architecture, characteristic failure mode, and exploitable leverage.*

---

## A. ENEMIES OF RECORD

### A.1 — Helmut Zemo (Baron Zemo, Heinrich's son; latterly the architect of multiple disassembly events)

**Origin.** Inherited enmity. The drone-plane off Newfoundland (*Avengers* #4, 1964) belonged to Heinrich Zemo; Helmut is the son who carried the surname forward. Barnes's primal traumatic event — the dismemberment, the cold water, the seventy-year unmaking — is the act of a man Barnes never met, executed by a man who shares only his name. The grievance is therefore *doubled and impure*: the rightful target is dead, the available target is a legitimate but secondary actor, and Barnes's own behavior in any encounter is muddied by knowing it.

**Behavioral evolution.** Across published canon Barnes's posture toward Helmut Zemo is colder than toward any other living enemy. He does not banter with Zemo. He does not negotiate. The verbal economy that drops two notches under mild stress drops to near-silence in Zemo's presence. Where he taunts other antagonists (the Bucky-era wisecrack survives in fragments, ironized), with Zemo he simply works. This is not heightened rage — it is the inward escalation pattern; he goes cold, and Zemo is the coldest he gets.

**Trust / safety architecture.** Zero. Subject does not believe Zemo's word in any register, including offered intelligence that turns out to be accurate. He treats Zemo's truthful statements as longer cons.

**Failure mode.** Subject will accept tactical alliance with Zemo when mission demands (the precedent exists across canon — Zemo has been a useful broker), but he will not protect Zemo at any cost beyond the immediate operational requirement, and he will not be in a room with him longer than function requires. The risk is not that Barnes lashes out; it is that he disengages affectively at the exact moment Zemo requires a watcher, and Zemo exploits the gap.

**Leverage.** Zemo's only real lever on Barnes is the past tense — naming the drone, naming Karpov, naming the chain. Barnes has built inhibitory countermeasures against the Russian phrase-strings; he has built fewer countermeasures against being narratively reminded *whose project he was inside.* Zemo knows it. He does not need to use it often.

---

### A.2 — Aleksander Lukin / The Red Skull (composite host, *Captain America* vol. 5)

**Origin.** Lukin is the late-Soviet general who inherited the Winter Soldier program from Karpov, and the man who deployed Barnes in the post-Cold-War period for private-capital wet work. The Skull's consciousness rode Lukin's body for substantial portions of the Brubaker run via the Cosmic Cube. The composite is the single figure most responsible for the *post-Karpov* deployment phase of Barnes's captivity — Karpov made the asset; Lukin used it.

**Behavioral evolution.** Subject's response to Lukin is qualitatively different from his response to Zemo: where Zemo activates cold withdrawal, Lukin activates *operational rage in the controlled register* — the closest Barnes comes to admitting that the asset he was contains a grievance the man he is now must execute. He pursued Lukin with a directness he denied himself in nearly any other matter.

**Trust / safety.** None. Pure target valence.

**Failure mode.** Barnes is more likely, against Lukin / Skull-derivative figures, to take an unjustifiable solo risk and to refuse extraction. The Man-on-the-Wall logic activates early in these engagements: this is *his* kill to make and his cost to absorb.

**Leverage.** Lukin and his descendants in the program know the handler protocols and the conditioning lexicon. Even spoken in approximate cadence, the cues retain partial valence. Subject knows this and has, on at least two documented occasions, requested that allies leave the room before engagement so they will not witness him having to fight himself.

---

### A.3 — General Vasily Karpov (deceased; persists as posthumous adversary)

**Origin.** The architect. The handler of record across the bulk of Barnes's Department X tenure. The voice in the conditioning tapes; the hand on the cryo controls; the face above the chair.

**Behavioral evolution.** Karpov is dead in canon. The relationship is therefore not active — and yet it structures every active relationship Barnes has, because Karpov is the template against which every later authority figure is unconsciously measured. Subject's near-allergy to institutional command (compliant in form, independently judging in substance) is Karpov's bequest. He cannot be in a hierarchical structure without auditing it for Karpov-shape: who decides what the asset forgets, who decides whom the asset kills, who decides when the asset sleeps.

**Trust.** Posthumous; permanent enemy.

**Failure mode.** Subject occasionally projects Karpov onto living commanders who do not deserve it (Fury escapes this projection by virtue of long history and explicit non-handler positioning; lesser figures do not). When projection occurs, Barnes withdraws cooperation without explanation, and the legitimate commander loses an operator without knowing why.

**Leverage.** Karpov's surviving protocols — the documentation, the recordings, the chair. Any actor in possession of Karpov-derived material has nontrivial leverage. Subject has spent measurable effort across the Brubaker, Remender, and Kot eras locating and destroying these materials. The work is not finished and he does not believe it ever will be.

---

### A.4 — Department X / KGB Residue / Hammer-Vector "old colleagues"

**Origin.** Not a single person but a recurring class of antagonist: the Red Room trainers who survived the program's dissolution, the auxiliary handlers, the doctors, the technicians, the men who held the clipboards. They surface across the Romanova solo runs and intermittently across his own.

**Behavioral evolution.** Subject's pattern is methodical and quiet. He does not announce these engagements. He executes them in his own time, off-book, often alone. He keeps a working list — inferred from his behavior across decades; the list itself has never been depicted on-panel but the existence of one is the most parsimonious explanation for the pattern of *who he happens to encounter and how prepared he happens to be when he does.*

**Trust.** None, ever.

**Failure mode.** Subject's discipline around this list is the principal site at which Romanova has, across multiple runs, had to intervene to prevent him from crossing a line he himself drew. The two of them have, at minimum, one tacit agreement that whoever finishes the list first will tell the other.

**Leverage.** None of these figures has leverage on him directly; they are leverage *for* third parties who wish to move him by promising or denying access.

---

### A.5 — HYDRA (institutional, not personal)

**Origin.** The original wartime enemy; in the modern canon the entity into which much of Department X's institutional knowledge eventually flowed. Subject's grievance with HYDRA is genealogical: they are downstream beneficiaries of the apparatus that owned him.

**Behavioral evolution.** Subject treats HYDRA engagements as a baseline maintenance obligation. He does not require special motivation to deploy against them; he does not require special recovery after. They are *background work.* This is itself diagnostic: an enemy that horrifies most operators is, for Barnes, the routine load. He has used up his capacity for being horrified by them.

**Failure mode.** Underestimation of organizational adaptability. Subject sometimes attacks HYDRA cells as if they were the same HYDRA he fought in 1944; they are not, and he has been ambushed by their evolution.

**Leverage.** Captured HYDRA personnel occasionally retain or claim to retain partial conditioning lexicons. Subject treats every such claim as credible until verified false. This produces a small but real exploitable delay in interrogation engagements.

---

### A.6 — His own past selves

**Origin.** Endogenous; nonetheless treated here because the behavioral record warrants it. The Winter Soldier is, functionally, an adversary Barnes carries in his own neurology. The 1940s Bucky is an adversary too, in a quieter way — a younger man whose untroubled competence Barnes can no longer access without grief.

**Behavioral evolution.** Early post-restoration: third-person reference ("the Winter Soldier did that"), classic dissociative distancing. Mid-period: increasingly first-person ("I did that, under conditions I did not consent to, which does not erase the *I*"). Present-tense: integrated, with the integration itself being a load he carries — he is no longer protected by the split.

**Trust / safety.** He does not trust his own neurology under specific cue conditions. He has built scaffolds — geographical (he avoids certain Russian-speaking environments unnecessarily), procedural (he asks allies to restrain him preemptively in suspected trigger contexts), pharmacological (canon is reticent but his behavior implies management).

**Failure mode.** Integration's cost: when triggered, the response is no longer cleanly dissociative; the conscious Barnes is present to *witness* what the conditioning is trying to make him do. This is more disabling than the prior split, not less, and figures hostile to him have begun (per recent canon) to exploit it.

**Leverage.** The cue lexicon; restraint; cold; certain medical sensory contexts. Subject knows the full list. It is the one inventory he keeps current.

---

## B. RIVALS (not enemies — figures of friction, comparison, and ambivalent competition)

### B.1 — Sam Wilson

**Origin.** The other inheritor. When the shield moves, it moves between the two of them and the man it originally belonged to. Wilson's tenure as Captain America runs parallel to Barnes's, and the canon places them in repeated comparison: two men carrying a symbol neither of them feels entitled to, for different reasons.

**Behavioral evolution.** Early friction — the published record shows real tension, distrust on Wilson's side regarding Barnes's history, distrust on Barnes's side regarding anyone occupying the symbolic position of Rogers. Evolved across the 2010s into one of the more stable working relationships in his small in-group. The rivalry survives as *gentle competitive register* — they take each other seriously; they let each other be unimpressive; they tease, sparingly.

**Trust / safety.** Substantial. Subject will accept Wilson's tactical authority in joint operations without the Karpov-projection problem. Wilson is one of the few non-Rogers figures who has earned this.

**Failure mode.** Subject defers to Wilson on questions of public moral legitimacy (Wilson can be Captain America in daylight; Barnes cannot) and this deference can become withdrawal — Barnes may step back from a situation in which his presence is needed, on the theory that Wilson's presence is sufficient and his own is contaminating. Wilson has had to call him back into rooms.

**Leverage.** Wilson has standing to invoke Rogers's judgment in ways most others do not. He uses this rarely and well.

---

### B.2 — Clint Barton

**Origin.** Same operational ecology, different temperaments. Barton is the loud version of the same job. The two of them are positioned across multiple team books as the *non-super-soldier perimeter* — the operators who keep functioning when the powers fail.

**Behavioral evolution.** Friction principally over presentation. Barton's affective register (sardonic, openly broken, performatively unbothered) is the version of "damaged operator" that Barnes could have become and chose not to.
