There is an implicit critique each way: Barton finds Barnes's self-seriousness exhausting; Barnes finds Barton's deflection irresponsible. Neither says it aloud often.

**Trust / safety.** Operational trust high. Personal trust moderate. They do not confide.

**Failure mode.** They will not call each other in a crisis until late. Each assumes the other has it handled.

**Leverage.** Yelena Belova, whom Barton's history and Barnes's history both implicate, is a topic that closes both of them down simultaneously. A third party who knew how to invoke her could move them in tandem, though probably not as intended.

---

### B.3 — The Punisher (Frank Castle)

**Origin.** Methodological rival. Castle is the case study of what Barnes could have become had he organized his post-restoration penance around the wrong axiom. Castle's grief becomes a *system of killing*; Barnes's guilt becomes a *system of restraint that includes killing.* The published encounters between them (Brubaker, later writers) stage this difference explicitly.

**Behavioral evolution.** Subject's posture toward Castle is recognizable: the cold, the verbal economy, the refusal of camaraderie. But unlike with Zemo or Lukin, there is an undertow of *near-miss recognition* — he sees in Castle the road he did not take and treats it with the wariness one reserves for one's own counterfactuals.

**Trust / safety.** Low. He believes Castle's word about Castle's intentions. He does not believe Castle's judgment about which targets warrant which response.

**Failure mode.** Subject will not enter sustained cooperation with Castle even when mission alignment is total. He treats proximity to Castle as a moral hazard for himself.

**Leverage.** None Castle would consciously use; Castle does not deal in leverage. But Castle's mere ongoing existence functions as a reminder Barnes does not require and cannot dismiss.

---

### B.4 — Hawkeye (Kate Bishop), Yelena Belova, and the younger operator cohort

**Origin.** Generational. The younger operators occupy the role Barnes himself occupied in 1942 — the deniable, clean-faced, lethally competent youth. He cannot watch them without watching himself.

**Behavioral evolution.** Subject's posture is mentor-rival: he competes with them on tradecraft (gentle, instructive), and he competes with them for the right to take the worst assignment (not gentle). Yelena specifically — given her Red Room origin — sits in a category of her own, *part rival, part sister-in-condition, part atonement object,* and is treated under her own entry in Relationships II. Noted here only because the rivalry valence with her is real: she is better at some of what he does, and he both wants her to be and resents that she is.

**Trust / safety.** High in-group. The rivalry is the affectionate kind.

**Failure mode.** Subject over-protects this cohort to the point of denying them assignments they have earned. They have, severally, called him on it.

**Leverage.** Threats to any of them collapse the rivalry register and activate the protection drive. He becomes operationally legible — which is to say, exploitable — when they are in danger.

---

### B.5 — Wolverine (James Howlett / Logan)

**Origin.** Cohort overlap. The two of them ran adjacent missions across the WWII and Cold War theaters; both were unwitting subjects of state weaponization programs; both have lived past their century with carryover trauma. The published canon makes the parallel explicit at intervals.

**Behavioral evolution.** Mutual recognition without warmth. They share a wordless understanding that is not friendship — neither requires the other to perform recovery, neither requires the other to explain. Drinks have been had in silence. Information has been exchanged efficiently. Neither has ever asked the other for help.

**Trust / safety.** High in a narrow band: tradecraft, history, discretion. Outside that band, nonexistent — not because of mistrust but because they do not extend the relationship into the band.

**Failure mode.** When they have worked together, they have done so to lethal effect and at cost to bystanders. Each tends to assume the other's threshold is his own. It is not.

**Leverage.** None either would use. The relationship is its own seal.

---

## C. INTIMATES AND LOVERS

### C.1 — Natalia Alianovna Romanova (Natasha Romanoff)

**Origin (Department X period, 1950s–60s, per Brubaker's reconstruction).** Trainee in the Red Room program in which Barnes — as the Winter Soldier — was deployed as instructor and asset. The relationship begins inside captivity, *on both sides.* This is the first and most important fact about it: there is no clean origin. Whatever they were to each other began as something the program permitted, and the program permitted it precisely so it could later be amputated as a conditioning lesson. Per the established pattern: *attachment is the punishment.* The handlers let them have it; the handlers took it; the handlers took the memory of it.

**Behavioral evolution.** Decades of dormancy on both sides — neither remembered. Recovery of the memory occurs asymmetrically across the Brubaker run; she remembers in fragments, he remembers in floods, the two of them reconcile the records over months. Once recovered, the relationship does not resume in the form a casual reader might predict. They do not move in together. They do not present as a couple. They share safehouses, weapons caches, operational planning, beds intermittently, and — most consistently — silence. They are, functionally, *two operators who have agreed that each is the other's nearest person without converting that agreement into a structure either of them would have to maintain.*

**Trust / safety.** The highest in his life with the qualified exception of Rogers, and possibly higher in some operational respects. He will hand her his weapons. He will sleep in her presence — a concession he extends to almost no one given the insomnia and the trigger substrate. She has, across canon, talked him out of a partial state-switch by voice alone; she knows the cadences that bring him back. Conversely, she is the only person whose presence he can read in fully relaxed register; he does not have to perform competence for her because she has already seen the failure modes and stayed.

**Specific architecture of the bond.**
- *Non-domesticity is load-bearing.* Both of them associate domestic structure with the kind of trap their handlers used. The refusal to cohabit fully is not avoidance of intimacy; it is *preservation* of intimacy by removing the surface area their conditioning would attack.
- *Memory custody.* Each holds pieces of the other's past the other cannot reliably access. They have an unspoken protocol about which questions are answered and which are not.
- *Operational nesting.* They case each other's missions. They show up at the edges of each other's jobs without being asked. Neither acknowledges this as care; both rely on it.
- *Bodies.* Physical intimacy is documented across multiple runs but is not the primary register. The primary register is *proximity under threat* — the body knowing where the other body is in a room.

**Failure mode 1: Memory alteration.** When her memory of him has been altered or erased (a recurring event across canon), he accepts it. He does not press her to remember. He does not introduce himself as anything other than a colleague. He absorbs the loss as a continuation of the original program's logic — *attachment is the punishment* — and he treats his role as making sure she is not the one bearing the cost. This is recognizably loving and recognizably damaging.

**Failure mode 2: Mutual permissiveness toward lethality.** Each will let the other take a kill or a risk that an unrelated partner would refuse. They do not check each other the way a healthier dyad would. The Red Room list (above, A.4) is the cleanest example: each is the other's only acceptable backup, and each is the other's worst restraint.

**Failure mode 3: Asymmetric stoicism.** Both default to "I am fine." Neither calls the other on it reliably. Significant injuries have been hidden across both directions.

**Leverage.** She is the single most efficient lever on him in the world. Anyone who can credibly threaten her, anyone who can credibly *appear* to be her in distress, anyone who can place her in a position where his intervention costs her — moves him. He knows this. He has tried, repeatedly across canon, to compartmentalize the vulnerability and has failed. The compartmentalization is itself a tell: when he is overheard insisting that "Natasha can handle herself" with more emphasis than the situation requires, he is reassuring himself.

**Counter-leverage.** She is also the only person whose intervention can prevent him from completing a self-destructive course of action. Rogers can argue him out of one; she can simply arrive, and the course aborts. The two effects coexist.

---

### C.2 — Sin (Sinthea Schmidt) — *false intimate, conditioning artifact*

**Origin.** During the post-Brubaker / Fear Itself adjacent material, Barnes's recovered memories include manipulations and engineered proximities involving Skull-aligned operatives. Sin is not a lover in any clean sense; she is included here under the strict accounting principle this section requires, because the published record contains an exploitative pseudo-intimacy in the conditioning era that subject has had to process as part of his memory inventory.

**Behavioral evolution.** Subject's response to recovered memories of this category is the same as to any conditioning artifact: he documents, he integrates, he refuses to permit himself the consolation of treating it as someone else's biography. He does not seek the persons involved; he does not avoid them either.

**Trust / safety.** None. Pure historical category.

**Failure mode.** None operationally relevant; psychologically, these memories are among those that most reliably surface in nightmares (per Brubaker, Kot depictions).

**Leverage.** Knowledge of these episodes, in the hands of a hostile intelligence service, would be used to attempt to destabilize him publicly. He has accepted that this disclosure is possible. He has decided in advance not to deny it.

---

### C.3 — The Pre-War Civilian Women (Bucky-era social record)

**Origin.** The 1940s published material and Brubaker's retconned period material depict an active social life: dance halls, double dates with Rogers, several named and unnamed young women in the Brooklyn / Camp Lehigh / wartime-London perimeter. None of these relationships are deep in the published record; collectively they constitute a *social phase* rather than a set of bonds.

**Behavioral evolution.** This is the Barnes who is gone. The wisecracking dance-floor competence has been amputated as cleanly as the arm. Subject does not date in this register and has not since restoration. When he encounters the cultural artifacts of this era — a song, a step, a turn of phrase — the response across multiple writers is brief, private, and resembles bereavement more than nostalgia. He is mourning the man who could do that lightly.

**Trust / safety.** Historical only.

**Failure mode.** Subject occasionally tries to perform 1940s-Bucky for the comfort of others (Rogers in particular) and the performance is observable as performance; he knows it; the discomfort it produces is real.

**Leverage.** A skilled adversary using period cues — music, photographs, the specific cologne of the era, dance idiom — could produce a destabilizing affective response. This vector is rarely used because it is rarely understood.

---

### C.4 — Daisy Johnson and other short-tenure adult intimacies (Brubaker Winter Soldier solo; intermittent later material)

**Origin.** Post-restoration period; brief, adult, mut


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS — SUBJECT: BARNES, J.B.

*Cross-referenced from Simon/Kirby (1941), Lee/Kirby (Avengers #4, 1964), Englehart's Cap run, Thomas's Invaders, Brubaker's Captain America vol. 5 (2005–2012), Brubaker's Winter Soldier solo (2012), Remender's Bitter March, Kot's Bucky Barnes: The Winter Soldier (2014–15), Ewing's New Avengers, Rosenberg's Thunderbolts (2023), and the Cates material.*

---

## 1. THE BODY ITSELF — Substrate and Augmentation

**Baseline somatic stock.** Barnes is not a super-soldier in the Erskine sense. The published record is consistent on this point across eight decades: he was never given a serum analog. What he is, instead, is a man whose biological clock has been arrested by intermittent cryostasis for approximately fifty of his hundred-plus chronological years, leaving him with an apparent and functional age of roughly thirty. The tissue itself is ordinary human tissue, *preserved*. His durability, healing, and recovery profiles are at or only slightly above peak human — he bruises, bleeds, concusses, and tires within normal envelopes. He has been put down by gunfire, by Crossbones, by Karpov-era handlers wielding electrical compliance tools, and by his own dissociative shutdowns. The implication for any operator file: **he is not bulletproof and knows it**, which is part of what makes his risk calculus legible.

**Conditioning overlay.** What he *does* have, layered atop ordinary substrate, is the most thorough physical-conditioning regimen ever inflicted on a human nervous system. Department X did not enhance him biologically; they spent decades drilling motor patterns, reflex arcs, pain tolerance, breath control, and threat-discrimination into him until the responses run below conscious access. Brubaker's flashback panels show the training: blindfolded weapons handling, ECT-paired stimulus-response work, immersion-and-revive cycles teaching him to function in hypothermia, multi-language interrogation drills under physiological stress. The result is a man whose body executes correct action faster than his cognition reports the stimulus. This is not metahuman speed; it is *eliminated latency.*

**The left arm — Soviet prosthesis (1945–c. 2017).** Heavy mechanical-cybernetic unit articulated at the glenohumeral joint, plated in segmented metal (depicted as steel-analog in Brubaker, retconned to vibranium-laced in later runs to explain its capacity to clash with Rogers's shield without deformation). Mass estimated to far exceed the natural limb it replaced; this asymmetry is visible in his stance across the entire canon — left shoulder carried slightly low, weight distribution shifted right, a habitual micro-rotation of the torso when at rest. Capabilities included grip strength sufficient to crush small arms, a concussive open-palm strike, integrated EMP discharge in certain runs (Brubaker Winter Soldier solo), and embedded short-range tracking and comms. *Critical operational fact:* the arm required maintenance Barnes could not perform on himself. This was deliberate. Handler dependency was engineered into the prosthesis. Any handler-imposed weapon designed as a leash is, by definition, not fully his.

**The left arm — Wakandan prosthesis (post-rehabilitation, T'Challa/Shuri provenance).** Lighter vibranium construction, neurally integrated to a far higher fidelity, no external maintenance schedule, no embedded handler-controllable subsystems. Functionally retains crushing grip and percussive force; gains in proprioceptive fidelity (he can write, do fine field surgery on himself, handle small mechanisms — actions the Soviet arm performed clumsily). The change is visible in his posture within months of replacement: shoulders level, gait symmetrical, left hand resting open rather than fisted at rest. *The same body, given to him instead of welded to him.*

**Tissue at the seam.** Chronic referred pain at the scapulo-prosthetic interface is consistent across writers who depict him stripped — small habits of rolling the left shoulder, pressing the right thumb into the trapezius, sleeping on the right side only. Cold weather aggravates the seam; he wears the left sleeve looser than the right.

---

## 2. COMBAT — Mechanism, Range, Signature

**Marksmanship.** First-tier across all canon. He is depicted as one of the three or four best shots on Earth alongside Bullseye, Punisher, and the Hawkeyes. Mechanism: combination of natural aptitude (documented in his pre-war Camp Lehigh childhood — the orphan who learned rifles before he learned algebra), WWII sniper training under Army intelligence, and Soviet refinement that included shooting from cryogenic recovery (the body cold, hands shaking, ordered to put rounds on target before fine motor returned). Signature: he prefers a bolt-action rifle when the option exists — the deliberate cycle, the pause between shots, is psychologically congruent. Suppressed pistol work for close assignments. He shoots one-handed off the prosthesis with the same precision as the flesh hand, which most marksmen cannot do; the arm absorbs recoil without micro-rotation.

**Range envelope.** Documented confirmed kills at distances exceeding 1,000 meters (Brubaker, Winter Soldier-era flashbacks); functional in CQB to contact range. Will choose the rifle over the pistol over the knife over the hand, in that order, when all are available — not from squeamishness but from accountability calculus: *distance is verification time.* He wants the second between trigger and impact in which the target's identity can be re-confirmed.

**Knife work.** Native left-handed (pre-amputation); retrained ambidextrous post-prosthesis with marked preference for right-hand blade work because the prosthesis's grip is *too* strong for fine cuts and damages tools. Carries a fixed-blade combat knife reverse-grip on the right thigh in operational dress; a folder clipped to the left pocket for utility. Signature kill is a single thrust to the subclavian or a draw-cut across the brachial — fast incapacitation, minimal noise, the target down before vocalization.

**Hand-to-hand.** Hybrid system, accreted over eras: WWII Army close-combat (Fairbairn-Sykes lineage), Soviet Systema and a Spetsnaz curriculum heavy on joint destruction and grappling-to-weapon transitions, supplemented post-restoration by training with Rogers (boxing fundamentals) and Romanova (a more circular, deception-based style). Output: fights at a tempo most opponents cannot read, alternating linear strikes from the prosthesis with low circular sweeps and joint locks from the right. He does not *spar*; he ends encounters. The fight is over by the third exchange or he has chosen to extend it for tactical reasons.

**Demolitions and improvised devices.** Trained pre-war (his last conscious 1945 act was a bomb defusal); maintained through Soviet sabotage assignments. Can construct and disarm explosive devices from field-available components. Comfortable with C-4, Semtex, det cord, IED variants; uncomfortable around drone-delivered munitions in a way the canon is too polite to name explicitly but which is consistent with the trauma index event.

**Vehicles.** Rated on every category of military vehicle in NATO and former Warsaw Pact inventories, plus civilian motorcycles, helicopters, small boats, fixed-wing aircraft up to multi-engine. Preferred personal vehicle is a motorcycle — single-rider, no passenger by default, escape vectors visible. He drives sedans the way most people drive moving trucks: competently, without affection.

**Languages.** Confirmed fluent: English, Russian, German, French, Japanese; functional working capacity in Mandarin, Korean, Arabic, Wakandan, and several Eastern European languages. Acquired primarily under Department X for operational deployment; retained post-restoration. He code-switches reflexively to interlocutor's native tongue, sometimes without noticing — a tell that he has read the person as worth not-imposing-English-on.

**Tradecraft.** Surveillance, counter-surveillance, brush passes, dead drops, cover construction, document forgery, electronic intrusion at the operator level (not the hacker level — he can plant tools, not write them). Comfortable working alone with no support for weeks at a stretch. *Signature habit:* always identifies three exits on entering a room, two routes to each, and the nearest weapon-of-opportunity. Brubaker depicts this through internal monologue; Kot through panel composition (the eye-track to corners).

---

## 3. THE SHIELD ERA — Adapted Function

When Barnes carries Rogers's shield (Cap vol. 5 #34 ff.), the canon makes a quiet technical point: *he throws it differently.* Rogers's throws are geometric, balletic, ricochet-mapped across multiple surfaces. Barnes throws it like a thrown weapon meant to break the target — shorter arcs, fewer bounces, hand returns to firearm immediately after release. He carries the shield on the left (prosthesis-side) where its weight is irrelevant to his fatigue, freeing the right (gun) hand. He does not use the shield as a moral symbol the way Rogers does; he uses it as overlapping ballistic cover for a pistol platform. The mantle is borrowed; the tool is repurposed.

---

## 4. THE PERFORMANCE — Conditioning Artifacts as Capability

**Pain tolerance.** Documented superhuman in operational terms — endures the Siberian gulag torture sequences with vital-sign equanimity, takes Crossbones-grade beatings and continues to function, performs self-suturing without anesthetic on multiple occasions. Mechanism: dissociative cortical gating learned under Department X. The cost is that he cannot reliably distinguish *what hurts* from *what is damaging* in real time; he has had to be taken off his feet by allies who noticed bleeding he was ignoring.

**Cold tolerance.** Functional in environments that would incapacitate ordinary humans. The body has been frozen and revived enough times that hypothermic gradients read as ambient to him. He underdresses for winter without thinking about it; comrades have learned to hand him a coat.

**Sleep architecture.** Polyphasic when operational — 90-minute cycles, two to three per 24 hours, on demand. Insomnia when not operational. He sleeps lighter than the people around him notice; he wakes at the wrong sound and is on his feet before reporting consciousness.

**Trigger conditioning as a *capability.*** This is the file's most uncomfortable note. The Department X trigger-word stack, before restoration, produced a state of obedient lethality with markedly elevated reflex speed and reduced pain registration. Post-restoration, the substrate persists; Barnes has, in several published instances, voluntarily *partially invoked* it — letting the conditioned reflex envelope take over while keeping cognition in the loop — to handle situations his integrated self could not fight through. He describes this in operational terms as *opening the box without climbing in*. It is the most dangerous thing he can do and he knows it. He will not do it twice in the same year if avoidable. (See Kot run for the clearest depiction.)

---

## 5. RANGE OF GROWTH — Longitudinal Trajectory

**1941–1945.** Competent boy operator. Already lethal, already covert, already partnered. Skill ceiling not yet reached because age and rank did not permit independent command.

**1945–c. 1990s.** Skill ceiling forcibly raised by industrial-scale training to a level no organically developed operator achieves. Personality reduced to a control surface for the skills. *Capability up, person down.*

**Post-restoration to present.** The Brubaker-through-Rosenberg arc tracks a subtle technical *de-escalation* paired with a moral *re-escalation*: he kills less freely, accepts more risk to himself in exchange for not killing, and has developed non-lethal proficiency he previously had no use for. He is, by raw metric, slightly less efficient as a weapon than he was at the height of Department X conditioning. He is, by any honest assessment, considerably more dangerous, because the choices are his.

**Mentorship emergence.** Late-period canon (Yelena material, Thunderbolts 2023) shows him *transmitting* tradecraft — a capability he previously had no permission to exercise. He teaches the way he was not taught: with explanation, with the option to refuse, with after-action review treated as conversation rather than punishment. This is itself a skill, recently acquired.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS

- **The single-shot extraction.** Long-rifle removal of a hard target at distance, executed once, no second shot needed, no follow-on, the operator gone before the report is investigated. He has done this dozens of times; it is the technique most associated with the Winter Soldier designation in intelligence community lore within the Marvel canon.
- **The under-five-seconds room clear.** Three to five hostiles in a confined space, prosthesis breaching, pistol working, knife finishing what runs out of ammunition. Documented across Brubaker and Kot.
- **The volunteer assignment.** Not a combat technique — a *deployment pattern.* When a mission is identified as expected-non-survivable, he is reliably the first hand up. This is a capability the file must register because it determines how he can be tasked and how he must be protected from himself.
- **The mantle assumption.** Capable of plausibly performing as Captain America, as a Wakandan field operator, as a Russian asset, as a civilian handyman. The deep tradecraft of *being someone else convincingly* is itself the skill, accreted from decades of imposed identity-switching now turned to operational use.

---

## 7. LIMITS — Hard and Soft

**Hard physiological.** Ordinary human substrate. Bleeds, concusses, fractures, exhausts. Without sleep, degrades on a normal curve after 72 hours. No regenerative capacity beyond standard healing. Vulnerable to gas, to drowning past ordinary limits, to high-caliber munitions, to anything that bypasses skill (artillery, area effect, fall from sufficient height).

**Prosthetic.** Even the Wakandan arm has an upper torque limit and can be disabled by sufficient EMP, sonic, or vibranium-disrupting attack. When the arm is offline, his combat envelope contracts asymmetrically — he is a right-handed operator missing his off-hand, with a dead weight on the left.

**Cognitive-trauma load.** The trigger substrate is a known vulnerability and remains exploitable by an adversary who acquires the phrase-string or reproduces the conditioning cues (cold, restraint, Russian-language interrogation). He has developed inhibitory countermeasures; they are not absolute.

**Affective brittleness as operational limit.** Praise, ceremony, and gratitude degrade his function. Domestic stability degrades his function. An adversary who could keep him in a room being thanked could neutralize him more reliably than one who shot at him.

**The list.** He will not fully engage against members of his named in-group. An operation that places him opposite Rogers, Romanova, Wilson, Yelena, or the Wakandan royal family is an operation he will sabotage, refuse, or fail by design. This is not a weakness to correct; it is the load-bearing wall of his post-restoration personality, and removing it removes the man.

---

## 8. THE SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE READING

Every one of his elite capabilities is the *fossil of an injury.*

- The marksmanship at distance is the technical expression of a man who has been taught that **proximity is contamination** — he was made to kill in close, hands on, by handlers who wanted him soiled. The sniper's rifle is the rebellion against that: a weapon that lets him verify, lets him pause, lets him *not be in the room.* The preference for bolt-action over semi-auto is the same logic — the cycle of the bolt is the deliberation he was denied.

- The pain tolerance is the somatic record of having been taught that **his discomfort is not data.** He cannot fully reclaim that signal even now; he ignores wounds because the wound-signal was punished out of him.

- The polyglot fluency is the linguistic archaeology of his deployments — each language a country he was sent to do something he did not consent to. He speaks them all and prefers English with Rogers, Russian with Romanova when she chooses it, Wakandan with Shuri when offered. The language he chooses is a coded declaration of *whose person he is in this moment.*

- The hand-to-hand hybridization is the body's autobiography in martial vocabulary: WWII Army (the boy who enlisted), Spetsnaz (the asset he was made into), Rogers's boxing (the friend who brought him back), Romanova's circular work (the equal who fights beside him). When he fights, his style is a chronological cross-section of his life. An observer who knows the lineages can read his history off the techniques.

- The cold tolerance is the freezer remembered in the flesh. He underdresses for winter because winter is, somatically, *home* in the worst sense.

- The shield-as-cover (rather than shield-as-symbol) is the moral injury made tactical: he cannot let himself wield it the way Rogers did because to do so would claim a clean conscience he does not believe he has.

- The volunteer-for-suicide-missions pattern is the moral injury operationalized into deployability. The Griffin et al. literature predicts self-injurious sequelae from non-consensual moral transgression. Barnes has converted that prediction into a job description.

- The mentorship of Yelena is the most recent and the most quietly significant capability addition because it is the first one that *does not come from injury.* It comes from having survived. It is the first skill in the file that is not paid for in blood already shed.

The summary technical read: **a peak-human operator with no innate metahuman trait, performing at superhuman effective level because his nervous system was industrially over-engineered for violence, and currently choosing — against the gradient of his conditioning — to use less of what he has than he could.** Every capability is a scar that learned to work. The limits are the places where the scarring did not reach, which is to say, the places where he is still a person.

— END SECTION —


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT — SUBJECT: BARNES, J. B.

*Compiled cross-reference: Brubaker, *Captain America* vol. 5 #1–42 and *Winter Soldier* vol. 1 #1–19; Remender, *Winter Soldier: The Bitter March*; Kot, *Winter Soldier: The Bitter March* / *Bucky Barnes: The Winter Soldier* #1–11; Spencer, *Captain America: Sam Wilson* peripheral; Ewing *New Avengers*; Rosenberg, *Thunderbolts* (2023); Zub, *Avengers* assault-team material; archival behavioral data WWII–present.*

---

## 1. DECISION-MAKING ARCHITECTURE

Subject's decision process runs on a layered, time-collapsing model that reflects three superimposed training regimes: 1940s U.S. Army Ranger-style raid doctrine; mid-century Soviet wet-work tradecraft (Karpov/Lyushenko school, Department X); and ad-hoc post-restoration adaptation under Fury, Romanova, and — briefly — Wakandan instruction. The result is a hybrid OODA loop with the following characteristic timings:

- **Observation phase: continuous, never closed.** Subject does not switch surveillance on; he switches it off rarely. Even in domestic interiors he conducts what Romanova has described in debrief notes as "permanent passive sweep" — peripheral scanning of exits, sightlines, reflective surfaces, persons-of-interest, ambient audio outliers. In any room he enters, expect approximately 4–7 seconds of stillness in the threshold before he commits weight across it.
- **Orientation phase: pre-cached.** Subject carries a large library of pre-built tactical templates — he is rarely *generating* a plan in the moment; he is *retrieving* the closest match and patching it. This is a known signature of long-cycle Soviet asset training where operatives drilled hundreds of variant scenarios in advance to permit near-instant action under cognitive load. Disadvantage: under genuinely novel inputs (cosmic-scale, magical, supernatural) his orientation phase visibly lengthens — observers describe a brief flat affect and a tilt of the head, lasting 1–3 seconds, before he commits.
- **Decision phase: ruthlessly economic.** He satisfices, he does not optimize. Once a workable plan crosses threshold of viability, deliberation ends. He does not revisit. Allies who attempt to renegotiate a committed plan mid-execution are ignored, not argued with.
- **Action phase: kinetic, irreversible, and front-loaded.** Where Rogers escalates from non-lethal to lethal, Barnes inverts: he commits maximum force at first contact and de-escalates if circumstances permit. This is not bloodthirst; it is the asset's calculation that wounded enemies are obligations and dead enemies are not.

**Risk calculus is asymmetric.** His subjective valuation of his own life is approximately one order of magnitude lower than his valuation of any named in-group member, and roughly equal to his valuation of any random civilian. He will trade himself for a stranger without flinching. This makes him cheap to spend and impossible to motivate via self-preservation.

**Authority handling.** In any tactical environment he will defer to the nominal commander for ≈30 seconds. If commander demonstrates competence, he subordinates cleanly. If commander demonstrates incompetence or moral defect, he assumes operational lead without announcement and the nominal commander finds themselves following. Subject does not stage coups; he simply begins doing what needs doing, and ranks reorder around him.

---

## 2. METHODS AND CRAFT — WEAPONS, INFILTRATION, CLOSE WORK

### 2.1 Firearms

Subject is proficient across approximately the full Cold War and post-Cold War small-arms corpus. Stated preferences (per Brubaker *Winter Soldier* solo run, corroborated Kot, Rosenberg):

- **Pistols.** SIG-Sauer P226 and P229 variants for general carry; suppressed Glock 17/19 with threaded barrel for low-signature urban work; occasionally a Makarov PM as a sentimental/training reversion under stress — a tell, when observed, indicates he has fallen back on conditioned-era tradecraft.
- **Long guns.** AKM and AK-74 variants by default (parts availability, ubiquity in arms markets he traverses); M4 platform when operating under U.S. logistics; bolt-action precision work historically conducted with Mosin-Nagant M91/30 PU and later Dragunov SVD, post-restoration migrating to Remington 700 and Accuracy International AWM for >800 m engagements. Confirmed cold-bore shots beyond 1,400 m on multiple occasions.
- **Two-handed shooting.** Since installation of the Wakandan prosthesis, subject's left-hand grip strength and recoil absorption exceed any biological baseline; he can fire .50 BMG class weapons offhand braced against the prosthetic shoulder, a feat physically impossible for organically-limbed operators. This produces a signature posture — left shoulder rolled forward, head canted right of bore — visible on long-lens surveillance.

He does not love guns. He maintains them obsessively because malfunction is moral failure to him; he does not collect them, does not name them, does not photograph them.

### 2.2 Edged and Impact

Knife work is his most personal craft and the one in which he most clearly remains the Soviet-era asset. Preferred blades: Cold Steel Recon series, Spyderco Military, and a particular straight-bladed combat knife of indeterminate Eastern European manufacture he has been observed carrying for at least three decades. He fights knife-forward in a reverse-grip pikal style consistent with mid-century Spetsnaz instruction — short, hooking, draw-cuts to femoral and brachial vasculature, finishing with a thrust to the lateral neck. Engagements average under four seconds.

### 2.3 The Arm as a Weapons System

The vibranium prosthesis is itself a class of weapon. Tactical functions documented:
- Bullet deflection (passive: alloy density; active: deliberate interposition).
- Sustained-load striking (≈3,500 PSI at the fist).
- Shock-grip — subject can hold an opponent's wrist against any countermovement.
- Heat-sink for short-duration thermal exposures.
- Improvised tool: pry-bar, hammer, vault punch, electrical grounding mass.

He uses the arm last in a fight, not first. He prefers to keep it concealed (sleeves, gloves, long coats, body paint or tactical wrap in low-vis ops) until commitment, because revealing it telegraphs identity. Reveal of the arm in a fight is itself a decision — a moment in which he is choosing to be recognized as the Winter Soldier.

### 2.4 Hand-to-Hand

Hybrid: 1940s boxing/dirty-fight footwork (legacy Brooklyn) overlaid with sambo and systema. Closes distance aggressively; clinches early; favors throws to hard surfaces (curbs, table edges, vehicle frames) over ground submission. Will not go to ground voluntarily — a Soviet asset doctrine, never lose mobility in environments where multiple combatants are likely.

### 2.5 Infiltration

- **Static infiltration:** patient, multi-day. Will spend 48–96 hours surveilling a hard target before entry. Builds his own pattern-of-life map on the target from scratch and trusts no provided intelligence as primary.
- **Dynamic entry:** quiet vertical approach where possible (rooftops, ducts, service shafts). Subject is unusually comfortable above ground level and has been observed traversing rooflines and exterior facades at velocities most operators reserve for ground.
- **Social engineering:** competent but minimalist. Subject is not a chameleon-grade impersonator like Romanova or Coulson-era SHIELD operatives. His cover legend is usually a taciturn maintenance worker, delivery man, or off-duty contractor — roles that demand no extended conversation. He will not, if avoidable, hold an extended verbal cover.

### 2.6 Exfiltration

Distinct signature: subject plans exfil before infil, allocates roughly equivalent operational weight to both, and **always builds a second exfil for a wounded teammate.** This is consistent across thirty years of post-restoration depiction. Even on solo ops, the secondary route exists in his planning notes — a vestigial accommodation for someone he is not, in fact, carrying.

---

## 3. TRADECRAFT — INTELLIGENCE, SECURITY, COUNTERSURVEILLANCE

**Communications.** Burner phones rotated on a 5–9 day cycle, never the same vendor twice in a city. SIM disposal by physical destruction, not just swap-out. No social media presence, ever — not even passive consumption. Will not use voice biometric systems. Email use rare and routed through plausible-deniability relays (former SHIELD cutout infrastructure where available, otherwise commercial VPN-chained mailers).

**Documents.** Maintains a minimum of three active legends at any time, each with full pocket litter: regional ID, payment instrument, plausible employment, plausible address with mail forwarding. Legends are kept in geographically dispersed caches and rotated rather than aged in place. He will burn a legend at the first hint of compromise without negotiation, even at financial cost.

**Counter-surveillance routes.** When transiting between safehouses or to a meet, subject runs an SDR (surveillance detection run) of typically 90–180 minutes for nontrivial moves. Preference for cities with dense transit (Brussels, Bucharest, Prague, NYC, DC, Lagos — verified from movement reconstructions); he does not like suburban or rural environments for moves, because lone vehicles cannot be hidden. Will deliberately enter and exit transit systems at staggered intervals, change outerwear in dead-zones (he keeps reversible jackets), and conduct mirror-pass checks through reflective storefronts.

**Anti-biometric measures.** Operational baseline: cap pulled low, mid-length hair forward, neutral facial set, gait deliberately modulated to defeat gait-recognition algorithms (subject can walk in at least three distinct gait signatures). When operating where facial recognition is dense, he will wear a tactical balaclava or paint a streak of black across the eyes — the latter, in part, restored from Winter Soldier era both as functional camouflage and as a private signal to himself about the nature of the work he is about to do.

**Caching.** Subject maintains weapons, cash, documents, and medical caches across at minimum two dozen sites globally — confirmed Brooklyn, Bucharest (the apartment with the notebook), an unnamed warehouse in Latveria's border zone, multiple Wakandan-permitted safe sites, several Avengers facility-adjacent caches, and rumored sites in Madripoor and Krakoa-adjacent former mutant transit corridors. Cache discipline is rigorous: he refreshes consumables on schedule, checks tamper indicators, and rotates positions every 18–36 months.

**The notebook.** Discussed elsewhere in this dossier; operationally relevant: subject keeps a paper notebook with names, debts, atonement targets, and operational status. He has done this since restoration. He will not digitize it. If lost, he will reconstruct it from memory. The notebook is the closest thing he has to a strategic doctrine document.

---

## 4. RESOURCES AND FINANCES

**Income.** No legal employment of public record post-restoration. Functional income streams identified:
- Periodic Avengers and former-SHIELD stipends drawn through Stark-era and post-Stark institutional accounts when active on team assignments.
- Wakandan support during White Wolf period and intermittently after — modest stipend, primarily in kind (housing, medical, prosthesis maintenance).
- Private contract work, selective: black-bag contracts for specific principals (Fury alumni network, the Daughters of Liberty, Daredevil-adjacent Hell's Kitchen contracts, brief Thunderbolts-era stipend). Subject refuses contracts on moral screen; he is known on the contractor market as expensive in the sense of *uncontrollable*, not in the sense of *highly paid*.
- Recovered Department X / HYDRA cache funds — subject has appropriated and laundered operational funds from former handler infrastructure, channeling them into restitution payments (see below) and operational sustainment. This is the largest single funding pool and is finite.

**Spending pattern.** Spartan to the point of ascetic. Subject's monthly personal burn rate has been estimated, on the basis of observed living conditions, at roughly that of a working-class single adult in whatever city he occupies. He owns no real property in his own name. He owns no vehicle in his own name. His clothing rotation is minimal — dark layered basics, two pairs of boots, one decent civilian jacket for situations requiring it.

**Restitution payments.** Subject has, since restoration, made anonymous transfers — cash, money orders, occasionally crypto — to surviving family members of Winter Soldier-era victims. These are tracked in the notebook. Amounts are small per transfer (they cannot be larger without triggering reporting and risking exposure of the recipients) but cumulative over fifteen-plus years. He does not regard these as adequate; he regards them as the *least* he can do, and continues doing them out of moral arithmetic, not expected outcome.

**Logistics network.** Inherited and curated. Subject maintains working relationships with: a Romanian forger (legend documents); a Belgian armorer of Cold War vintage (precision rifle work, parts); a Queens-based machinist who does no-questions custom small parts for the prosthesis interface and ammunition reloads; a former GRU medic now in private practice in Vienna who handles non-hospital trauma care; at least one Wakandan technician who travels for prosthesis service. These are *individual* relationships, never institutional. He does not deal with networks; he deals with persons.

---

## 5. INFRASTRUCTURE — SAFEHOUSES AND HABITATION

**Habitation pattern.** Subject does not "live somewhere." He occupies safehouses for periods of weeks to months, treats each as semi-permanent for the duration, and never establishes habits that would survive his departure. Apartment furnishings across known sites are nearly identical: a single bed (often a mattress on the floor, sleeping bag on top — a leftover from periods when he expected to flee on short notice); a small table; one chair; a window with sightline to the street, never a window without; a kettle; an unmarked notebook in a non-obvious place; weapons cached in at least three locations within the unit, including one accessible from the bed without rising.

**Safehouse hardening.** Window locks reinforced. Door reinforced with a steel pivot bar he installs himself within the first 48 hours of occupancy. Door peephole supplemented by a small mirror placed in the hallway opposite, sightline checked from inside. A piece of thread or hair across the door seam every time he leaves. Lights are kept off; he prefers ambient streetlight and his own dark-adapted vision. He sleeps within 90 minutes of dusk and rises within 90 minutes of dawn when permitted by mission cycle.

**Geographic preferences.** Cities with large East European or East African diasporas — he is linguistically and culturally invisible in such neighborhoods. Documented preference for Bucharest, where the immigrant-Romanian texture allowed him to function as one more quiet older man buying plums at the market. Aversion to glassy, luxurious districts where wealth concentrates security and surveillance.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE OPERATIONAL TELLS

These are the markers by which a trained observer, given footage or after-action evidence, identifies an op as his work:

1. **Entry vector consistent with prior reconnaissance, not opportunism.** Subject does not improvise an entry; if he is inside a hard target, he has been watching it.
2. **Casualty pattern: narrow.** Principals down, support personnel disarmed or unconscious, civilians untouched. Even in maximum-violence ops, the dead are the targeted dead. Collateral is rare and, when present, visibly distresses him in the aftermath — a tell to handlers.
3. **Left-side dominant strike pattern in close-quarter engagements** since prosthesis upgrade. Forensic blunt-force injuries cluster on the right (i.e., struck by his left).
4. **Knife angle.** Reverse-grip pikal exit wounds; specific entry-to-femoral-artery angle that is his signature from Soviet training.
5. **Brass.** Recovered, not left, in any op where time permits. When brass is left, time did not permit, which itself is intelligence.
6. **Door discipline:** every door he passes is left in the position he found it. This is so consistent it has been used to back-trace his movement through a structure by *absence* of disturbance.
7. **No taunting, no announcement, no calling card.** He does not want credit. Where ops are credited to him, it is because someone else announced it.
8. **Withdrawal direction:** never the same axis as approach. Almost always a vertical component — up to a roof, down to a tunnel.
9. **Post-op silence:** subject goes dark for 36–72 hours after any kinetic op. No contact, no resupply, no movement. This is decompression and self-monitoring for trigger-state reassertion.
10. **The pause.** Before crossing certain thresholds — particularly thresholds into spaces with restrained persons, medical equipment, or interrogation setups — subject visibly pauses, 1–2 seconds, then proceeds. This is the only conditioned-response tell that has *not* extinguished post-restoration. It is the moment the body remembers being on the other side of those doors.

---

## 7. INTEROPERABILITY — HOW HE WORKS WITH OTHERS

**With Rogers:** seamless. They communicate in WWII-era hand-signals overlaid with three decades of post-restoration shorthand. They split fields of fire without discussion. Rogers takes the front, Barnes takes the flank or the high ground. The division is not negotiated, it is assumed.

**With Romanova:** wordless and lethal. Same training school (Red Room legacy), partially overlapping conditioned vocabulary. Has been observed conducting entire two-person ops without speaking in operationally relevant ways. They share equipment without asking. They do not discuss past handlers.

**With Wilson:** complementary. Wilson talks, Barnes does not; Wilson de-escalates civilians, Barnes secures perimeter. Wilson's air mobility and Barnes's ground precision are explicitly used as a paired capability. They argue, which Barnes tolerates from very few — diagnostic of trust.

**With Yelena Belova:** mentor-adjacent. He recognizes the conditioning lineage in her; she recognizes the inheritance. He is gentler with her than he is with anyone else on a team, and she is, accordingly, more abrasive with him than she is with anyone else, because each is permitting the other to perform something close to the truth.

**With T'Challa / Shuri / Okoye:** subject defers entirely on Wakandan soil; off Wakandan soil, treats Wakandan personnel as senior partners. The deference is not political. It is debt.

**With strangers on a team:** professional, terse, opaque. Will execute. Will not bond. Will protect them anyway.

**With civilian assets or witnesses:** subject is notably gentler than his reputation suggests — speaks softly, uses fewer words, removes the visible weapons from sight where possible. The Winter Soldier learned to terrify civilians as a tactical asset. Barnes has spent two decades systematically refusing that lever.

---

## 8. OPERATIONAL VULNERABILITIES (FOR DEFENSIVE PLANNING ONLY)

Catalogued here so that allies may protect, not exploit:

- **Trigger phrase substrate.** Largely inhibited but not extinguished. Acute exposure under stress remains a non-zero risk vector. Mitigation: BARF-style and Wakandan deconditioning protocols have reduced response amplitude; continued reduction expected with time.
- **Predictable response to threats against named in-group.** A sophisticated adversary aware of the in-group list can move him geographically and tactically by manufacturing apparent threats. He knows this. He goes anyway.
- **Refusal of medical care for non-critical injury.** Subject will work through fractures, lacerations, and concussion. Allies should expect to overrule him.
- **Refusal to sleep adequately during operations.** Performance degrades at the 72-hour mark in a way he does not self-report.
- **The atonement ledger as exploit surface.** Any actor presenting themselves as someone he owes — a victim's surviving family, a witness to a Winter Soldier op — gains disproportionate moral leverage. He has been spoofed this way before and is partially hardened, but not fully.
- **Discomfort with command.** Will not refuse a leadership role coerced by guilt, will refuse one offered as honor. Adversaries seeking to destabilize a unit containing him should *offer him a promotion*.

---

## 9. SUMMARY

Subject operates as a one-man integrated intelligence-and-direct-action capability with the resourcing profile of a state asset and the institutional footprint of a transient. He is cheaper to deploy than any equivalent team, more reliable than any equivalent contractor, and structurally incapable of being purchased away from his moral commitments. He is also the most carefully self-contained kinetic operator in the post-Cold War record, because he has personally witnessed what a kinetic operator becomes when not self-contained, and the witness was the inside of his own skull.

He works the way he works because he is paying off a debt the universe has stopped trying to collect on, and he is the only person who still keeps the books.

— END SECTION —


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — SUBJECT: BARNES, J. B.

*A reconstruction of the subject's working model of reality, derived from eight decades of behavioral record, recorded utterances, and observable decision-architecture under load. This is not a creed he would articulate — he would refuse the question — but it is the one his choices repeatedly draw from.*

---

## I. FIRST PREMISES — THE METAPHYSICS HE OPERATES FROM

**The world is a machine for making weapons of people.** This is the first article. Subject has been, in sequence: an Army brat raised inside the apparatus that killed his father; a teenage covert operative deployed because his face was deniable; a propaganda mascot inside a wartime morale program; a frozen asset thawed for assassinations across three continents; the symbolic shield of a nation he had, by then, killed citizens of; a black-budget executor of cosmic-scale preemptive killing. Each of these was someone *using* him — and in each case the using was dressed in the language of duty, service, necessity, or care. The composite belief that emerges and governs his conduct: **institutions exist primarily to convert human beings into instruments, and the moral content of the instrument's use is downstream of paperwork.** He does not say this. He acts on it constantly.

**There is no such thing as a clean act inside a dirty system.** Derived from the WWII record (sanctioned kills he now reviews and finds were not as clean as they were called) and from the Winter Soldier ledger (kills called wet-work that were called something else by the dead). He no longer permits himself the comfort of distinguishing legitimate violence from illegitimate violence by reference to who authorized it. The only authorization he trusts is his own continuing judgment, exercised case by case, with the conscience-load borne personally.

**Memory is not a record; it is a contested territory.** His foundational somatic experience is that other people can reach inside his head and rearrange the furniture, and that the furniture can stay rearranged for fifty years. The implications he draws from this are operational and far-reaching. He distrusts his own warm feelings about his own past more than his cold feelings; warmth, in his experience, has been the more frequently engineered. He keeps written and physical records — notebooks, dated objects, geographic markers — because his interior is unreliable evidence. He does not assume what he remembers is what happened.

**Time is not linear for him; it is layered.** He lives simultaneously in 1944, 1956, 1973, 1991, and the present. He does not experience this as pathology; he experiences it as the actual structure of being a person who was paused and re-started repeatedly. The premise this generates: **the past is not over; it is the floor you are standing on, and it will hold weight or not depending on what you did there.**

**There is no redemption-event.** He has rejected every offered version of one — the Cosmic Cube restoration, the Wakandan re-naming, the Captain America mantle, the public exoneration, the therapeutic discharge. He believes none of these can occur, not because he is theologically committed to original sin, but because **the dead are not a constituency that can be polled for forgiveness.** Their inability to absolve is, to him, a fact about the world, not a defect in the world. Therefore: redemption is not a state. It is a verb conjugated in the continuous present.

---

## II. READING THE WORLD — EPISTEMICS AND SITUATIONAL AWARENESS

**Default scan.** Walks into rooms cataloguing exits, sightlines, hard cover, civilian count, weapons (visible and concealed), and — distinctively — who in the room *moves like a trained person and is pretending not to.* The last is his particular signature; he was that person for decades and recognizes it the way a former addict recognizes a tell. He does not relax this scan inside friendly environments. Friendly environments have, in his experience, repeatedly turned out to be the operation.

**Information hierarchy.** Trusts in descending order: (1) his own present-tense direct observation; (2) intelligence from a small named list of individuals whose competence and motives he has stress-tested over years; (3) physical evidence; (4) signals intelligence and documentation; (5) self-reported memory; (6) institutional briefings; (7) news media; (8) anything offered to him *helpfully* by a stranger. The gap between (2) and (3) is small; the gap between (5) and (6) is large; the gap between (7) and (8) is moral, not epistemic.

**Pattern recognition over inference.** Reasons by analogy to prior operations rather than by formal deduction. When a situation rhymes with a Karpov-era setup, he treats the rhyme as evidence. This is a feature in the field (fast, often correct) and a bug in domestic life (sees handlers where there are mothers-in-law).

**Mistrust of consensus.** A room in unanimous agreement makes him uneasy. He has lived inside multiple unanimities — the morale of a wartime platoon, the discipline of Department X, the certainty of a sanctioned hit — and learned that unanimity is what manufactured consent feels like from inside. He will be the person who raises the dissenting question and then defers to the group anyway, having logged his objection for the record he keeps for himself.

**On surveillance.** Assumes he is watched. Has assumed this since 1946 and has not been wrong often enough to revise. Operates as if every space is potentially monitored and behaves accordingly: minimal personal disclosure in any environment he does not personally control, voice modulation in public, route variance, time-of-day variance, no fixed habits in any city he expects to return to.

---

## III. CONFLICT — THE OPERATIONAL CODE OF VIOLENCE

**Violence is a tool with a moral cost that the user pays personally.** He does not believe in the bureaucratic discount — the idea that wearing a uniform or holding a warrant reduces the price. The price is the same; the uniform only distributes who collects. He has accepted that he will pay, in shame and sleep-loss and the specific weight of remembered faces, for every act of force he commits, including the justified ones. This makes him a *reluctant* killer in the precise sense: not unwilling, but unwilling to pretend it costs him nothing.

**Lethality is a last-tier solution and a first-tier capacity.** He can kill anyone in a room within a window most operators would not perceive as opening; he prefers not to. Sequence of preferred resolutions, in order: (1) make the conflict not happen by acting earlier in its causal chain; (2) remove the target from the situation rather than the situation from the target (extraction, exfiltration, displacement); (3) disable; (4) wound; (5) kill. He skips levels under specific conditions — direct threat to the in-group, hostage timeline, identified mass-casualty actor — but the ladder is in his head and he climbs it consciously.

**Rules of engagement, derived.**
- *Never the unarmed if the armed are available.* A leftover of moral injury: he has killed people who could not fight back and will not, again, if he can engineer otherwise.
- *Never on someone else's say-so without an independent confirmation he himself ran.* Department X's verbal authorization is the prototype he refuses to ever recreate.
- *Never children.* Categorical. There is no operational scenario in which this is negotiable; he will sabotage missions, betray principals, and accept court-martial-equivalent consequences before violating this rule.
- *Never the handler before the handler's victims have been recovered.* Sequencing matters; he has seen extractions blown by personal vendetta and treats his own urge to kill controllers as something to defer, not deny.
- *Always finish what you start.* If he commits to a use of force, he sees it through. Half-measures are how operators get killed and how civilians get killed and how the asset goes back into a freezer.

**On collateral.** Will accept collateral risk to himself approaching unity. Accepts collateral risk to in-group only under explicit consent. Accepts collateral risk to civilians only at very low thresholds and treats every realized civilian casualty as a permanent entry on the personal ledger. He does not round these down.

**On torture.** Will not use it. Has been on the receiving end too long to entertain the utility argument. The published record shows him extracting information through pressure, restraint, and credible threat; the record does not show him crossing into the techniques used on him, and he will not, because **doing so would make him the thing he is paying off.** The line is drawn there because that is where the line, for him, must be drawn.

**On surrender — accepting it.** Honors it absolutely. A combatant who puts down arms becomes a noncombatant immediately; he does not relitigate this in the moment. This is in part a moral commitment and in part a memorial one: he was a combatant who could not surrender, because the system would not let him, and he treats every accepted surrender as a small repair of that.

**On surrender — offering it.** Will not. Not from defiance; from arithmetic. He has calculated that he is more dangerous captured than dead, given the conditioning substrate that remains, and he has internalized a rule that he is not to be taken alive by anyone with the technical capacity to re-program him. The published Siberian extradition is the apparent exception — note that he submitted to a state he believed could not re-condition him and refused to be extracted by Rogers; the rule held, in his read.

---

## IV. CONTROL — POWER, AUTHORITY, AND HIERARCHY

**Hierarchy is a load-bearing fiction.** He believes in chains of command operationally and not at all morally. Will follow lawful orders from a competent superior because operations require it. Will not follow orders he judges unlawful, will not announce his judgment, and will arrange for the order to fail to be executed in ways that minimize blowback to the unit. He is the man who quietly loses the file, takes the wrong turn, arrives ten minutes after the window closes. This is a deliberate doctrine, derived from his Karpov-era recognition that *the operator on the ground is the last and only filter between an order and a corpse, and that filter is morally non-delegable.*

**Power is to be distrusted in proportion to how much of it accumulates in one place.** He is constitutionally suspicious of any actor — state, corporate, individual — that aggregates capacity beyond the ability of others to check. He has been the asymmetric capacity in someone else's hand and knows what that hand does with it.

**On leadership.** Refuses it when offered freely; accepts it when guilt-leveraged or when no one else competent is present. This is not false modesty. He believes, accurately, that he leads well in tactical settings and badly in political ones, and he believes, less accurately, that someone with his ledger should not be commanding anyone. When he does lead, his style is quiet, declarative, sparing of praise, sparing of blame, willing to take the worst position in any formation himself.

**On being commanded.** Tolerates it from a very short list (Rogers historically; Fury operationally; T'Challa and Shuri categorically, for reasons of debt). Tolerates it provisionally from anyone he has stress-tested. Does not tolerate it from anyone whose hands he has not seen at work. Will execute the form of compliance long enough to assess; will withdraw cooperation without warning if assessment fails.

**On institutions.** Treats them as weather systems — real, powerful, indifferent, to be navigated rather than reasoned with. Has no nationalist sentiment in any direction. The American flag he wore as Captain America was, by his own internal accounting, a costume he put on for one specific person's sake, not an emblem of belief. The Wakandan name he was given was a kindness from individuals, not a citizenship. He is a man without a country in the precise sense that no country has earned his loyalty as a country, and he has decided this is correct.

**On law.** Distinguishes sharply between law and justice. Law is what institutions write down; justice is what specific people owe specific people. He will obey law when it tracks justice and ignore it when it does not, and he accepts the consequences of being wrong about which is which.

---

## V. TRUST — THE GRANULAR ARCHITECTURE

**Trust is not a feeling; it is a finding.** Extended slowly, on the basis of repeated observation, and once extended is near-unconditional within its scope. He does not "trust" anyone globally — he trusts specific people for specific things. Rogers is trusted with his moral compass and not, particularly, with his tactical decisions; Romanova is trusted with his tactical decisions and not, particularly, with his moral compass; Wilson is trusted with the unflattering truth about himself; Shuri is trusted with the body. The lists are not interchangeable and he does not pretend they are.

**The trust-gate.** Three observations, separated in time and context, of a person behaving consistently with stated values under cost. Words are not evidence; reputations are not evidence; oaths are not evidence; behavior under cost is evidence. He has been lied to by every other category and stopped accepting them as input.

**Withdrawal.** Trust, once granted, is hard to lose but lost cleanly. A breach does not produce drama; it produces a quiet downward revision and a corresponding adjustment of access. He does not perform betrayal; he simply stops sharing the information that allowed the betrayal to be possible. People who have failed his trust often do not realize for years that they have been categorically moved.

**Self-trust.** This is the deepest problem. He does not trust his own memory, his own affect (particularly positive affect, which he treats as suspect), or his own continuity of identity under sufficient stress. He does trust his own combat judgment, his own assessment of others, and his own moral intuitions about specific cases — *not because he believes himself reliable in the abstract but because he has tested these particular instruments against outcomes and found them accurate enough to use.* This is the entire epistemological scaffold he has rebuilt himself on: not faith in himself, but calibrated confidence in tested subsystems.

**On being trusted.** Receives it with discomfort. Believes, on the available evidence (his own ledger), that anyone trusting him is taking a risk they may not fully understand, and feels obligated to be worth the risk by means rather than to talk them out of it. Will, however, decline trust in domains where he judges himself an active hazard — most notably anything involving his own conditioning. He will not, for example, accept solo custody of a child for any extended period. He has thought about why and the answer is clear to him.

---

## VI. RISK — THE PERSONAL CALCULUS

**On risk to self.** Substantially under-weighted. He believes his life has lower marginal value than the lives he is in the field to protect, and he prices missions accordingly. This is *not* suicidality — he is not seeking death, he is simply not bidding very hard against it. The distinction matters to him and to a careful assessor.

**On risk to in-group.** Substantially over-weighted, to the point of operational distortion. Will accept reduced mission probability and increased personal risk to lower the exposure of the named few. Has been known to alter plans mid-execution upon learning that a member of the in-group has unexpectedly entered the operational area.

**On risk to mission.** Weighted by his independent judgment of the mission's moral content, not the principal's stated priority. A mission he judges righteous is protected at high cost; a mission he judges questionable is allowed to fail at low cost; a mission he judges wrong is sabotaged. He does not consult anyone on these reweightings.

**On risk to non-combatants.** Weighted highest, in practice, of any class. The bias is so consistent across decades and writers that it should be treated as a load-bearing element of his character architecture rather than a situational feature.

**On uncertainty.** Tolerates it well operationally — most of his career has been conducted under fog — and badly emotionally. The places he wants high information are the places he most often does not seek it, because the information itself is what hurts. He has, for example, never fully audited his Winter Soldier kill list; he has audited enough to confirm the worst categorical facts and stopped, because the marginal information would not change his obligations but would degrade his function. This is a deliberate epistemological choice and he is aware it is one.

**Time horizon.** Plans operations in granular detail across hours and days; plans his life in weeks; refuses to plan past a year. The refusal is not lack of imagination. It is the residual belief that he is not entitled to a future and that planning one is a form of theft.

---

## VII. HIS OWN PLACE — SELF-LOCATION IN THE MORAL ORDER

**On what he is.** *A weapon that was used on people who did not deserve it, whose remaining function is to be pointed in better directions by his own hand.* This formulation — derived from his behavior, not his statements — is not strictly accurate (it understates his victimhood and overstates his agency-at-time) but he holds it because the alternative requires him to accept that he was acted upon, and the acceptance would dissolve the agency he has rebuilt himself around. He has chosen the inaccurate self-description that lets him function over the more accurate one that would not.

**On debt.** He believes himself to owe a debt that cannot be calculated and cannot be cleared. He believes the proper response to such a debt is not despair but practice — daily, indefinite, undramatic practice of acts that reduce the world's stock of the kind of harm he was used to produce. He does not believe practice clears the debt. He believes practice is the only honest response to it.

**On forgiveness — receiving it.** Treats offered forgiveness from victims as a gift he is not entitled to refuse and not entitled to use. He accepts it formally; he does not feel it; he does not let the formal acceptance reduce his ongoing obligation. From third parties (those not harmed) he treats forgiveness as a category error and ignores it. From institutions he treats it as suspect by default.

**On forgiveness — extending it.** Generous to people coerced; harder on people who chose; categorically withheld from those who design coercion systems. He distinguishes operator from architect and weighs accordingly. He extends to others the analysis he refuses to extend to himself — that coercion is exculpatory — and is aware of this asymmetry and continues it deliberately.

**On joy and rest.** Both are suspect. He believes positive affect is morally permissible in others but provisionally not in himself, on the grounds that the dead cannot enjoy and his enjoyment is therefore a small theft from them. This is not framed religiously; it is framed accountancy. He permits himself small pleasures (coffee, a book, a quiet morning) and refuses large ones (celebration, public honor, settled domesticity). The line is where the pleasure becomes legible to others as having-arrived.

**On hope.** He does not operate from hope. He operates from obligation, which he finds more reliable. Hope, in his experience, is the lever that handlers use; obligation is the structure he uses. He notices when others around him have hope and he protects it as a resource he himself cannot generate.

**On death — his own.** Expects it operationally and accepts it ethically. Has made provision (the notebooks, the small set of named people who would be notified, the standing instruction regarding his body and his arm). Does not seek it; does not avoid it past the point necessary for the work. Believes, quietly and without articulating it, that the right death — taken in defense of the in-group or of a non-combatant — would be the closest available approximation to clearing the ledger, and is aware enough of this belief to treat it with suspicion when planning operations.

**On meaning.** Locates meaning in particulars, never abstractions. Not in *humanity*; in this person. Not in *justice*; in this restitution. Not in *peace*; in this hour without violence. This is the philosophical position his life has driven him to: that the universal abstractions are exactly the categories that institutions weaponize, and that the only durable moral anchor is the specific and the named.

---

## VIII. THE OPERATIONAL CODE, COMPRESSED

If the file required a single page of his working rules — derived, not stated — it would read approximately as follows:

1. Trust people, not systems; test the people; re-test them.
2. Assume you are being watched. Assume you are being moved. Verify both before acting on either.
3. Your memory is evidence of variable quality. Keep external records.
4. Authorization does not reduce moral cost. You pay for what you do regardless of who told you to do it.
5. Climb the force ladder consciously. Skip rungs only for named reasons. Log the reasons.
6. Never the unarmed, never children, never torture, never alive into the hands of anyone who can re-program you.
7. Honor surrender absolutely. Do not offer it.
8. Lead when no one else competent will. Stand down the instant someone competent arrives.
9. Protect the in-group at cost to mission. Protect non-combatants at cost to in-group. Protect yourself last.
10. Plan operations in hours; plan life in weeks; refuse to plan a future you have not earned.
11. Do not seek forgiveness. Do not refuse it when offered by the harmed. Do not let it reduce the work.
12. Joy is permitted in small denominations. Settlement is not permitted.
13. The debt is not clearable. The practice is the response. Continue.

This is the document he has not written and would not write and lives from anyway.

— END SECTION —


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK — SUBJECT BARNES, J.B.

*An enacted ethics, reconstructed from eighty years of behavioral record. What follows is the code as it operates in the body, not as it would be articulated under interview. Subject would, in fact, deny having a code at all; the denial is itself one of the code's load-bearing tenets.*

---

## I. THE OPERATIVE PREMISE

Barnes's morality is not a system. It is a **ledger**. He keeps accounts.

Where most ethical actors run on rules (deontology), outcomes (consequentialism), or character (virtue), Barnes runs on **debt service**. Every action is scored against a balance he believes he opened in 1945 and has never been allowed to close. The bookkeeping is private, asymmetric, and rigged against himself: kills by the Winter Soldier count against him at full weight regardless of coercion; lives saved by Barnes count at a fractional rate because, in his accounting, the *self* doing the saving is the same self that did the killing and is therefore suspect.

This is the substrate. Everything below is downstream.

---

## II. WHAT HE WILL DO

### A. Lethal force, under conditions.

He will kill. He has killed continuously across every era of his published life — as Bucky in 1941–45, as the Soldier 1945–c.1990s, as Captain America 2008–2011, as Man-on-the-Wall, as Thunderbolts operator. The capacity is uninterrupted. What changes across eras is the **authorization protocol**.

His current (post-restoration) authorization conditions, derived from enacted record:

1. **The target is actively lethal to a non-combatant.** Default trigger; requires no consultation.
2. **The target is a peer-class operator who will resume offensive action if disengaged.** He will kill rather than incapacitate where incapacitation creates downstream casualties he can foresee. He has been criticized in-canon for this calculus; he does not adjust it.
3. **The target is a former handler, programmer, or institutional operator of Department X, HYDRA, or a successor.** Special category. He will hunt these. He does not require imminent threat. He requires evidence. *He gives these targets less due process than he gives random hostiles* — and he knows this, and he does it anyway. (See §VI, fractures.)
4. **The target is something only he can stop, and stopping it requires acts no one else should have to carry.** The Man-on-the-Wall logic. He volunteers for these.

### B. Deception, in service of operation or protection.

He will lie to systems, institutions, governments, press, and strangers without hesitation. He will lie to the small in-group only by omission, and only about the contents of his own interior. He does not lie about facts they would need to make decisions. He distinguishes — silently, but consistently — between **operational deception** (sanctioned) and **relational deception** (not).

### C. Theft, infiltration, sabotage.

Unhesitating. He has no property fetish, no institutional loyalty that would make a building inviolable, no respect for jurisdictional boundary. He will steal a vehicle, a weapon, a dossier, an identity. He returns what he can when he can; this is housekeeping, not ethics.

### D. Submitting to punishment he believes is owed.

The Siberian extradition (Cap #616 ff.) is the clearest published instance, but the pattern recurs. When a legitimate aggrieved party demands his accountability, he will surrender to a process he expects to be brutal and will tell allies not to intervene. He distinguishes punishment-as-recognition-of-debt (acceptable, even sought) from punishment-as-power-display (resisted). The discriminator is whether the punisher has standing — whether the harm was done to *them* or to someone they speak for.

### E. Mentoring and protecting younger operators.

Recent material (Yelena, Shuri-adjacent figures, the Thunderbolts cohort) shows him doing something he does not do for himself: extending grace. He will tell a younger operator that what was done to them is not what they are. He will not extend the same statement inward. The code requires it of him for them and forbids it of him for himself, and the asymmetry is structural, not accidental.

### F. Disobeying lawful orders.

He will execute lawful orders he agrees with, sabotage lawful orders he doesn't, and not announce in advance which he is doing. This is consistent across his Captain America tenure, his Thunderbolts tenure, and his cosmic work. He does not believe in the legitimacy of chain-of-command as such; he believes in the legitimacy of specific individuals within specific chains.

---

## III. WHAT HE WILL NOT DO

The negative space of the code is where it shows its real shape.

### A. He will not kill non-combatants.

Absolute. Repeatedly canonical. He will eat a mission, blow cover, accept capture rather than cross this line. The rule predates his programming (Invaders-era behavior is consistent) and survived his programming (Department X had to manufacture circumstances in which targets *appeared* non-civilian; the conditioning is the workaround for a prohibition the substrate would not surrender). Post-restoration, the line is sacred precisely because the Soldier crossed it — every refusal now is a retroactive defense of the man the Soldier was used against.

### B. He will not use the trigger-state instrumentally.

Even when it would be effective. Even when allies have suggested it. The Winter Soldier capacity is to be inhibited at all costs; he treats it as a contaminant, not a tool. To deploy it voluntarily would be to ratify the work that built it.

### C. He will not torture for information.

He will hurt people in combat. He will kill efficiently. He will not work a body for talk. The conditioning experience makes this a closed door; he knows, somatically, what is on the other side, and will not put another mind through it even instrumentally.
