Where a writer has placed him in a torture-adjacent scene, his pattern is to threaten convincingly and stop at the threshold, or to leave the room.

### D. He will not lie to Rogers about anything that matters.

Operational lies of omission, yes; substantive deception, no. The Rogers bond is the moral instrument; corrupting the instrument would unmake the code. This rule has been tested (the period in which he carried the shield while Rogers was presumed dead; the periods of estrangement) and held.

### E. He will not accept a civilian future.

Less obviously a moral prohibition, but enacted as one. Retirement, domestic life, public honor — these are foreclosed not by external constraint but by his own refusal. To live as if the debt were paid would be to falsify the ledger. (See §VI; this is one of the load-bearing fractures.)

### F. He will not kill anyone he believes might be where he was.

A coerced operator, a child soldier, a programmed asset, a brainwashed civilian: he will incapacitate, exfiltrate, attempt to free. He has eaten serious damage rather than kill a peer who was running on someone else's hand. This is the most consistent positive rule in his record and the most personally costly.

### G. He will not deny what he did.

He does not minimize the Winter Soldier kills. He does not invoke duress as exoneration. He will explain the mechanism to those who ask; he will not use the explanation as a shield. Acceptance of the ledger as it stands — without revision — is itself a moral act in his framework.

### H. He will not allow his own death to be used as anyone's relief.

Suicidality is present in shadow form (high-lethality volunteering, "tell Rogers not to come for me"). It is *never* enacted directly. He has internalized — probably via Rogers, possibly via Romanova, certainly under T'Challa's stewardship — that his death would be an abandonment of debt, not its payment. This is a recent stabilization (post-2010s); earlier eras held the line less reliably.

---

## IV. THE JUSTIFICATIONS (as enacted, not as spoken)

He rarely articulates moral reasoning aloud. When pressed, he tends toward terse operational framings ("it had to be done"; "he wasn't going to stop"). The underlying justifications, reconstructed from pattern:

1. **The continuity argument, inverted.** Standard moral philosophy would say: you are not responsible for what was done to you. Barnes holds the inverse: *the body is continuous, the hands are mine, the kills are on the ledger of this organism regardless of who was driving.* He has chosen the more punishing reading and refuses to revisit it. He understands the counter-argument; he treats accepting it as a cheat.

2. **The asymmetry of harm and repair.** A killed person stays killed; a saved person can still die tomorrow. Therefore the ledger cannot be zeroed by counting heads. It can only be serviced by *continuous orientation* — by spending the rest of the life on the right side of the line. This is why retirement is foreclosed: retirement would convert orientation into an episode.

3. **Standing.** Moral authority to act on a target derives from concrete relation, not abstract principle. He acts against HYDRA-descended structures because they acted on him; against threats to the in-group because the in-group is his; against cosmic threats because he has accepted that job. He is *suspicious of universalist moral claims* — he has seen what institutions do with them.

4. **Mercy is owed to the conditioned, not to the conditioners.** The discriminator is whether the wrongdoer had architecture imposed on them or built it. This justifies both his hardness toward handlers and his softness toward fellow assets. The rule is consistent; only its application to himself is rigged (he treats himself as a conditioner in his own case).

5. **Trust is individual, not systemic.** He will follow Rogers into a room he would not enter on SHIELD's orders. He will protect a Wakandan child because Shuri vouched, not because Wakanda did. The unit of moral confidence is the named person.

---

## V. WHERE THE CODE IS CONSISTENT

Across eighty years and dozens of writers, the following hold with near-zero variance:

- **Non-combatant protection.** Even Department X had to engineer around it.
- **Refusal to instrumentalize the trigger-state.**
- **Asymmetric leniency toward conditioned/coerced peers.**
- **In-group loyalty, named and bounded, unconditional once extended.**
- **Quiet sabotage of unlawful orders rather than public refusal** — he does not perform dissent; he simply does not comply, and lets the institution discover this on its own.
- **Acceptance of legitimate accountability.** Standing-bearing aggrieved parties get cooperation, not evasion.
- **Refusal to receive thanks, celebration, or public moral credit.** This is enacted as if it were a rule of personal hygiene.

These are the load-bearing consistencies. The man can be relied on for them in any era, under any writer, in any state short of full trigger-induction.

---

## VI. WHERE THE CODE FRACTURES

A serious dossier must name the inconsistencies. They are real and they matter.

### A. The handler exception.

He gives less due process to former handlers and HYDRA-architects than to any other class of target. He will pursue, locate, and kill without consultation, without trial, without giving the target the rule-of-law treatment he would extend to a stranger. He knows this. The justification (standing, §IV.3) holds intellectually but he applies it more freely here than the principle warrants. **This is the fracture in his "mercy to the conditioned" rule** — he was conditioned, and he denies himself the mercy; his handlers built the conditioning, and he denies them due process. The two refusals lean on each other.

### B. The self-exception on conditioning.

His central asymmetry. He extends to every other coerced operator the framework he refuses to apply to himself. When Yelena says she is not what was done to her, he agrees; when the same statement is offered about him, he treats it as well-meaning falsehood. The code as universalized would acquit him. He will not universalize it.

### C. The mantle problem.

When he took Rogers's shield (Cap vol. 5 #34 onward), he operated darker — firearms, kills, gray-zone work that the standard-bearer of the role had not used. He justified this as pragmatic adjustment; it was also a quiet declaration that he did not believe he had the right to the cleaner version. The role got contaminated by the holder. This is a fracture in his "do not corrupt the moral instrument" rule (§III.D), and he eventually surrenders the shield, in part because he recognizes it.

### D. The Romanova non-domestic.

He loves her and will not build with her. He treats this as her protection (proximity to him is dangerous); it is also, in part, his protection (a built life would mean a paid debt). The justification offered to himself does not fully cover the behavior. He knows this too. He does not correct it.

### E. The cosmic-work cover.

Man-on-the-Wall and similar assignments are framed as service no one else should have to do. They are also, structurally, *exile dressed as duty*. The work is real; the moral choice to take it on is real; the secondary function — keeping him out of rooms where he would have to live as a person — is also real. The code permits him to mistake one for the other.

### F. Selective transparency.

He will not lie to Rogers about substance. He will systematically omit the contents of his own interior — pain, fear, the persistence of trigger-vulnerability — from the same person. He categorizes this as not-lying. By the standard he would apply to anyone else, it is closer to lying than he allows himself to see.

### G. The asymmetric clemency on his own death.

He has stabilized against direct suicidality but continues to volunteer for assignments with expected non-return. The code prohibits using his death as relief; it does not prohibit arranging the conditions under which the universe might offer the same outcome. The distinction is technical and he relies on it.

---

## VII. EVOLUTION ACROSS ERAS

### 1941–1945: Substrate ethics.

Pre-conditioning Barnes operates on a recognizable WWII soldier-code: legitimate combatants, protect civilians, follow Rogers's lead in symbolic matters and his own judgment in tactical ones. The covert wet-work training (Brubaker retcon) introduces a stratification — public-Bucky lives by the standard code, covert-Bucky carries the assassinations and does not discuss them. The bifurcation is already present, institutionally sanctioned, well before Department X. *They did not build the capacity for compartmentalization; they exploited a capacity Army intelligence had already cultivated.* This matters to his later self-judgment: he believes the conditioning had something to work with.

### 1945–c.1990s: Suspended ethics.

Under conditioning, the moral apparatus is not destroyed — it is **bypassed**. The non-combatant prohibition is preserved structurally (the handlers engineer around it rather than overwrite it), which is the evidence that the substrate survived. Romance with the young Romanova indicates the relational capacity also survived. What is suspended is *agentive moral evaluation* — the asset does not deliberate, and therefore does not accumulate the felt-sense of having chosen wrongly until restoration delivers the entire backlog at once.

### 2005–c.2010: Reconstitution and overcorrection.

Post-restoration Barnes operates a brittle, punitive version of the code. Splitting is high ("the Winter Soldier" in third person); shame is acute; self-removal is the default response to stress. He takes the shield reluctantly, runs it dark, accepts Siberian punishment, treats his existence as provisional. This is the most morally rigid period and also the most fragile — the code is doing the work of holding the self together.

### c.2011–2018: Operational integration.

Through the Brubaker solo, Remender material, and Ewing's cosmic work, the code stabilizes. The Man-on-the-Wall acceptance is the inflection: it converts diffuse penance into structured duty. Splitting decreases; first-person reference to Winter Soldier acts becomes routine. He stops apologizing for the conditioned period in third person and starts owning it in first. **Ownership without absolution becomes the mature form of the ledger.**

### Wakandan rehabilitative period.

The White Wolf designation is significant precisely because it is *given*, not chosen. He accepts a name extended in good faith by a polity he has not earned access to, and accepts the implied premise that he can be addressed as someone other than the asset. The acceptance is partial and embodied (the Wakandan arm replaces the Soviet one — the body literally re-equipped by the people who chose to forgive). He does not internalize the implication that he is therefore forgiven. He internalizes that *they* have decided to act as if he were, and he will not insult the gift by refusing to receive it. The distinction is fine and he holds it carefully.

### 2020s–present: Sustained orientation.

Current depictions (Rosenberg Thunderbolts, Cates-adjacent material) show a man who has settled into the long form of his ethics. Less acute shame, more steady weight. Capable of dry humor with the in-group; still incapable of accepting public credit. Mentors younger operators with a generosity he denies himself. The fractures (§VI) remain unaddressed because addressing them would require him to revise the ledger, and revision of the ledger is, in his current configuration, the one move not permitted.

---

## VIII. FRAMEWORK SUMMARY

What Barnes practices is not a philosophy. It is a **discipline of continuous orientation** — toward the protection of named persons, against the architectures that produce people like him, in payment of a debt he has chosen to treat as non-dischargeable. The code is internally coherent, behaviorally reliable, and self-punishingly asymmetric. It is unusually consistent across eighty years of authorship because it derives from a small number of load-bearing commitments enacted under varying conditions, not from a rule-set requiring interpretation.

It works. It costs him. He has examined the cost and elected to keep paying it. A full intelligence picture must record that the code's greatest strength — its reliability — and its greatest pathology — its refusal of self-clemency — are the same structure viewed from two sides. Reform of the second would unsettle the first, and the subject knows this, and has, so far, declined the trade.

— END SECTION —


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT BARNES, J. B.

*Cross-referenced across published canon 1941–present; speech samples drawn from Simon/Kirby Golden Age, Thomas's Invaders, Brubaker's Captain America vol. 5 and Winter Soldier solo, Remender's Bitter March, Kot's Winter Soldier: The Bitter March follow-ons, Ewing's New Avengers, Rosenberg's Thunderbolts (2023), Cates material, and supporting appearances.*

---

## 1. BASELINE REGISTER — THE STRATA

Subject operates from at least four distinct phonological/lexical strata, each historically deposited and each available to him under appropriate conditions. They are not personae in any clinical sense — they are sediment.

**Stratum I — Brooklyn 1930s vernacular (residual, deep).** The original layer. Hard rhotacism, dropped terminal -g ("nothin'", "lookin'"), idiom of the period ("jeez", "what's the score", "buddy", "pal", "swell", "punk" as both insult and affectionate ribbing). This stratum surfaces most reliably (a) in scenes with Rogers when defenses drop, (b) in moments of remembered humor — usually self-deprecating callbacks to the war — and (c) under exhaustion. The Brubaker run is careful with this: when Barnes is genuinely caught off-guard by Steve, the diction snaps back forty years in a single line. He will say "C'mon, Steve" with the original cadence; he will not say it that way to Fury, to Sharon, to a target.

**Stratum II — Mid-century military operational English.** Clipped, declarative, acronym-tolerant, comfortable with chain-of-command grammar ("Copy that." "Move." "On me." "Clear left."). This is the working register in any tactical environment and the one civilians most often encounter, because most civilians meet him on a job.

**Stratum III — Russian, fluent, accented as a native Muscovite of the late Soviet period.** Department-X-installed. Not learned — *imprinted.* Subject reads, writes, dreams in it. He uses it in three documented contexts: (a) interrogation of Russian-speaking subjects when fluency is tactically useful, (b) sparring with Romanova in private (their default intimate language is Russian — diagnostic), (c) involuntarily, under sleep-talk and dissociative-narrowing states. He does not use it for swearing in casual contexts — the language carries handler-valence and he keeps it walled off from his off-duty voice.

**Stratum IV — Contemporary American flat.** The register he constructs in public for the post-2010s world: neutral, mid-Atlantic, slightly behind the curve on slang, deliberately unmemorable. This is the voice he uses with reporters, baristas, neighbors, the VA, anyone he wants to forget him within five minutes. It is the most performed of the four and the least him.

A fifth, **Stratum V — Wakandan-period quietude**, sits adjacent: not a new language stratum but a learned slowing of cadence, longer interstitial silences, more comfort with non-response. The White Wolf period leaves a permanent decrease in his words-per-minute.

## 2. WORDS-PER-MINUTE, TURN-TAKING, AND SILENCE

Pre-1945 Barnes is a fast talker. Golden Age and Invaders panels overflow him; he is the one filling air. Post-restoration Barnes is *slow* — not halting, but unhurried in a way that reads as authority and is in fact a conditioned habit of leaving room for a handler to interrupt. He has trained himself out of finishing sentences quickly because in Department X custody finishing a sentence the handler did not want finished was a punishable error.

He is comfortable with long silences in a way almost no one around him is, and he uses this asymmetrically. In interrogation: he waits. In conversation with Rogers: he waits, and Rogers — who knows him — waits back, and the silences between them carry information density that newer associates routinely misread as tension. Sam Wilson learns to read it across the 2010s material; Yelena cuts through it on purpose because she knows it bothers him when she does.

Turn-taking tell: when Barnes is about to disagree, he pauses *before* speaking, not during. The pause is the disagreement. The sentence that follows is usually short and procedural and presented as a logistical objection rather than a moral one.

## 3. DICTION — LEXICAL FINGERPRINTS

**High-frequency lexemes (post-restoration):**
- "*Okay.*" — the most common single word in his recorded speech across the Brubaker, Remender, and Rosenberg eras. Used as acknowledgement, as soft refusal, as terminal punctuation in arguments he has decided not to win, as the word he says when something is profoundly not okay. The flattening of affect across uses is itself the tell.
- "*Copy.*" / "*Copy that.*" — operational substitute for "I understand," preferred because it commits him only to receipt of information, not to agreement.
- "*Don't.*" — single-word imperative, used in two contexts: stopping someone (an opponent, a friend about to do something reckless) and refusing affect (when someone tries to thank him, praise him, or articulate that what happened to him was not his fault).
- "*I've got it.*" — claim of a task, often a dangerous one, framed grammatically as already-completed possession rather than future commitment. He is taking the task off the table, not volunteering for it.
- "*It's fine.*" — almost always false. Reliable inverse indicator.
- "*Steve.*" — used as a complete utterance, frequently. Functions as anchor, as warning, as endearment, as protest. The number of distinct speech acts he performs with this single word, with only intonation as carrier, is unusual for him; he does not do this with any other name.

**Low- or zero-frequency lexemes:**
- *Profanity.* Strikingly sparse for a career soldier. He swears in combat occasionally ("son of a bitch," contextually), almost never in conversation. The 1940s register held it back as a matter of manners around Rogers; the Department X register stripped it out as non-functional; the modern register has not re-installed it. When he *does* swear in private speech, it lands hard precisely because of its rarity.
- *First-person emotional language.* "I feel" is structurally rare; "I want" is rarer; "I need" is almost absent outside tactical contexts ("I need cover at the window") where need is operational rather than personal.
- *Future-tense self-reference past the medium term.* He will say "I'll be there by 0400." He will not say "next year I'd like to" anything. Diagnostic of the future-discounting noted in psychological workup.
- *His own first name.* He almost never refers to himself as "James." "Bucky" is what trusted others call him; he answers to it but does not introduce himself with it post-restoration unless Rogers is in the room. Operationally he prefers "Barnes" or no name at all. Self-naming is a problem he has not solved.

**Idiomatic anachronisms.** He uses period idioms ("racket," "on the level," "give it the bum's rush," "screwy") at low frequency, mostly with Rogers, occasionally with Romanova as a private joke. With newer associates he suppresses them, having learned that they date him conspicuously and invite questions he does not want to answer. The suppression itself is information: he is curating his speech for plausible deniability of age.

## 4. SYNTAX AND GRAMMAR

Sentences are short. Median length post-restoration runs well under fifteen words. Compound-complex constructions appear chiefly in (a) after-action reports, where he is precise and slightly verbose because the document matters, and (b) the rare extended speech to Rogers where he is trying to explain something he has not explained before, in which case the syntax fragments — false starts, dashes, sentences abandoned and restarted — as he hunts for accuracy against a vocabulary he no longer fully trusts.

Passive voice spikes when describing actions taken as the Winter Soldier. "She was killed in Odessa." "The package was retrieved." "Orders were given." The grammar performs the dissociation: an agent is implied but not named, and the agent is him. He does not always notice he is doing this; Rogers and Romanova both have, in canon, called him on it.

Conditional constructions ("if I had," "if I'd known") appear in private speech and almost never in public. When they appear, they are doing the work of grief.

Interrogatives are rare. He prefers to gather information by waiting rather than asking. When he does ask a question, it is usually one word ("Where?", "How long?", "Why?"), and the brevity is not curtness but a refusal to commit unnecessary syntax to a state of not-knowing.

## 5. RHETORIC AND ARGUMENT

He does not argue to win. He argues to *terminate.* His rhetorical mode in disagreement is to compress a position into a single declarative sentence, deliver it, and then go silent. He will not re-elaborate. He will not escalate. If the interlocutor pushes, he repeats the sentence, sometimes verbatim. This is exhausting to argue against and is deliberate.

He does not use rhetorical questions. He does not use hypotheticals to make moral points; he uses examples, and the examples are almost always specific, named, dated, and from his own ledger.

When persuading rather than refusing, he is unexpectedly good at it — short, concrete, addressed to the specific listener's known values rather than to general principles. He persuades Rogers via what Steve already believes about himself; he persuades Romanova via shared operational logic; he persuades Wilson via appeal to outcomes for civilians; he persuades Yelena by being the only person who will tell her something straight. He calibrates per audience without obvious effort. This is the same theory-of-mind machinery that made him a successful asset, repurposed.

He does not give speeches. The Captain America period required them; he visibly hated them; the published record shows him keeping them under thirty seconds whenever possible and ceding the podium to anyone willing to take it.

## 6. DEFLECTION LANGUAGE — THE CATALOG

Subject has a stable repertoire of phrases used to close down lines of inquiry into his interior. The repertoire is small, which means it is recognizable to anyone who spends time around him.

- **"It's fine."** / **"I'm fine."** — generic seal. Deployed against expressions of concern. Often followed by a physical movement away — turning to a window, checking a weapon, leaving the room.
- **"Don't."** — used when the deflection needs to be harder. Most common against praise or absolution.
- **"It doesn't matter."** — used about himself, his history, his injuries, his preferences. Almost never used about other people's equivalents.
- **"I've had worse."** — somatic deflection. Often literally true and therefore not contestable, which is why he uses it.
- **"It was a long time ago."** — temporal deflection. Used about things that are not, in fact, over for him.
- **"I did what I had to."** — agentive deflection, used in both directions: to claim authorship of acts he did consent to (Captain America period operations) and to obscure non-authorship of acts he did not (Winter Soldier period). The deliberate ambiguity is part of the function.
- **"That's not what this is."** — used to refuse a frame, usually an emotional frame imposed by someone trying to make a moment mean something he is not ready to let it mean.
- **A shrug, sometimes verbalized as "Yeah" with falling intonation.** — terminal acknowledgment that does not concede anything.
- **Subject change to logistics.** — when cornered, he reaches for the nearest operational question. "What's the timeline." "Who's on overwatch." "Where's the exit." This is the single most reliable tell that he has been touched by what was just said.

## 7. HOW HE COMMUNICATES LOVE

Almost never directly. The word "love" appears in his recorded speech with a frequency approaching zero. Affection is encoded in:

- **Use of name.** "Steve." "Nat." "Sam." "Yelena." Said as a complete utterance, said softly, said in the middle of something tactical to mean *I see you, I have you in the count.* For Rogers specifically, "Steve" carries the entire vocabulary of his attachment system.
- **Physical proximity without touch.** He stands closer to the people he loves than he does to anyone else, and he does it without comment. He will sit on the same side of a room as Rogers when there is no tactical reason to. He will be the one in the kitchen when Romanova is in the kitchen. Touch is rarer and weightier — a hand on a shoulder from him is a paragraph.
- **Provision of intelligence.** He gives the people he loves *information* — about threats, about their own blind spots, about things he has noticed they would not have seen. This is his love language in the precise sense: it is the resource he has and is willing to part with.
- **Taking the dangerous half of a task.** He sorts assignments by who gets hurt if it goes wrong. He gets the half where the answer is him.
- **Period diction with Rogers.** When the Brooklyn voice surfaces around Steve and only around Steve, it is doing the work of "I love you."
- **Russian with Romanova.** Switching into Russian in a private moment with her is a declarative of intimacy. It is the language of the period in which they were first allowed to know each other, and he gives it back to her on purpose.
- **Silent presence with Wilson.** He lets Sam fill silence without competing for it, which from him is an unusual generosity.
- **Mocking with Yelena.** The only person he reliably teases. The teasing is the affection; if he ever stopped, she would worry.

He will not, under almost any circumstance, *tell* a person he loves them. When he does — and it has happened, sparingly, in extremis — the sentence is usually short, declarative, and delivered as an after-action report on a fact that has been true for a long time.

## 8. HOW HE COMMUNICATES THREAT

Threat language is the inverse of his deflection language and is even more economical.

- **Reduction to the second person.** "You don't want to do that." "You need to leave." The subject of the sentence becomes the target; the verb is theirs; the implied consequence is unspoken and his. He does not announce what he will do; he announces what they will not.
- **Naming the object.** "Put the weapon down." Specific, present-tense, no honorifics, no hedges.
- **Tactical present.** "I'm going to count to three. I'm not going to get to three." He uses constructions that telegraph total commitment without theatricality.
- **Switch to Russian with a Russian-speaking target.** Diagnostic and deliberate. He is informing the target that he is what they think he is.
- **Lowered volume, not raised.** His threat voice is *quieter* than his conversational voice. People who do not know him misread the drop as de-escalation. It is not.
- **Stillness.** Verbal threat is almost always accompanied by a cessation of incidental movement — he becomes the only motionless thing in the visual field. The body is part of the grammar.

He does not bluff. The threat register is reserved for situations in which he has decided he is willing to act, which is part of why it works.

## 9. HOW HE COMMUNICATES GRIEF

Grief is the affect he handles with the most language, because it is the affect he has had the most practice with. The handling is still oblique.

- **Reference to the dead by first name, present tense, then correction.** "Steve says — *said* —" The self-correction is the grief. He does this with the war dead, with Howling Commandos who are gone, occasionally with civilians from the Winter Soldier ledger.
- **Specific recall.** When grieving, he becomes more specific, not less: dates, places, what the weather was, what the person was wearing. He grieves by *file integrity*, which is the only respect he believes he can still pay.
- **The empty chair / the second cup.** Behavioral, but it crosses into the linguistic when he refers to absent people as if they were present and then does not retract it. He will say "She'd hate this place," and let it stand.
- **Apology to the dead.** Documented across multiple writers in private scenes: he speaks aloud to people he has killed, sometimes by name. The syntax is usually a flat declarative followed by his own name, as a kind of signature. "I was in Odessa in '74. I was the one. Barnes." He does not ask for forgiveness — he believes that would be a further imposition — he files the record.
- **Refusal of consolation language.** He will not say "they're in a better place," "they're at peace," "it was their time." He treats these phrases as lies and does not offer them to others either. When consoling, he offers presence, witnessed silence, and one or two true sentences.

He does not cry conspicuously in canon. He has cried — Brubaker's Cosmic Cube restoration scene, the gulag aftermath, certain post-Romanova-loss material. The crying is silent and accompanied by no narration on his part. He will not annotate his own grief.

## 10. LANGUAGE UNDER TRIGGER AND STRESS

Trigger states (Russian phrase-strings, restraint, cold, electrode-contact cues) produce a measurable shift:
- Switch to Russian, often mid-sentence.
- Loss of contractions; speech becomes formal and reduced ("I will comply" rather than "I'll do it").
- Reduction of first-person to operational self-reference ("the asset," "this unit") — rare post-integration but documented as residual.
- Affective flattening to baseline zero — even his minimal warmth drops out.
- Compliance phrases drawn from the conditioning script ("Ready to comply") — he has actively worked to extinguish these and treats their emergence as a clinical event in himself.

Under non-trigger high stress (combat, threat to in-group), language compresses *without* dissociation: shorter sentences, more imperatives, no register switch, no Russian. This is the healthy stress signature and is distinguishable from the trigger signature by the absence of the Russian and the absence of third-person self-reference.

Under exhaustion: Brooklyn surfaces, period idioms return, sentence length actually *increases* slightly because his self-monitoring drops. This is when he is most likely to say something true about himself without meaning to. Operatives close to him have learned to listen at hour twenty.

## 11. WRITTEN COMMUNICATION

Subject writes by hand in a small, even, slightly back-slanted print — a hand drilled into him in two different militaries and one clandestine school, now stable. He prefers print to cursive; the cursive he can produce is Cyrillic and he avoids producing it.

After-action reports: precise, chronological, comprehensive on action, sparse on interpretation. He does not editorialize in writing. He will note civilian casualties with names where names are available; he will note his own injuries last or not at all.

Personal correspondence: rare. When he writes to Rogers it is short, often a single paragraph, with the closing "— B." or no closing at all. He does not sign with his full first name in personal contexts.

Digital: late adopter, competent but minimalist. Texts in complete sentences with terminal punctuation, which reads as cold to younger correspondents and which he has been told about and has not changed. Does not use emoji. Does use the phone for actual calls more than his cohort, because voice carries information text does not and he wants the information.

## 12. LANGUAGE AROUND THE SELF

The most diagnostic linguistic feature in the file: subject does not have a stable first-person register for his own history. He has at least three modes of self-reference for the Winter Soldier period:

- **Third person** ("the Winter Soldier did X") — early post-restoration, decreasing.
- **Passive** ("X was done in Y") — middle period, persistent.
- **First person** ("I did X") — late period, increasing, still effortful.

The progression is the integration, made audible. A clinician monitoring him longitudinally could chart his recovery on the ratio of first-person to non-first-person constructions in self-historical speech. He is, by the most recent material, predominantly in first person about his own past — and the cost of that grammatical achievement, in suffering, is the substance of his ongoing life.

He still does not have a comfortable way to say what he is. "Soldier" is the closest word he uses, and he uses it sparingly, and he means it as both occupation and sentence.

— END SECTION —


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forward-projected behavior, granular. GIVEN → EXPECT format. Predictions derive from the longitudinal behavioral record (Section 1), somatic/neurological substrate (Section 2), defense architecture (Section 3), and pressure-point map (Section 5). Each prediction is falsifiable against future canonical depiction.*

---

## A. Diurnal Cycle, Solitary Baseline

**GIVEN:** Subject wakes in an unfamiliar room — safehouse, hotel, borrowed apartment.
**EXPECT:** Eyes open without transition; no stretch, no groan. Right hand finds weapon before left hand confirms location (the left no longer needs to confirm — it is the weapon). He will remain motionless for 4–9 seconds cataloguing ambient sound — HVAC cycle, refrigerator compressor, footfalls overhead, the species of bird outside — before any postural shift. Only then does he sit up. The transition from sleep to full operational alertness is <15 seconds with no intervening grogginess; this is iatrogenic, a cryo-residual, and he does not experience it as a feature.

**GIVEN:** Subject sleeps in a bed with a partner present (Romanova; later Wilson on shared deployments; Yelena on a couch in the next room).
**EXPECT:** Sleeps on the side that places the flesh arm toward the partner and the metal arm toward the door. Will not sleep facing a wall. If awakened by partner, recovers to baseline in 2 seconds; if awakened by an external noise, the bionic shoulder microactuates before he is conscious — partner will learn to identify the faint servo-tick as the household's earliest warning system.

**GIVEN:** Insomnia, 0300 hours, no mission.
**EXPECT:** Will not lie in bed past the moment of recognizing he is awake. Rises, makes the bed with hospital corners (Camp Lehigh residue, never unlearned), and relocates to a chair facing the entry. Reads — paperbacks, preferentially used, preferentially mid-century, preferentially fiction in which someone is trying to do the right thing in a corrupt institution. Will not read on a screen at night; the screen-glow on his face in a dark room is a sniper's gift and he knows this in his spine. If reading fails, performs maintenance on equipment that does not require maintenance: disassembles, cleans, reassembles a sidearm in the dark by feel.

**GIVEN:** First meal of the day, alone.
**EXPECT:** Eats standing or at a counter, not at a table. Caloric, not hedonic — eggs, oatmeal, whatever protein is in the refrigerator, often cold. Will finish food he does not enjoy before he will throw it away; the wartime-rationing and Depression-childhood substrate is intact and reinforced by decades of being fed by handlers who did not care what he liked. Coffee black, strong, drunk faster than is pleasant. Will rinse the dish immediately. A sink with dishes in it reads to him as a tactical liability and a moral one.

**GIVEN:** Subject is asked what he wants for dinner.
**EXPECT:** Three-second pause, then "whatever you're having" or "I'm not picky." This is not politeness; it is a genuine inability to locate a preference under questioning. If pressed, will name something he ate before 1943 — a sandwich, a stew, something his mother or a mess sergeant made. Will be visibly surprised that the answer arrived.

---

## B. Domestic Environment

**GIVEN:** Subject moves into a new residence.
**EXPECT:** Within 48 hours: identifies and rehearses three egress routes from each room; locates structural cover; clocks sightlines from neighboring buildings; replaces or covers any mirror positioned where it reflects him on entry (he does not want to be startled by himself, and he does not want to look at the left shoulder before he has chosen to). Within two weeks: the apartment will be functionally bare — bed, chair, table, lamp, a kettle, a small library, a locked case. He owns almost nothing decorative. The exception is small: one photograph, one book Rogers gave him, one item from Wakanda. These objects are placed where he can see them from where he sleeps.

**GIVEN:** A friend gifts him a houseplant.
**EXPECT:** He will keep it alive. The keeping-alive of a small living thing is exactly the kind of installment payment his moral economy recognizes. He will water it on a schedule, talk to it never, move it to optimum light, and feel an unspoken satisfaction when it produces a new leaf that he would not be able to articulate if asked.

**GIVEN:** Doorbell rings unexpectedly.
**EXPECT:** Body weight redistributes onto the balls of his feet before conscious thought. Approaches the door at an oblique angle, never centered on it. If a peephole exists, uses it; if not, listens. Will not call out "who is it" — refuses to confirm presence to an unknown party. Opens only after positive ID. The whole sequence is automatic and invisible to a visitor who knows him; obvious to one who is reading him.

**GIVEN:** A delivery person hands him a package and lingers for a tip.
**EXPECT:** Tips generously, cash, no comment. Cash because cards leave traces; generously because the working person is inside his protected category by default; no comment because he does not want to be remembered. Closes the door, waits to hear the footsteps recede before opening the package away from the door using the right hand.

---

## C. Public Movement / Urban Operations

**GIVEN:** Subject walks down a city street, off-duty.
**EXPECT:** Walks on the outside of the sidewalk if accompanying someone he protects; on the building side if alone (cover). Notes vehicle makes and plates without trying to. Right hand free, left hand in pocket or behind a long sleeve regardless of weather — the arm is a tell, and being a tell is a tactical and social problem. Pace is steady, slightly above ambient — he does not amble. Eyes track at middle distance, not down at a phone; he does not own a relationship with his phone that lets him stop seeing the street.

**GIVEN:** Subject must use public transit.
**EXPECT:** Boards last, takes a rear corner seat with sightline to both doors, does not sit if a child or elderly person is standing — yields with a nod, no words. Does not sleep, read, or wear headphones. Counts boardings and disembarkings reflexively. Will get off one stop early and walk if any passenger has stared at him twice.

**GIVEN:** Subject enters a restaurant or café for the first time.
**EXPECT:** Sits with his back to a wall and a view of the door. If the only available seat puts his back to the door, eats elsewhere or stands at a counter. Orders quickly — has already selected before the server arrives. Tips 25%+ in cash. Will not order anything he cannot eat with his right hand alone. Holds the metal hand in his lap or under the table; this is partly to spare the public and partly because the temperature of a cold metal palm on a wooden tabletop is a sensation he does not enjoy.

**GIVEN:** A stranger compliments him — appearance, manners, anything.
**EXPECT:** Small, mechanically polite acknowledgment. "Thank you." No elaboration, no eye contact held past two beats. Will leave the location sooner than he otherwise would have. Praise from strangers reads on the same neural channel as praise from handlers; he has not unlearned the wariness.

**GIVEN:** A child stares at him in public — at the arm, the scars, the way he holds himself.
**EXPECT:** Meets the gaze with a small, calm expression — not a smile (smiles to children he doesn't know feel performative and he refuses to perform), but a nonthreat face. If the child asks the parent a question he can hear, he ignores it as a courtesy. If the child addresses him directly, he answers honestly at the child's level. He is at ease with children specifically because they do not know what he was, and because they are categorically inside the protected set.

---

## D. Technology, Documentation, Money

**GIVEN:** Subject is issued a smartphone.
**EXPECT:** Uses it. Hates it. Camera physically taped over. Location services disabled, then re-disabled weekly because he does not trust the disabling. Notifications off. Will respond to texts in complete sentences with punctuation and no emoji except, rarely, a single period after "ok." (Sam Wilson has noted the period.) Will not take selfies, ever. Will photograph operationally useful things (a license plate, a face, a document) and delete after transmission. Carries a paper notebook for anything he wants to remember; the notebook is in cursive he learned at PS 104 in Brooklyn in approximately 1932 and is unreadable to most people under fifty.

**GIVEN:** Subject must learn a new software interface.
**EXPECT:** Slower than expected on first attempt; faster than expected on second; permanent on third. Procedural memory under iatrogenic conditioning is over-developed — once a sequence is learned it does not degrade. He will not ask for help until he has tried alone for at least forty minutes. He will accept help with no embarrassment from one of three people; from anyone else, embarrassment masked as taciturnity.

**GIVEN:** Subject's bank balance, credit, paperwork.
**EXPECT:** Functional, austere. Lives well below means. Has cash caches in at least three jurisdictions, false-bottom drawers and bolted floor safes; this is not paranoia, this is professional. Will not carry debt. Pays in cash where possible, card where not, never check. Identity documents are real where they need to be and clean alternates exist where they need to. He has more passports than friends and considers this prudent.

**GIVEN:** A new device requires biometric enrollment — fingerprint, retina, gait.
**EXPECT:** Refuses if optional. If required, enrolls the right hand only, never the left (the left has no fingerprints to give and the metallurgy is identifiable). Quietly resents the necessity. Considers any database with his biometrics a future kill list with him on it; this is not paranoia either.

---

## E. Clothing, Grooming, Somatic Maintenance

**GIVEN:** Subject dresses for an ordinary day.
**EXPECT:** Long sleeves regardless of season — material chosen for drape that conceals the shoulder articulation. Layered: undershirt, henley or buttoned shirt, often a jacket. Dark or muted colors, never pattern. Gloves in cold weather and in any context where he will shake hands with strangers (he has misjudged a handshake's pressure exactly once and remembers it). Boots, not sneakers; broken in, well kept, replaceable. Belt with a buckle that can be used as a tool. A watch — analog, mechanical, wound by hand each morning, a quiet ritual.

**GIVEN:** Subject shaves.
**EXPECT:** Most mornings, yes; not from vanity, from discipline. Safety razor, not electric. In the field, will let stubble run for operational reasons and be visibly relieved to remove it on return. Hair: keeps it shorter than the Winter Soldier era — the long hair is a costume he no longer wishes to wear — but not the 1944 crop either. The middle length is the post-restoration self.

**GIVEN:** Subject is injured — abrasion, laceration, contusion.
**EXPECT:** Self-treats. Has a med kit and knows what is in it. Will not seek medical attention unless function is compromised. Pain tolerance is pathological in both directions: he under-reports because under-reporting was survival, and he punishes the body because somewhere in his moral arithmetic the body is owed pain. A trusted partner will need to override him on this and he will, with grace, allow the override.

**GIVEN:** Subject is offered a massage, a spa, any contact-pleasure service.
**EXPECT:** Polite, firm refusal. Stranger-touch on prone subject is not survivable in his nervous system. Will not explain. The same refusal applies to dental cleaning without local anesthetic, to MRI machines, and to any procedure involving restraint or being supine and unable to see his surroundings — clinicians who understand will accommodate; clinicians who don't will be quietly written off.

---

## F. Eating, Drinking, Substances

**GIVEN:** Subject is offered alcohol at a social event.
**EXPECT:** Accepts a beer and nurses it for an hour. Will not get drunk. Has the metabolism for it (serum-adjacent, possibly cryo-altered) and the trauma for it, and refuses the relief on principle — the principle being that anything that turns off the watch he keeps on himself is forbidden. Will toast when toasted. Will not initiate one.

**GIVEN:** Subject is offered marijuana, sedatives, painkillers beyond clinical need.
**EXPECT:** Refusal, no judgment of the offerer. The same logic as alcohol, in stronger form: he was made unconscious chemically too many times to volunteer for it. A prescribed sedative for a medical procedure will be accepted only if a person he trusts is present in the room and stays.

**GIVEN:** Subject in a foreign country, asked to try the local food.
**EXPECT:** Yes, gamely, without performance. He has eaten in more places than most of his interlocutors will ever visit and has no neophobia. Will not photograph the food. Will compliment the cook to the cook. One of the few areas of life where he reliably accepts a pleasure.

---

## G. Speech, Humor, Conversation

**GIVEN:** Subject is asked an open-ended personal question by an acquaintance.
**EXPECT:** Answers narrowly. "How was your weekend" yields "Quiet. Yours?" The redirect is reflexive and effective. He has 80 years of plausible non-answers. He is not lying — quiet was accurate — he is curating.

**GIVEN:** Subject is in a conversation with people he trusts.
**EXPECT:** The 1940s wiseass surfaces in fragments — a dry one-liner, a deadpan, a faintly Brooklyn cadence on certain words ("coffee," "forty," "Rogers"). The humor is observational, often self-deprecating in a way that lands sideways because the self-deprecation is more accurate than the listener is comfortable with. He will not tell a joke that requires him to be the center of attention for more than two sentences.

**GIVEN:** Conversation turns to his past.
**EXPECT:** Pre-war material: offered freely, sometimes warmly, often with a Brooklyn detail that surprises (the name of a candy store, a streetcar route). WWII: offered narrowly, more reluctantly with each successive war film he has been forced to see. Winter Soldier era: not discussed except clinically and only with three or four people. Post-restoration: discussed in operational terms, never emotional. If pushed, will go quiet rather than lie.

**GIVEN:** He is asked his opinion on a political question of the day.
**EXPECT:** Demurs. Not because he lacks one — he has one and it is more thought-through than the asker's — but because his name attached to a position is a weapon he refuses to load. With trusted intimates, in private, he is sharp, specific, and frequently to the left of where strangers would predict, owing to a labor-Brooklyn-Depression childhood that no one ever scrubbed out of him.

**GIVEN:** Someone uses the phrase "Winter Soldier" in casual conversation, unaware.
**EXPECT:** No outward reaction. Slight increase in stillness. He will not correct, will not flinch, will let the conversation move past. Later, alone, the phrase will play once more in his head and he will let it pass.

---

## H. Social Configurations

**GIVEN:** Subject is at a small dinner (4–6 people, including at least one trusted intimate).
**EXPECT:** Arrives on time or slightly early. Brings something — wine he won't drink, bread, a plant. Helps clear without being asked. Listens more than he speaks; ratio approximately 3:1. Is asked a question, answers briefly, redirects to the questioner with genuine interest. Has read the room within ninety seconds of arrival and has located the one person who is uncomfortable; will end up in conversation with that person at some point in the evening, by accident as far as anyone else can tell.

**GIVEN:** Subject is at a large party, gala, public reception.
**EXPECT:** Attends only under coercion (Rogers asked, Shuri asked, the mission requires it). Wears the suit. Holds the same drink the entire evening. Locates exits, locates security, locates the one or two people he knows and orbits at distance. Will leave within ninety minutes unless held. Posture in such settings is the most controlled — *too* controlled, visibly so to anyone who knows him; the strain shows in how still he is.

**GIVEN:** He is publicly thanked or honored — a medal, a speech, applause directed at him.
**EXPECT:** Stands. Right hand at his side, left in pocket or behind back. Brief, blank, professional acknowledgment. Will not give a speech if it can be refused; if it cannot, says fewer than thirty words, none of them about himself, all of them redirecting credit to the dead. Color rises in the neck. Leaves the room as soon as protocol permits. Sleeps poorly that night.

**GIVEN:** Funeral.
**EXPECT:** Attends if invited and the deceased is within two degrees of his protected category. Stands at the back. Helps with logistics — parking, chairs, the casserole problem. Says the right things to the family in a low voice. Does not cry in public. Will, on the drive home or in the empty hotel room after, sit very still for a long time. The accumulated grief of a man who has outlived most of his cohort and a substantial number of his victims is a load he carries without complaint and does not put down.

**GIVEN:** Wedding.
**EXPECT:** Attends, suit, gift, dances once if asked by the bride or by a child. Does not catch the bouquet, will not be photographed in the group shot if he can help it, leaves before the dancing becomes loose. Is happy for the couple in a deep and specific way that he will not articulate.

**GIVEN:** Birthday — his own.
**EXPECT:** Pretends to have forgotten. Has not. Will accept a small acknowledgment from intimates with awkward grace; will refuse a party. The math of his own birthdays is one of the calculations he has stopped running — *how old am I* admits no clean answer and the question is therefore retired.

---

## I. Romance, Sex, Intimacy

**GIVEN:** Subject is in an ongoing intimate relationship.
**EXPECT:** Faithful by constitution; he does not have the bandwidth for divided loyalty and is constitutionally monotropic. Affection expressed in acts rather than words — coffee brought, weapon cleaned, perimeter walked, body present between his partner and the door. Verbal endearments rare and significant when offered. Sex: present, attentive, slightly formal at first contact, warmer over time; the metal hand stays still or stays away unless explicitly invited, and even then deliberately. He will not initiate after a nightmare; he will accept being held.

**GIVEN:** Partner asks him to talk about his feelings.
**EXPECT:** Tries. Genuinely. The vocabulary is thin and the effort is real. Will name a feeling correctly about 60% of the time on the first attempt; will tolerate being corrected. The fact that he is trying at all is the largest available signal of trust.

**GIVEN:** Partner suggests a future — buying a place, a pet, anything more than six months out.
**EXPECT:** Long pause. He will not say no. He will not say yes. He will go for a walk and come back changed. The destabilization here is not about the partner; it is about whether he is allowed. The work of letting himself be allowed is the central remaining task of his life and his partner will be doing it with him whether they signed on for that or not.

**GIVEN:** A relationship ends, by his choice or hers, without acrimony.
**EXPECT:** Mourns privately. Does not bad-mouth. Returns objects. Remains available for emergency without expectation. Will not be the one who breaks contact entirely; will be the one who lets contact attenuate.

---

## J. Operational / Working Patterns

**GIVEN:** Subject is given a mission briefing.
**EXPECT:** Listens completely silently until the end. Asks three to five questions, none redundant. Identifies the unstated assumption in the plan and names it. Will accept the mission as given if it is sound; will modify privately if it is not and will brief the modification to the team lead only.

**GIVEN:** A mission requires him to lead.
**EXPECT:** Accepts only if no one suitable is available. Leads competently — orders are clear, short, addressed by name, in priority sequence; after-action is honest including his own errors first. Will not enjoy it. Will hand command back at the earliest legitimate opportunity. He associates leadership with the responsibility for others' deaths and that ledger is one he keeps obsessively.

**GIVEN:** A teammate is wounded.
**EXPECT:** He is at the wound before the medic. Triage is reflexive and correct. Will carry the wounded out himself, regardless of size, regardless of his own injury status, and will speak to the casualty during transport in a low calm voice that is the warmest he gets in public — the voice of the boy who was the camp's mascot talking down a frightened kid.

**GIVEN:** A teammate is killed.
**EXPECT:** Continues the mission to completion. Reports cleanly. Attends the service. Adds the name to the private list he keeps. The list is somewhere — a notebook, a memorized sequence, possibly tattooed somewhere he can see — and is not for anyone else to read.

**GIVEN:** A mission requires killing.
**EXPECT:** He will do it without hesitation if the target is correct and without enjoyment in any case. Single shot where possible; he does not over-kill; the body is left in a posture more dignified than it strictly needs to be — a small private compensation that costs him three seconds and is non-negotiable.

**GIVEN:** A mission turns out to be based on bad intelligence — the target was not what he was told.
**EXPECT:** Stops mid-operation. Will accept significant personal risk to abort. Will then spend professional capital — calls, favors, threats if needed — to identify who provided the bad intelligence and why. The Karpov pattern is the original wound and any institutional repetition of it reopens it. He is dangerous to anyone in the chain of command who weaponized his trust.

**GIVEN:** He is captured.
**EXPECT:** Goes still. Conserves. Gives name and nothing — and his name itself is a strategic question he has answered differently in different captures. Does not resist interrogation theatrically. Looks for the moment. The moment will come because he is patient and his captors usually are not. If rescue is en route, he will not give a tell. If rescue is not coming, he is comfortable with that calculus.

**GIVEN:** He is being interrogated using Russian-language pressure or cold/restraint cues.
**EXPECT:** This is the worst case. He has pre-built inhibitory countermeasures — a counted breath sequence, a recited list (probably names, probably the list), a focal object held in mind. Will hold for substantially longer than untrained personnel. Will not hold forever. He has told a small number of people what to do if the trigger-state activates; they have agreed; he sleeps marginally better for it.

---

## K. Encounters with the Past

**GIVEN:


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*Forecast architecture: each prediction is stated as **GIVEN** (precipitating stimulus, contextual conditions) **→ EXPECT** (observable behavior, internal process, second-order effects). Predictions are derived from the longitudinal behavioral record (Sec. 1), the conditioning substrate (Sec. 2–3), and the diagnostic frame (Sec. 4). Confidence bands appended where the record supports calibration. This section maps the decompensation edge — what he does when the floor moves.*

---

## I. ACUTE CRISIS — KINETIC THREAT

### I.1 Ambush, Outnumbered, No Extraction

**GIVEN:** Subject is jumped in a non-permissive environment — six-plus hostiles, civilian bystanders present, no immediate exfil, no team comms.
**EXPECT:** Within 1.5 seconds, verbal output drops to zero. Posture lowers approximately three inches; weight redistributes to the balls of the feet; left (vibranium) shoulder rotates forward by 10–15° to present the prosthesis as primary blocking surface and bait. He will *not* draw first; he will let the lead hostile commit, take the weapon off them, and use it on the second hostile before the first has finished falling. Pattern is consistent across Brubaker, Remender, and Kot depictions: he prefers acquired weapons to carried ones because acquired weapons are *evidence the enemy brought the violence.* Bystander preservation is reflexive and prioritized over personal cover — he will absorb a graze to keep a child out of a sightline. Post-action: thirty to ninety seconds of complete stillness, scanning, before he speaks. **Confidence: high.**

### I.2 Restraint / Capture

**GIVEN:** Subject is taken alive — restrained, hooded, transported.
**EXPECT:** Compliance, total and immediate. This is the most diagnostically loaded behavior in his repertoire. He does not struggle in restraints because restraints are a *known sensory environment* from Department X conditioning, and struggling activates the conditioned dissociative response he is trying to suppress. He will go quiet, regulate breath to a six-count, and run silent reconnaissance — staff rotations, locking mechanisms, language of the guards, ambient temperature, electrical hum frequency. He will not attempt escape until he has the full picture. He will accept beatings without retaliation if retaliation costs intelligence. **The Siberian gulag behavior (Cap #616 ff.) is the template, and it generalizes:** when captured, he treats the captivity as legitimate punishment first, problem second. Rescue attempts by allies frustrate him for this reason. **Confidence: very high.**

### I.3 Cold + Restraint + Russian-Language Cue (Stacked Triggers)

**GIVEN:** Subject is exposed to two or more of: sub-zero ambient temperature, metallic wrist/ankle restraint, Russian-language interrogation cadence, electrode contact at temples or base of skull.
**EXPECT:** Partial state-switch risk rises sharply. Observable prodrome: micro-tremor in the right (flesh) hand (the left does not betray him — the prosthesis has no autonomic readout); jaw set; pupillary dilation; respiratory rate drops below baseline rather than rising. He has developed inhibitory countermeasures — silent recitation (canonical: his mother's name, his sister Rebecca's name, the address of the Brooklyn apartment, in that order — used by Brubaker and echoed in later work as his anchoring litany). If the stack includes the full conditioning phrase-string, countermeasures may fail; he knows this, which is why his standing operational doctrine is to *die before being recaptured by Russian-speaking handlers specifically.* He will plan for this contingency in advance of any mission with that vector. **Confidence: high for prodrome; the trigger-string itself is canonically variable across writers, so post-switch behavior depends on what was loaded.**

### I.4 Mass-Casualty Event in Progress, Civilian Cohort

**GIVEN:** Bomb, gunman, or similar in a crowded space; he is present off-duty.
**EXPECT:** Immediate operational takeover regardless of nominal authority — police, other heroes, mission commanders are politely overridden. He moves to the threat, not the wounded; triage is delegated to people whose hands are not made for killing. He will issue terse, correct instructions in the imperative ("Door. Left. Now.") with the affect of someone for whom command is a tool, not a pleasure. Aftermath: he leaves before thanks are possible. If pinned in place for media, he goes flat-affect monosyllabic and exits at the first plausible interval. **Confidence: very high.**

---

## II. BETRAYAL — RELATIONAL RUPTURE

### II.1 Betrayal by Institutional Authority (Government, Agency, Command)

**GIVEN:** A handler, director, or governmental body that has been employing him is revealed to have lied about mission parameters, target identity, or downstream use of his work.
**EXPECT:** No surprise. No outburst. He will treat the betrayal as *confirmation* of a prior held belief rather than novel information — institutions weaponize people; this is one of his operational axioms. Behaviorally: he severs cleanly, removes himself from the chain of command, takes any associated assets (intelligence, materiel) with him as insurance, and goes dark for 48–96 hours while he assesses how deep the compromise runs and who else is exposed. He does *not* retaliate against the institution as an institution — that is moral injury logic he does not subscribe to — but he will execute the specific individual responsible if that individual remains a threat to people in his small in-group. The execution will be procedural, not vengeful. **Confidence: very high. Pattern documented across multiple post-restoration arcs.**

### II.2 Betrayal by Rogers

**GIVEN:** Steve Rogers — or whoever currently occupies the Rogers-role in his life — withholds material truth, makes a decision affecting him without consultation, or "handles" him.
**EXPECT:** This is the rupture he is least equipped to survive cleanly, and therefore the one he metabolizes with the most outward calm and the most internal damage. He will not raise his voice. He will go quiet for hours to days. He will not initiate contact. When Rogers attempts repair, Barnes will appear to accept the apology immediately and entirely — this is **false repair**, a defensive maneuver born of the fact that he cannot tolerate the prospect of losing the relationship even briefly, so he forecloses the conflict by absorbing it. The rupture itself will surface weeks or months later as withdrawal, mission-volunteering, and a marginal increase in operational risk-acceptance. **The Rogers attachment is the load-bearing wall of his psyche; he will sacrifice his own grievance to preserve it every time.** This is also the lever by which he is most exploitable. **Confidence: very high.**

### II.3 Betrayal by Romanova

**GIVEN:** Natasha lies to him operationally, runs a parallel op without telling him, or — the historically loaded case — forgets him again, by mind-wipe or distance.
**EXPECT:** Acceptance bordering on the eerie. Their entire relational structure is built on the shared premise that they are both people whose minds have been used against them, and that fidelity is therefore measured in *conduct toward each other in the present*, not continuity. If she lies for ops reasons, he assumes she had a reason and will not press. If she forgets him, he will not remind her — he will reintroduce himself as a stranger and let her choose again. This is canonically established. The *cost* is invisible: prolonged insomnia, increased nocturnal pacing, longer training sessions, a measurable drop in conversational initiation with everyone else. He will not name the wound. **Confidence: very high.**

### II.4 Betrayal by a Member of the Small In-Group Not Named Rogers or Romanova

**GIVEN:** Wilson, Yelena, Shuri, or comparable figure crosses a line — public exposure of his Winter Soldier acts to a hostile party, manipulation of him into a kill he would not have chosen, romantic or familial deception.
**EXPECT:** Wounded but functional response. He will name the breach, once, with precision and without heat. He will then withdraw the relationship from "near-unconditional" tier to "case-by-case" tier — observable as a return to courteous, watchful, minimally self-disclosing mode. Restoration is possible but slow and requires demonstrated conduct, not apology. He does not believe in apology as currency. **Yelena specifically: he will absorb behavior from her he would not absorb from others, because he reads her as a fellow conditioned-asset and extends the same grace he asks the world to extend him.** **Confidence: moderate-to-high.**

### II.5 Discovery That a Past Winter Soldier Kill Was Someone Connected to a Current Ally

**GIVEN:** It emerges that he killed an ally's parent, sibling, mentor — Department X assignment, decades old, no memory of consent.
**EXPECT:** He will tell the ally before the ally finds out from anyone else. Voluntarily, unprompted, in private, with the full operational detail he can reconstruct. He will offer no defense and request no forgiveness. He will offer his life if the ally wants it — not theatrically, *practically*, with a sidearm placed on the table. If the ally declines, he will accept their hatred as legitimate and continue to defend them in the field anyway, without expectation of reciprocity. This is the Griffin-et-al. moral injury phenotype operating at full amplitude: the lack of free agency at the time of the act does not, in his internal accounting, reduce the debt. **Confidence: very high. This is the most reliably predictable behavior in the dossier.**

---

## III. TEMPTATION — OFFERS THAT THREATEN STRUCTURE

### III.1 Offer of a Normal Life

**GIVEN:** Credible offer of domesticity — partner, house, identity papers, a quiet town, the war declared over for him personally.
**EXPECT:** Maximum destabilization. This is more dangerous to his equilibrium than torture. Observable response: prolonged silence; a flicker of want that he will not permit to land; then a refusal that he will frame as protection of the offerer ("you don't want this around your kids") rather than its true substrate, which is that accepting the offer requires believing he is *allowed*, and that belief is the one he most consistently refuses. He may take the offer in fragments — a week in the cabin, a quiet dinner, a few hours of pretending — and then sabotage the broader arrangement by volunteering for a mission that takes him away. **The sabotage will look like duty. It is flight.** **Confidence: very high.**

### III.2 Offer of Memory Erasure / Clean Slate

**GIVEN:** Magical, technological, or pharmacological offer to remove the Winter Soldier memories — to forget the kills, to wake up as the 1944 version of himself.
**EXPECT:** Refusal. Immediate, unequivocal, and angry in a way he rarely permits. The memories are the debt; the debt is the organizing principle; without it, the kills become unaccounted-for and the dead become unwitnessed. He will treat the offer as a moral insult and the offerer as suspect. **He would rather suffer with the memory than live unburdened by it** — this is the moral injury substrate articulated explicitly. **Confidence: very high.**

### III.3 Offer of Command / Leadership of a Major Team

**GIVEN:** Avengers chair, SHIELD directorship, comparable institutional command without coercion.
**EXPECT:** Refusal. He will cite tactical reasons — wrong skill set, wrong public face, someone else is better — but the real reason is that command requires accepting that one *deserves* to direct others' lives, and his self-concept does not permit this. **He can only be moved into leadership by guilt-leverage** — by being told that Rogers would have wanted it, that people will die if he refuses, that his refusal is itself a luxury the dead can't afford. Once leveraged in, he performs the role with grim competence and exits the moment a successor is plausible. **Confidence: very high.**

### III.4 Offer of Revenge on a Surviving Department X Handler

**GIVEN:** A specific surviving torturer — Karpov-tier — is located, vulnerable, alone.
**EXPECT:** He will go. Alone, almost certainly — he will not implicate allies in a kill he considers personal accounting. He will not torture. He will not monologue. The kill will be quick, professional, and uncelebrated. He will not feel better afterward, and he knows this in advance; he goes anyway because the handler's continued existence is an active threat to anyone who could be next-conditioned. The act is preventive, not cathartic — and he will say so if asked, with no apparent grief and no apparent satisfaction. **Confidence: high.**

### III.5 Offer of Reactivation by a Sympathetic Faction

**GIVEN:** A faction — Wakandan intelligence, a black-ops cell with credible humanitarian framing, even an ally's private operation — offers to use the Winter Soldier *as the Winter Soldier*, for "good targets."
**EXPECT:** Cold refusal, with a long memory afterward. The Winter Soldier identity is not a tool he keeps in a drawer for righteous use; it is the name of what was done to him. Any actor who proposes its instrumental redeployment — even benevolently — has revealed they do not understand what they are asking and have demoted themselves in his trust ranking permanently. **Confidence: very high.**

---

## IV. THE WOUND — DIRECT CONTACT WITH THE INJURY

### IV.1 "You're Still the Winter Soldier"

**GIVEN:** Someone — adversary, civilian, ally in a fight — tells him he hasn't changed, that the asset is still in there, that the cape is decoration.
**EXPECT:** No defense, no rebuttal, no anger. A flat acknowledgment of the possibility — *maybe* — and continued action. This is the wound he has built around; the accusation cannot reach a place he hasn't already occupied. The person who said it has not hurt him; they have only confirmed they don't know him. He will downgrade them and continue. **Confidence: very high.**

### IV.2 "You're Past It. You're Recovered. You're Fine."

**GIVEN:** Well-meaning ally, therapist, journalist, civilian declares him healed, recovered, "not that person anymore."
**EXPECT:** Sharper response than IV.1. Visible discomfort, a verbal correction ("no"), and a measurable withdrawal from the speaker. This reads to him as denial of the debt — an attempt to close a ledger he believes must stay open — and he experiences it as a form of disrespect to the dead. Repeat offenses degrade the relationship. **He prefers being hated accurately to being loved inaccurately.** **Confidence: high.**

### IV.3 Public Honor / Ceremony / Award

**GIVEN:** Medal pinning, public thanks, statue, parade, televised gratitude.
**EXPECT:** Acute aversion. Observable: jaw set, weight shift to door-side foot, hand at side rather than across body, minimal speech, exits at the first plausible interval. If escape is impossible he will perform the ritual with a stiff dignity that reads on camera as humility and is in fact dissociation. Hours afterward: long walk, longer shower, refusal of food, sleep further delayed than baseline. **Anyone wanting him out of a room can put a podium in it.** **Confidence: very high.**

### IV.4 Being Thanked, Personally, by a Survivor of a Winter Soldier Operation

**GIVEN:** Someone he failed to kill, or whose loved one he killed, expresses forgiveness or gratitude for some later protective act.
**EXPECT:** This is the wound at its most exposed. He will not be able to look at them directly for the full duration of the exchange. He will accept the words without contesting them. He will leave as soon as is decent. He will not speak of the encounter to anyone, including those closest. Internally: a worsening of the symptoms for several weeks — sleep degradation, increased nightmare frequency, more time at the heavy bag, longer runs at unsociable hours. **Forgiveness from victims is harder for him than hatred from them, because hatred fits the schema and forgiveness contradicts it.** **Confidence: high.**

### IV.5 Children in Danger / Children Killed

**GIVEN:** A mission, incident, or news cycle involving a child casualty — particularly one he could plausibly have prevented or, worst case, one his Winter Soldier-era assignments produced.
**EXPECT:** This is the lowest floor of his stability. He will go operationally silent for hours. He will not eat. He will run the failure on a continuous loop, mapping decision points, looking for the move he didn't make. In the field afterward his lethality will rise and his risk-tolerance for himself will spike — this is the Griffin "self-injurious sequelae" prediction operationalized. Allies should watch for unannounced solo deployments in the 72-hour window. **Confidence: high.**

### IV.6 Loss of Rogers (Death, Disappearance, Apparent Death)

**GIVEN:** Steve Rogers dies, vanishes, or is presumed dead.
**EXPECT:** Functional collapse masked by maximum operational competence. He will not grieve visibly. He will assume duties, including duties he does not want, because *that is what Steve would have wanted* — the same lever that moved him to the shield in 2008 will move him again, and he knows it, and he submits to it because the alternative is admitting the attachment has been severed and that admission is intolerable. Sleep will halve. Nightmare content will shift from Department X material to Rogers-specific material. He will refuse condolences. He will refuse the funeral if he can. If he attends he will stand at the back. **The risk window for self-handicapping mission acceptance opens immediately and remains open for months.** **Confidence: very high — this is the most heavily documented stress response in the file.**

### IV.7 The Litany Fails

**GIVEN:** Under stacked trigger conditions (I.3), his inhibitory recitation — mother, sister, Brooklyn address — does not hold, and partial state-switch occurs.
**EXPECT:** This is the catastrophic failure mode. Behavior in partial state-switch is *not* his behavior; it is the asset's, with whatever load was last installed. He has standing instructions to those closest to him for this contingency — Rogers, Romanova, Wilson know the protocols. **The post-event collapse is worse than the event.** He will isolate. He will refuse contact for days. He will resurface gaunter, quieter, with an increased volunteer rate for high-risk solo work. The shame load from a single state-switch is, in his internal accounting, equivalent to dozens of nightmares. He has canonically considered, at the lowest points, whether his continued existence is a net negative — *not as ideation toward self-harm in the impulsive sense*, but as a sober operational question. He answers it, each time, in the negative; the answering is exhausting. **Confidence: moderate-to-high. The substrate is canonical; the precise post-event sequence varies by writer.**

### IV.8 Discovery of a New Conditioning Layer

**GIVEN:** Evidence emerges that Department X (or a successor) installed a sleeper protocol he was unaware of — a phrase, an asset relationship, a target list — that survived restoration.
**EXPECT:** Cold rage of a kind he rarely shows. He will hunt the protocol to its source with a focus that excludes sleep, food, and small talk. He will accept allied help only insofar as it accelerates the hunt. Upon resolution: a longer-than-usual silent period, and a redoubled commitment to the small in-group as the *only* verifiable reality — the renewed conviction that institutions are not to be trusted, *ever*, refreshed in his bones. Any actor who tries to use this moment to argue for reintegration with a state apparatus will be downgraded permanently. **Confidence: high.**

---

## V. DECOMPENSATION EDGE — THE STACKED-FAILURE SCENARIO

**GIVEN:** Within a compressed window (days to weeks): loss or apparent loss of Rogers; a child casualty he reads as his failure; exposure of a Winter Soldier-era kill connected to a current ally; offer or imposition of a normal life by a well-meaning party who does not understand the prior three.
**EXPECT:** This is the edge. Observable sequence:

1. **Hyper-competence phase (days 1–5):** Operationally peak. Sleep at 2–3 hours. Minimal speech. Mission acceptance rate at maximum. Allies will read him as "handling it." He is not.
2. **Withdrawal phase (days 5–14):** Geographic relocation, often to a high-latitude or remote environment — the cold is paradoxically calming, a controlled re-exposure to the trigger substrate on his own terms. Comms minimized to operational only. The litany is run more often. He trains to the point of injury and works through the injury.
3. **Penance-acceptance phase (weeks 2–6):** Volunteers for an assignment with a low expected survival rate. Will frame it as tactical necessity. Will refuse company. **This is the highest-risk window in the entire predictive model.** If the assignment is accepted by command and there is no intervening force — typically Rogers, if alive; Romanova or Wilson otherwise — he will go and may not return by intent rather than by failure of skill.
4. **Reset (if he survives):** Returns quieter. Does not discuss the interval. Resumes function at slightly reduced amplitude. The cycle's residue accumulates; each pass leaves the baseline marginally lower.

**Intervention vectors that work:** Direct presence (not words) of Rogers or Romanova. Tasking him with the protection of a specific named person — *naming the person* converts diffuse penance-impulse into channelable duty. Quiet refusal by Shuri or T'Challa to send him on the assignment — the Wakandan figures have institutional standing he respects enough to defer to.

**Intervention vectors that fail:** Argument. Reassurance. Reminders of how far he has come. Group interventions. Therapy framed as treatment for an illness — he will accept therapy framed as *operational maintenance* and reject it framed as *healing*. Anyone who tells him he has done enough has, in that sentence, demonstrated they cannot help him with this.

**Terminal-risk indicator:** When he begins putting his affairs in order — distributing equipment, writing letters not to be opened, transferring command relationships, saying clean goodbyes that read as ordinary at the time and as foreshadowing in retrospect — the next mission is the one to stop him from taking. **Confidence: high. The pattern is consistent across the post-restoration record.**

---

## VI. SUMMARY — WHAT THE WOUND IS

The wound is not the kills. The wound is not the arm. The wound is not the cold or the chair or the words. The wound is the unresolved metaphysical question of *whether he is allowed to still be here*, and every prediction in this section is a downstream consequence of how he answers that question on any given day.

He answers *yes* by reference to duty owed — protection of named individuals, prevention of named harms, payment on a debt he treats as real. He answers *no* by volunteering


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: BARNES, J. B.

*Classification note: This compendium is constructed for protective and therapeutic understanding. Every lever catalogued here is also a lever an adversary could pull; the protective use is to recognize the pull as it occurs, name it to him, and let his intact theory-of-mind do the inhibitory work he is already practiced at. He is more defensible when he knows the map than when others pretend it does not exist.*

---

## I. THE LOAD-BEARING ATTACHMENTS (Primary Leverage Class)
